8 min
The Nerve of a Dead Animal: Impurity and the Refutation of the Pain Argument
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the impurity of the nerve with critical refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the nerve, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute, and evaluate the refutation of the pain argument.

Core Idea
The nerve is impure by transmitted ruling, but the pain argument is refuted as inconclusive.

This lesson delves into the contested ruling on the nerve of a dead animal. While the correct Hanafi position holds it impure, a minority argued it is pure. The commentator refutes their reasoning but upholds the ruling based on transmitted authority.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The nerve is impure (najis) according to the correct narration.
2
Identify the opposing view
Some scholars say it is pure because it resembles a solid bone.
3
Follow the opposing proof
The nerve experiences pain when cut, indicating life and hence impurity.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The pain is due to connection to flesh; if pain indicated impurity, bone would also be impure when broken.
The ruling of impurity stands regardless of this refutation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If nerve is impure, wet clothes touching it become impure; if pure, no issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زال عن العظم زال عنه النجس، والعظم في ذاته طاهر لما أخرج الدارقطني إنما حرم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من الميتة لحمها فأما الجلد والشعر والصوف فلا بأس به والعصب نجس في الصحيح من الرواية لأن فيه حياة بدليل التألم بقطعه ، وقيل : طاهر لأنه عظم غير صلب (ونافجة المسك طاهرة) مطلقاً ولو كانت تفسد بإصابة الماء كما تقدم في الدباغة الحكمية (كالمسك) للإتفاق على طهارته (وأكله) أي المسك (حلال) ونص على حل أكله لأنه لا يلزم من طهارة الشيء حل أكله كالتراب طاهر لا يحل أكله (والزباد) معروف (طاهر نصح صلاة متطيب به لإستحالته للطيبية كالمسك فإنه بعض دم الغزال وقد اتفق على طهارته، وليس إلا بالإستحالة للطيبية والإستحالة مطهرة والله تعالى الموفق بمنه وكرمه.
قوله: (بدليل التألم بقطعه) ردّه في مجمع الأنهر بأن التألم الحاصل فيه للمجاورة والإتصال باللحم، ويلزم هذا القائل أن يقول بنجاسة العظم أيضاً لأنه يتألم بكسره ولا قائل به. قوله : (ونافجة المسك) بالجيم والفاء المفتوحة كما في أكثر كتب اللغة الجلدة التي يجتمع فيها المسك. قوله: (ولو كانت تفسد بإصابة الماء) الأولى ولا تفسد بإصابة الماء، وقوله مطلقاً يفسر بأنها سواء كانت من ذكية، أو ميتة، أو انفصلت . من حية .
قوله : (كما تقدم في الدباغة الحكمية) لم يقدمه على أن هذا خلاف المنصوص فإنه تقدم عن السراج أنه يشترط عدم عود الفساد إلى الجلد عند حصول الماء فيه، والذي في الشرح، وقد علمت حكم الدباغة الحكمية وعدم العود إلى النجاسة بإصابة الماء على الصحيح اهـ وهو الأولى وأوقعه في هذا الإيهام الاختصار، وتبعه السيد في الشرح قوله: (وأكله حلال) ولو من حيوان غير مذكي، ولأكله فوائد ذكرها صاحب القاموس فارجع إليها إن رمتها . قوله : (والزياد) كسحاب كما في القاموس قوله : (معروف) هو وسخ يجتمع تحت ذنب السنور على المخرج فتمسك الدابة وتمنع الاضطراب ويسلت الوسخ هنالك بليطة، أو بخرقة قاموس.
When blood is removed from the bone, the impurity is removed, and the bone in itself is pure because al-Daraqutni narrated: The Messenger of Allah (SAW) only forbade the meat of the dead animal, but as for the skin, hair, and wool, there is no problem. The nerve is impure in the correct narration because it has life, evidenced by the pain felt when it is cut, and it is said: it is pure because it is a solid bone. And the musk pouch is absolutely pure, even if it spoils by contact with water, as previously stated in the section on legal tanning. Like musk, there is consensus on its purity. And eating musk is permissible, and it is explicitly stated that its eating is permissible because the purity of a thing does not necessitate that its eating is permissible, just as dust is pure but not permissible to eat. And civet is known and pure, it is permissible to pray perfumed with it because it has transformed into a perfume like musk, for it is part of the blood of the deer, and there is consensus on its purity, and that is only due to transformation into perfume, and transformation is a purifier. May Allah grant success.
His saying: (evidence of pain when cut) is refuted in Majma‘ al-Anhur because the pain that occurs is due to adjacency and connection to the flesh, and this would oblige the one who says this to say that the bone is also impure because it feels pain when broken, but no one says that. His saying: (and the musk pouch) with jim and fa' pronounced with fatha as in most lexicons: the skin in which musk collects. His saying: (even if it spoils by contact with water) the better expression is 'and it does not spoil by contact with water', and his saying 'absolutely' is interpreted as meaning whether it is from a slaughtered animal, a dead animal, or separated from a living one.
His saying: (as previously stated in the section on legal tanning) he did not mention it earlier in a way that this contradicts what is transmitted, for it was mentioned earlier from al-Siraj that it is a condition that the impurity does not return to the skin when water contacts it, and what is in the commentary is: and you have learned the ruling of legal tanning and that it does not revert to impurity by contact with water according to the correct opinion, etc., and it is better, and this misunderstanding is caused by abbreviation, and al-Sayyid followed him in the commentary. His saying: (and its eating is permissible) even if from an animal not slaughtered, and its eating has benefits mentioned by the author of al-Qamus, so refer to them if you desire. His saying: (and civet) like 'sahab' as in al-Qamus. His saying: (known) it is the dirt that collects under the tail of the cat at the excretory opening; the animal stops and prevents disturbance, and the dirt is wiped off there with a piece of leather or a cloth. Qamus.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the base text Maraqi al-Falah. It discusses several rulings related to purity and impurity.

First, it deals with the bone of a dead animal. The correct view is that the bone is pure because the prohibition of consuming a dead animal applies only to its flesh, not to bones, skin, hair, or wool. This is supported by a hadith from al-Daraqutni. When impurity (blood) is removed from the bone, the bone itself becomes pure; it is not inherently impure.

Second, it addresses the nerve. According to the sound transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah), the nerve of a dead animal is impure. The reason given is that it contains life, evidenced by the pain felt when cut. However, the commentator refutes this reasoning by stating that the pain is due to the nerve's connection to the flesh, not life within the nerve itself. If pain indicated impurity, a bone would also be impure because it causes pain when broken—but no scholar holds that view. Despite this refutation, the ruling that the nerve is impure remains the relied-upon position.

Third, musk from a musk deer is pure and its eating is halal. The musk pouch (nafajat al-misk) is pure even if it comes from a dead animal or if water damages it. The permissibility of eating musk is distinct from its purity; purity alone does not imply halal consumption, as exemplified by dust which is pure but not edible. The basis for both purity and edibility is the transformation (istihala) of the blood into a pure substance.

Fourth, civet (zabad) is also pure, and it is permissible to pray while perfumed with it. Like musk, it undergoes transformation into a pure perfume.

Finally, the commentator clarifies terms: nafajat al-misk is the pouch in which musk forms; civet is a secretion under the tail of a cat-like animal. The discussion reinforces that istihala (transformation) is a valid purifier in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
عصب (asab): Nerve of an animal
نجاسة (najasa): Impurity
مجمع الأنهر (Majma' al-Anhur): A Hanafi fiqh reference work by Ibn al-Sa'ati

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator still uphold the nerve's impurity after refuting the pain argument?
A) Because the pain argument is irrelevant
B) Because there is a hadith
C) Because of transmitted ruling (al-sahih)
D) Because of consensus

Key Takeaway
The nerve is impure by transmitted Hanafi ruling, even though the pain argument is logically refuted.

Taharah — Purification

6 min
Musk and Civet: Purity and Permissibility through Istihala
Rulings on musk and civet with explanation of istihala.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on musk and civet and explain the role of istihala in their purification.

Core Idea
Musk and civet are pure and edible because they have transformed into a new pure substance.

This lesson covers the rulings on two perfumed substances: musk (from the musk deer) and civet (from the civet cat). The Hanafi school considers them pure and permits eating musk, based on the principle of istihala (transformation) which turns a potentially impure origin into a pure end product.

Guided Path
1
Identify the substances
Musk pouch (nafajat al-misk) and civet (zabad).
Both are animal secretions initially impure.
2
State the ruling
Both are pure (tahir), and musk is also halal to eat.
3
Understand the basis
Istihala – transformation into a pure perfume.
The original substance (blood) becomes entirely different.
4
Distinguish purity from edibility
Purity alone does not imply edibility (e.g., dust).
But for musk, both are established by consensus.
5
Note the application
Perfuming with these substances for prayer is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زال عن العظم زال عنه النجس، والعظم في ذاته طاهر لما أخرج الدارقطني إنما حرم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من الميتة لحمها فأما الجلد والشعر والصوف فلا بأس به والعصب نجس في الصحيح من الرواية لأن فيه حياة بدليل التألم بقطعه ، وقيل : طاهر لأنه عظم غير صلب (ونافجة المسك طاهرة) مطلقاً ولو كانت تفسد بإصابة الماء كما تقدم في الدباغة الحكمية (كالمسك) للإتفاق على طهارته (وأكله) أي المسك (حلال) ونص على حل أكله لأنه لا يلزم من طهارة الشيء حل أكله كالتراب طاهر لا يحل أكله (والزباد) معروف (طاهر نصح صلاة متطيب به لإستحالته للطيبية كالمسك فإنه بعض دم الغزال وقد اتفق على طهارته، وليس إلا بالإستحالة للطيبية والإستحالة مطهرة والله تعالى الموفق بمنه وكرمه.
قوله: (بدليل التألم بقطعه) ردّه في مجمع الأنهر بأن التألم الحاصل فيه للمجاورة والإتصال باللحم، ويلزم هذا القائل أن يقول بنجاسة العظم أيضاً لأنه يتألم بكسره ولا قائل به. قوله : (ونافجة المسك) بالجيم والفاء المفتوحة كما في أكثر كتب اللغة الجلدة التي يجتمع فيها المسك. قوله: (ولو كانت تفسد بإصابة الماء) الأولى ولا تفسد بإصابة الماء، وقوله مطلقاً يفسر بأنها سواء كانت من ذكية، أو ميتة، أو انفصلت . من حية .

Key Terms
نافجة المسك (nafajat al-misk): The skin or pouch in which musk collects, often from a musk deer.
الزباد (al-zabad): A secretion from the civet cat, used as perfume.
الإستحالة (al-istihala): Transformation of an impure substance into a pure one by change in essence.

Conditions for the Obligation of Prayer
Conditions for prayer obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the three conditions for the obligation of prayer in the Hanafi school and explain the rationale for each condition.

Core Idea
Prayer is only obligatory on a Muslim who has reached puberty and is sane — these are the preconditions for legal address.

Before an act of worship becomes binding on a person, that person must be legally responsible (mukallaf). This lesson examines the three conditions that make the prayer obligatory: Islam, puberty, and sanity. Understanding these conditions helps us know when a person is accountable for their deeds.

Guided Path
1
List the three conditions
From the text: Islam, puberty, and sanity are the preconditions for fardiyyah of prayer.
2
Explain why each condition is necessary
Islam is a condition because the address of Sharia is directed to believers; a non-Muslim is not addressed with the branches of Sharia. Puberty because there is no address upon a minor. Sanity because there is no obligation without it.
The text states: 'Islam because it is a condition for address with the branches of Sharia; puberty for there is no address upon a minor; sanity for there is no obligation without it.'
3
Connect to the concept of taklif
These three conditions together constitute the criteria for being a mukallaf (legally responsible). Without any one of them, the person is not obligated to perform prayer.
This is a foundational concept in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(يشترط لفرضيتها) أي لتكليف الشخص بها ثلاثة أشياء (الإسلام) لأنه شرط للخطاب بفروع الشريعة (والبلوغ) إذ لا خطاب على صغير (والعقل) لإنعدام التكليف دونه (و) لكن تؤمر بها الأولاد) إذا وصلوا في السن السبع سنين وتضرب عليها العشر بيد لا بخشبة أي عصا كجريدة رفقاً به وزجراً بحسب طاقته ولا يزيد على ثلاث ضربات بيده قال : مروا أولادكم بالصلاة لسبع واضربوهم عليها لعشر وفرقوا بينهم في المضاجع. اعترض بأن الدليل أعم من المدعى وأجيب بأنه خص الضرب بغير الخشبة لقرينة، وهو أن الضرب بها إنما ورد في جناية صدرت من مكلف ولا جناية من الصغير، وقد ورد في بعض الآثار ما يدل عليه، وهذا الضرب واجب كما في تنوير الأبصار قوله : وفرقوا بينهم في المضاجع قال : في الحظر والإباحة من الدر ، وإذا بلغ الصبي أو الصبية عشر سنين يجب التفريق بينهما، وبين أخيه، وأخته وأمه وأبيه في المضجع لقوله عليه السلام وفرقوا بينهم في المضاجع وهم أبناء عشر، ولعل المراد التفريق بحيث لا يشملهما سائر واحد مع التجرد أما النوم بالمجاورة مع ستر كل عورته بسائر يخصه ولو كان الغطاء واحداً، فلا مانع ويحرر
It is stipulated for its obligation, meaning for the person to be obligated, three things: Islam, because it is a condition for address with the branches of Sharia; puberty, for there is no address upon a minor; and sanity, for there is no obligation without it. But children are commanded to it when they reach the age of seven, and are beaten for it at ten with the hand, not with a stick, meaning a staff like a palm branch, out of gentleness and deterrence according to his capacity, and he should not exceed three strikes with his hand. He said: Command your children to pray at seven and beat them for it at ten and separate them in beds. It was objected that the proof is more general than the claim, and it was answered that he specified beating with other than a stick due to a clue, which is that beating with it is only reported for a crime committed by a legally responsible person, and there is no crime from a child. This beating is obligatory as in Tanwir al-Absar. His statement: 'and separate them in beds' – he said in al-Hazr wa al-Ibaha from al-Durr: When a boy or girl reaches ten years, separation between them and between their brother, sister, mother, and father in bed becomes obligatory due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Separate them in beds when they are ten years old.' The intended meaning is likely separation such that a single covering does not cover them while naked; as for sleeping adjacent with each covering their own private parts with a covering specific to them, even if the blanket is one, there is no objection. It is recorded.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of Maraqi al-Falah. It opens with the conditions for the obligation of prayer (fardiyya): Islam, puberty, and sanity. These are necessary for a person to be addressed by the divine command. The author then adds an important exception: although children are not obligated, they are to be commanded to pray at age seven and punished (lightly) for neglecting it at age ten. This is based on the hadith: 'Command your children to pray at seven and beat them for it at ten and separate them in beds.' The commentary addresses an objection about the generality of the proof, specifying that beating here is with the hand, not a dangerous implement. The obligation to separate children in beds at ten is explained to prevent inappropriate physical proximity. This ruling is from the Hanafi school, with the beating being wajib (obligatory) upon the guardian.

Key Terms
فرضية (fardiyyah): The quality of being obligatory (fard), meaning the legal obligation to perform an act.
بلوغ (bulugh): Puberty, the age at which a person becomes legally responsible (mukallaf).
عقل (aql): Sanity, the mental capacity to understand and be addressed by legal obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of prayer in the Hanafi school?
A) Islam
B) Puberty
C) Sanity
D) Circumcision

Key Takeaway
The obligation of prayer requires the person to be Muslim, mature, and sane; these are the preconditions for being legally addressed by the Sharia.

Commanding Children to Pray: The Hanafi Ruling
Ruling with proof on training children in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on commanding children to pray, including the ages, the method of discipline, and the obligation of separation in beds.

Core Idea
Children are not obligated to pray, but guardians must command them at seven and lightly beat them at ten — this is wajib training, not punishment for sin.

While children are not mukallaf, the Sharia places a duty on guardians to train them in prayer. This lesson unpacks the hadith and its Hanafi interpretation, addressing the limits of discipline and the separation of sleeping arrangements. Understanding this helps guardians fulfill their educational responsibilities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the age thresholds
Command at age 7, beat at age 10. The beating is conditional on the child neglecting prayer after ten.
2
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith is the primary dalil. The imperative 'muru' indicates obligation (wajib) on guardians per Hanafi usul.
3
Address the objection and answer
The hadith seems general, but the Hanafi school restricts beating to the hand based on a qarina (context): beating with a stick is for crimes of mukallaf, and children are not criminally liable.
4
Apply the ruling on separation
At age ten, children must be separated in beds even from siblings and parents to prevent inappropriate physical contact. The separation means they cannot share a single cover while naked; adjacent sleeping with separate covers is allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(يشترط لفرضيتها) أي لتكليف الشخص بها ثلاثة أشياء (الإسلام) لأنه شرط للخطاب بفروع الشريعة (والبلوغ) إذ لا خطاب على صغير (والعقل) لإنعدام التكليف دونه (و) لكن تؤمر بها الأولاد) إذا وصلوا في السن السبع سنين وتضرب عليها العشر بيد لا بخشبة أي عصا كجريدة رفقاً به وزجراً بحسب طاقته ولا يزيد على ثلاث ضربات بيده قال : مروا أولادكم بالصلاة لسبع واضربوهم عليها لعشر وفرقوا بينهم في المضاجع. اعترض بأن الدليل أعم من المدعى وأجيب بأنه خص الضرب بغير الخشبة لقرينة، وهو أن الضرب بها إنما ورد في جناية صدرت من مكلف ولا جناية من الصغير، وقد ورد في بعض الآثار ما يدل عليه، وهذا الضرب واجب كما في تنوير الأبصار قوله : وفرقوا بينهم في المضاجع قال : في الحظر والإباحة من الدر ، وإذا بلغ الصبي أو الصبية عشر سنين يجب التفريق بينهما، وبين أخيه، وأخته وأمه وأبيه في المضجع لقوله عليه السلام وفرقوا بينهم في المضاجع وهم أبناء عشر، ولعل المراد التفريق بحيث لا يشملهما سائر واحد مع التجرد أما النوم بالمجاورة مع ستر كل عورته بسائر يخصه ولو كان الغطاء واحداً، فلا مانع ويحرر
It is stipulated for its obligation, meaning for the person to be obligated, three things: Islam, because it is a condition for address with the branches of Sharia; puberty, for there is no address upon a minor; and sanity, for there is no obligation without it. But children are commanded to it when they reach the age of seven, and are beaten for it at ten with the hand, not with a stick, meaning a staff like a palm branch, out of gentleness and deterrence according to his capacity, and he should not exceed three strikes with his hand. He said: Command your children to pray at seven and beat them for it at ten and separate them in beds. It was objected that the proof is more general than the claim, and it was answered that he specified beating with other than a stick due to a clue, which is that beating with it is only reported for a crime committed by a legally responsible person, and there is no crime from a child. This beating is obligatory as in Tanwir al-Absar. His statement: 'and separate them in beds' – he said in al-Hazr wa al-Ibaha from al-Durr: When a boy or girl reaches ten years, separation between them and between their brother, sister, mother, and father in bed becomes obligatory due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Separate them in beds when they are ten years old.' The intended meaning is likely separation such that a single covering does not cover them while naked; as for sleeping adjacent with each covering their own private parts with a covering specific to them, even if the blanket is one, there is no objection. It is recorded.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of Maraqi al-Falah. It opens with the conditions for the obligation of prayer (fardiyya): Islam, puberty, and sanity. These are necessary for a person to be addressed by the divine command. The author then adds an important exception: although children are not obligated, they are to be commanded to pray at age seven and punished (lightly) for neglecting it at age ten. This is based on the hadith: 'Command your children to pray at seven and beat them for it at ten and separate them in beds.' The commentary addresses an objection about the generality of the proof, specifying that beating here is with the hand, not a dangerous implement. The obligation to separate children in beds at ten is explained to prevent inappropriate physical proximity. This ruling is from the Hanafi school, with the beating being wajib (obligatory) upon the guardian.

Key Terms
تضرب (tudrabu): She is beaten, referring to light physical punishment for children neglecting prayer after age ten.
بلوغ (bulugh): Puberty, the age at which a person becomes legally responsible (mukallaf).
أمر (amr): Command, in this context referring to the guardian's duty to order children to pray.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, at what age must parents begin to command their children to pray?
A) 7 years
B) 10 years
C) 1 year
D) 15 years

Key Takeaway
Guardians must command their children to pray at seven, lightly beat them at ten if neglecting, and separate them in beds at the same age.

Time of Fajr Prayer: True Dawn and Its Proof
Defines true dawn, states Fajr time, and provides hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the beginning and end of Fajr prayer time according to the Hanafi school and explain the hadith proof distinguishing true dawn from false dawn.

Core Idea
Fajr begins at true dawn (horizontal light) and ends shortly before sunrise.

Knowing the exact timing of Fajr prayer is essential for its validity. This lesson clarifies the two types of dawn—true and false—and provides the prophetic evidence for the Hanafi ruling. You will learn how to identify the correct beginning and end of Fajr time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is determining the time of Fajr prayer. The ruling is that Fajr time begins at true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq) and ends shortly before sunrise (qabl tuloo' al-shams).
The timing is a condition (shart) for the validity of the prayer.
2
Distinguish true dawn from false dawn
True dawn appears as horizontal light spread across the horizon. False dawn appears vertically and then disappears. Only true dawn marks the start of Fajr.
This distinction is agreed upon by all schools.
3
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Jibril (as narrated by Muslim): 'The time of Fajr prayer is as long as the first horn of the sun has not risen.'
The full hadith lists all five prayer times.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'ma lam yatla' qarn al-shams al-awwal' uses a negation of a condition ('as long as not'). This indicates that the time continues until the moment the sun begins to rise, i.e., just before sunrise.
The 'first horn' is the first edge of the sun.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and Hanafi tarjih
A weak opinion holds that Fajr ends when the archer sees his arrow's landing place. The Hanafi school does not rely on this because it lacks strong evidence. The consensus of the ummah supports the hadith-based ruling.
The difference is not considered due to its weakness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقت مقدار من الزمن مفروض لأمر ما (من) ابتداء (طلوع الفجر) لإمامة جبريل حين طلع الفجر (الصادق) وهو الذي يطلع عرضاً منتشراً والكاذب يظهر طولاً ثم يغيب، وقد أجمعت الأمة على أن أوله الصبح الصادق وآخره إلى قبيل طلوع الشمس) لقوله عليه السلام: وقت صلاة الفجر ما لم يطلع قرن الشمس الأول) (و) ثانيها (وقت) صلاة الظهر من زوال خاتمة : ذكر بعضهم بيان ساعات النهار فأولها الشروق، ثم البكور، ثم الغدوة، ثم الضحي ثم الهاجرة، ثم الظهيرة ثم الرواح ثم العصر ثم العصيرة ثم الأصيل ثم العشاء ثم الغروب وساعات الليل أولها الشفق، ثم الغسق ثم الغدرة ثم العتمة ثم السدفة ثم الجنح ثم الروبة ثم الزلفة ثم الهير ثم السحر ثم الفجر ثم الصبح. قوله : (الصادق) صادقاً لأنه صدق عن الصبح وبينه قاله في الشرح قوله : (والكاذب الخ) سمي كاذباً لأنه يضيء، ثم يسود ويذهب النور ويعقبه الظلام فكأنه كاذب قاله في الشرح . قوله : (وقد أجمعت الأمة الخ) نوزع الإجماع بما نقلناه في أوله سابقاً عن مجمع الروايات وبأنه قيل أن آخره إلى أن يرى الرامي موضع نبله فالخلاف ثابت في أوله وآخره، وأجيب بأنه لم يعتبر هذا الخلاف لضعفه. قوله : ما لم يطلع قرن الشمس أي مدة عدم طلوع قرن الشمس وتمام الحديث، ووقت صلاة الظهر إذا زالت الشمس عن بطن السماء ما لم يحضر وقت العصر ووقت صلاة العصر، ما لم تصفر الشمس، ويسقط قرنها الأول، ووقت المغرب إذا غابت الشمس ما لم يسقط الشفق، ووقت العشاء إلى نصف الليل رواه مسلم.
Time is a quantity of duration prescribed for something, beginning from the rising of Fajr, due to Jibril's leadership when Fajr rose – the true dawn, which appears horizontally spread out; the false dawn appears vertically and then disappears. The ummah has consensus that its beginning is true dawn and its end is shortly before sunrise, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'The time of Fajr prayer is as long as the first horn of the sun has not risen.' And second is the time of Zuhr prayer from the Zawal. Conclusion: Some mentioned the explanation of the hours of the day: first is sunrise, then early morning, then forenoon, then Duha, then midday heat, then midday, then past midday, then Asr, then late afternoon, then evening, then nightfall, then sunset. The hours of the night: first is twilight, then darkness, then dusk, then deep night, then dimness, then deep darkness, then the time for sleeping, then the approach of dawn, then the last part, then dawn, then morning. He said: (al-Sadiq) truthful, because it tells the truth about morning and clarifies it, said in the Sharh. He said: (al-Kadhib...) It is called false because it gives light, then becomes dark and the light goes and darkness follows it, so it is as if it is lying, said in the Sharh. He said: (And the ummah has consensus...) This consensus is contested by what we transmitted earlier from Majma' al-Riwayat and by the statement that its end is when the archer sees the place of his arrow, so difference exists in its beginning and end. It was answered that this difference is not considered due to its weakness. He said: 'as long as the first horn of the sun has not risen' i.e., the duration of non-rising of the first horn of the sun. The full hadith: 'The time of Zuhr prayer is when the sun declines from the middle of the sky as long as the time of Asr has not come; the time of Asr prayer is as long as the sun has not become yellow and its first horn has not set; the time of Maghrib is when the sun sets as long as the twilight has not disappeared; the time of Isha is until the middle of the night' – narrated by Muslim.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage defines the time of Fajr prayer and provides proof. It distinguishes between true dawn (fajr sadiq) which appears horizontally, and false dawn (fajr kadhib) which appears vertically and vanishes. The ruling states that Fajr begins at true dawn and ends shortly before sunrise, based on the hadith of Jibril and the general consensus of the ummah. The hadith from Muslim lists all five prayer times. The commentator (al-Tahtawi) notes that some contested the consensus, citing alternative opinions, but these are weak. The passage also includes a list of day and night segments, which is a supplementary clarification.

Key Terms
الفجر الصادق (al-fajr al-sadiq): The true dawn: light that appears horizontally spread across the horizon, marking the start of Fajr prayer.
الفجر الكاذب (al-fajr al-kadhib): The false dawn: light that appears vertically then disappears, not considered the start of Fajr.
قرن الشمس (qarn al-shams): The first horn of the sun: the initial edge of the sun appearing at sunrise, used as a marker for the end of Fajr time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The appearance of false dawn (fajr kadhib)
B) The appearance of true dawn (fajr sadiq)
C) The disappearance of stars
D) The rising of the sun

Key Takeaway
Fajr prayer time begins at true dawn (horizontal light) and ends shortly before sunrise, as proven by the hadith of Jibril.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: End Time of Zuhr Prayer (Misl vs. Mislain)
Dispute over Zuhr's end time: two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding the end of Zuhr time, explain the basis of each, and apply the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position to determine the validity of a Zuhr prayer.

Core Idea
Two narrations from Abu Hanifa on Zuhr's end: one at mislain (mufta bihi), one at misl (Sahibayn).

This passage addresses a classical intra-Hanafi dispute: when exactly does Zuhr prayer time end? Imam Abu Hanifa transmitted two narrations: one that it ends just before the shadow becomes twice the object's height (mislain), and another that it ends when the shadow equals the height (misl). The commentators weigh conflicting hadith reports and conclude that the first narration is the sahih (correct) and mufta bihi (operative) because it provides greater precaution against praying outside the valid time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The core question: At what point does Zuhr time end? The start is agreed (zawal), but the end boundary is contested.
2
State the two positions
First narration (sahih): Zuhr ends just before the shadow of every object becomes twice its height (mislain), excluding the fay' al-zawal. Second narration: Zuhr ends when the shadow equals the object's height (misl).
3
Identify the proponents
First narration: majority of mashayikh and texts, considered the correct view. Second narration: Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and al-Tahawi.
Al-Tahawi is a major Hanafi authority.
4
Analyze the reasoning
The majority chose mislain because of conflicting reports (ta'arud al-athar). Precaution (ihtiyat) requires taking the later end to ensure Zuhr is not prayed after its time. The hadith of Jibra'il showing Asr at the beginning of mislain suggests Zuhr ends before that. The hadith to delay Zuhr in extreme heat seems to support misl, but the majority held that the latter hadith is not strong enough to contradict the precaution.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the first narration (end just before mislain). This is the basis for fatwa because it provides certainty (yaqin) that the obligation is discharged. Any prayer after misl but before mislain is valid according to this view.
The text states: 'الأخذ به أحوط لبراءة الذمة بيقين' (taking it is more precautionary for clearing the obligation with certainty).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشمس) عن بطن السماء بالاتفاق ويمتد إلى وقت العصر وفيه روايتان عن الإمام في رواية (إلى) قبيل أن يصير ظل كل شيء مثليه سوى فيء الزوال لتعارض الآثار وهو الصحيح وعليه جل المشايخ والمتون والرواية الثانية أشار إليها بقوله ( أو مثله) مرة واحدة (سوى ظل الإستواء) فإنه مستثنى على الروايتين والفيء بالهمز بوزن الشيء ما نسخ الشمس بالعشي والظل ما نسخته الشمس بالغداة واختار الثاني الطحاوي وهو قول الصاحبين) أبي يوسف، ومحمد الإمامة جبريل العصر فيه ولكن علمت أن أكثر المشايخ على إشتراط بلوغ الظل مثليه، والأخذ به أحوط لبراءة الذمة بيقين إذ تقديم الصلاة عن وقتها لا يصح وتصح إذا خرج وقتها فكيف والوقت باق إتفاقاً، وفي رواية أسد إذا خرج وقت الظهر بصيرورة الظل مثله لا يدخل وقت العصر حتى يصير ظل كل شيء مثليه فبينهما وقت مهمل فالإحتياط أن يصلي الظهر قبل أن يصير الظل مثله والعصر بعد مثليه ليكون مؤدياً بالإتفاق كذا في المبسوط
The sun (from the middle of the sky) by agreement, and it extends to the time of Asr, and there are two narrations from Imam (Abu Hanifa): in one narration (to) just before the shadow of everything becomes twice its height excluding the fay' al-zawal, due to conflicting reports, and this is the correct view, and upon it are the majority of mashayikh and texts. The second narration he pointed to by his saying (or its like) once (except the shadow of midday) for it is excluded in both narrations. Al-fay' with a hamza weighing shay' is what the sun cancels in the evening, and al-zill is what the sun cancels in the morning. Al-Tahawi chose the second view, and it is the saying of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The imamate of Jibril for Asr was in it, but you know that most of the mashayikh are on the condition of the shadow reaching twice its height, and taking it is more precautionary for the clearing of the obligation with certainty, since offering prayer before its time is not valid, and it is valid if its time exits, so how [is it] while the time remains by agreement? And in the narration of Asad: when the time of Zuhr exits by the shadow becoming its like, the time of Asr does not enter until the shadow of everything becomes twice its like, so between them there is neglected time. So the precaution is to pray Zuhr before the shadow becomes its like, and Asr after its like, to be performing [the prayer] by agreement. Thus in al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the end time of Zuhr prayer. The author states that the start of Zuhr time is agreed upon (when the sun passes the meridian). The dispute is about its end. There are two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa: One (considered sahih) is that Zuhr time ends just before the shadow of every object becomes twice its length (excluding the fay' al-zawal). The second (attributed to Hasan ibn Ziyad) is that it ends when the shadow becomes equal to the object once (misl). The word fay' refers to the afternoon shadow (after zawal), while zill is the morning shadow. Al-Tahawi chose the second view, which is also the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. However, the majority of mashayikh prefer the first view (mislain) for precaution, as it ensures the prayer is offered within its valid time. The text then mentions the narration of Asad (ibn 'Amr) that if Zuhr time exits at misl, Asr does not enter until mislain, creating an interval of neglected time. The precaution is to pray Zuhr before misl and Asr after mislain to be safe by consensus.

Key Terms
الظل (al-zill): The morning shadow cast by an object after sunrise, before zawal.
الفيء (al-fay'): The shadow after zawal (afternoon), that returns from west to east.
المِثْل (al-mithl): The length of an object's shadow equal to its height (excluding the fay' al-zawal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the shadow of everything becomes equal to its height (misl).
B) Just before the shadow becomes twice its height (mislain).
C) At the beginning of Asr time.
D) When the shadow becomes three times its height.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that Zuhr time ends just before the shadow reaches twice its height (mislain), based on precaution and majority support.

Definition of Asr Prayer Time: From Shadow Excess to Sunset
Explains Asr time boundaries with proof and intra-school refinement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the start and end times of Asr prayer according to the Hanafi school and distinguish between the well-known view and the view of Hasan ibn Ziyad.

Core Idea
Asr time ends at sunset, proven by hadith; yellowing marks end of ikhtiyar only.

Prayer times are foundational to valid worship. The Hanafi school defines Asr time with precision, linking it to shadow lengths after Zuhr and the hadith about catching a rak'ah before sunset. A subtle intra-school dispute about earlier exit tests our understanding of 'time of choice' versus 'permissible time.' This lesson unpacks the boundaries and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
Asr is a wajib prayer; its time boundaries determine validity. The passage defines start and end.
Start: when shadow exceeds the misl or mislain (end of Zuhr). End: sunset on the mashhur view.
2
Locate the Dalil
The hadith: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.'
This hadith is ahad, zanni al-thubut, but sufficient for wajib.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The hadith explicitly ties the prayer to sunset; catching a rak'ah before sunset counts, so time extends to sunset.
The operative phrase 'before the sun sets' (qabl an taghrib al-shams) proves continuity until sunset.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that Asr time ends when the sun turns yellow. The mashhur view interprets this as end of ikhtiyar time, not permissible time.
The passage says 'wa humila 'ala waqt al-ikhtiyar' – it is carried upon the time of choice.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
The well-known (mashhur) position is that Asr time ends at sunset. Mufta bihi follows this; Hasan's view is for ikhtiyar.
Tarjih authority: 'ala al-mashhur' and the hadith support sunset.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) أول (وقت العصر من ابتداء الزيادة على المثل أو المثلين) لما قدمناه من الخلاف إلى غروب الشمس على المشهور لقوله ﷺ من أدرك ركعة من العصر قبل أن تغرب الشمس فقد أدرك العصر، وقال الحسن بن زياد إذا اصفرت الشمس خرج وقت العصر، وحمل على وقت الإختيار قوله: (و) أول وقت (المغرب منه أي غروب الشمس (إلى) قبيل غروب الشفق الأحمر على المفتى (به) وهو رواية عن الإمام وعليها الفتوى وبها قالا
And the first time of Asr is from the beginning of the increase over the misl or mislain, due to the difference we have mentioned, until sunset, according to the well-known (view), because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.' And al-Hasan ibn Ziyad said: 'When the sun turns yellow, the time of Asr exits.' And it is interpreted as the time of choice. His saying: 'And the first time of Maghrib is from it, meaning sunset, until just before the disappearance of the red twilight, according to the mufta bihi, and it is a narration from Imam, and upon it is the fatwa, and both of them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said it.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage establishes the time for Asr prayer. Asr begins when the shadow exceeds the length that marks the end of Zuhr—whether that be misl or mislain (depending on the preferred view discussed previously). The standard end of Asr time is sunset, as proven by the hadith that one who catches a rak'ah before sunset has caught Asr. However, Hasan ibn Ziyad reported an opinion that Asr time ends when the sun becomes yellow, but this is interpreted as the time of choice (ikhtiyar), not the permissible time (jawaz). The text then transitions to Maghrib time, stating that Maghrib begins at sunset and lasts until just before the red twilight disappears (shafaq ahmar), which is the mufta bihi view, a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, and also the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Key Terms
وقت الاختيار (waqt al-ikhtiyar): The preferred time for prayer, free from dislikedness; ends at yellowing for Asr.
المثل والمثلين (al-misl wa al-mislain): One or two lengths of an object's shadow; the marker for end of Zuhr and start of Asr.
غروب الشمس (ghurub al-shams): Sunset; the end of Asr permissible time and start of Maghrib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the end of Asr prayer time according to the well-known (mashhur) Hanafi view?
A) When the sun turns yellow
B) At the disappearance of the red twilight (shafaq ahmar)
C) At sunset
D) When the shadow becomes twice the height (mislain)

Key Takeaway
Asr prayer is valid until sunset, but it is best to complete it before the sun turns yellow.

The End of Maghrib Time and the Definition of Shafaq
States Maghrib time from sunset until red twilight disappears, with a dispute on shafaq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling for the end of Maghrib time and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the definition of shafaq.

Core Idea
Maghrib time ends with the disappearance of the red twilight (shafaq ahmar) according to the mufta bihi view of Imam Abu Hanifa.

This passage tackles a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: what exactly is the twilight (shafaq) that marks the end of Maghrib prayer? While the madhhab's official position follows Imam Abu Hanifa's identification of the red twilight, a significant number of early scholars and even the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held that it is the white twilight that appears after. Understanding the evidence and the tarjih (preference) process is essential for correctly applying prayer times.

Guided Path
1
State the mufta bihi Hanafi position
Identify the relied-upon view regarding the definition of shafaq that determines the end of Maghrib time.
The mufta bihi view is that shafaq is the red twilight (al-shafaq al-ahmar).
2
Identify the opposing intra-Hanafi view
Recognize that the Sahibayn and some Companions and early scholars held shafaq to be the white twilight that follows the red.
This view is attributed to Abu Bakr, Aisha, Anas, Mu'adh, Abu Huraira, and others.
3
Analyze the linguistic and practical evidence
Consider the linguistic ambiguity (shafaq can mean both red and white) and the precautionary principle cited by the author.
Al-Kamal argued that uncertainty leads to precaution: delay Isha until certainty.
4
Examine the tarjih mechanism
Note the authority arguments: Abu Hanifa is the founder of the madhhab, and his view is preferred unless there is clear weakness.
Reference to al-Bahr and al-Kamal strengthening Imam's view.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Apply the dispute to a real scenario: when exactly does Isha time begin?
According to the mufta bihi, Isha begins after red twilight disappears; according to the Sahibayn, it begins after white twilight disappears.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : إلى غروب الشفق الأحمر) وقيل هو البياض الذي بعد الحمرة، وهو قول الصديق والصديقة وأنس ومعاذ وأبي هريرة، ورواية عن ابن عباس رضي الله تعالى عنهم أجمعين، وبه قال عمر بن عبد العزيز والأوزاعي وداود الظاهري وغيرهم، واختاره من أهل اللغة المبرد، وثعلب، وصحح كل من القولين وأفتى به ورجح في البحر قول الإمام قال : ولا يعدل عنه إلى قولهما، ولو بموجب من ضعف أو ضرورة تعامل لأنه صاحب المذهب فيجب إتباعه، والعمل بمذهبه حيث كان دليله واضحاً ومذهبه ثابتاً ولا يلتفت إلى جعل بعض. المشايخ الفتوى على قولهما اهـ وقوى الكمال قول الإمام أيضاً بما حاصله أن الشفق يطلق على البياض، والحمرة وأقرب الأمر أنه إذا تردد في أن الحمرة أو البياض، لا ينقضي الوقت بالشك، ولا صحة لصلاة قبل وقتها فالاحتياط في التأخير، وقال العلامة الزيلعي، وما روي عن الخليل أنه قال : راعيت البياض بمكة كرمها الله ليلة فما ذهب إلا بعد نصف الليل محمول على بياض الجوّ، وذلك يغيب آخر الليل وأما بياض الشفق وهو رقيق الحمرة، فلا يتأخر عنها إلا قليلاً قدر ما يتأخر طلوع الحمرة عن البياض في الفجر .
His saying: 'until the disappearance of the red twilight' and it is said it is the whiteness that comes after the redness, and this is the saying of al-Siddiq (Abu Bakr) and al-Siddiqa (Aisha?) and Anas and Mu'adh and Abu Huraira, and a narration from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them all), and it was said by Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz and al-Awza'i and Dawud al-Zahiri and others. Al-Mubarrad and Tha'lab from the linguists chose it. Each of the two sayings was declared sahih and fatwa was given. In al-Bahr, the saying of Imam (Abu Hanifa) was preferred. He said: 'One should not deviate from it to their (the Sahibayn's) saying, even if due to a cause of weakness or necessity in transactions, because he (Abu Hanifa) is the founder of the madhhab, so following him is obligatory. And acting upon his madhhab is necessary wherever his evidence is clear and his madhhab is established, and no attention is paid to some mashayikh giving fatwa on their saying.' Al-Kamal also strengthened the saying of Imam, its sum being that shafaq applies to both whiteness and redness, and the closest matter is that if one is uncertain whether it is redness or whiteness, time does not end with doubt, and no prayer is valid before its time, so precaution is in delay. Al-Zayla'i said: 'What is narrated from al-Khalil that he said: I observed the whiteness in Mecca one night and it did not disappear until after midnight, is interpreted as the whiteness of the atmosphere, which disappears at the end of the night. As for the whiteness of shafaq, which is a light redness, it does not lag behind the redness except a little, like the lag of the red dawn behind the whiteness in the morning.'
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage discusses the end time of Maghrib prayer, which is determined by the disappearance of the twilight (shafaq). The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that Maghrib ends when the red twilight (shafaq ahmar) disappears. However, there is a view that shafaq is the white twilight that appears after the redness. This view is attributed to several Companions and early scholars. Linguists such as al-Mubarrad and Tha'lab also supported it. Despite this, the author of al-Bahr (a Hanafi text) prefers Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion that it is the red twilight. The commentary argues that since Abu Hanifa is the founder of the madhhab, his view must be followed unless there is compelling reason. It further explains that the term shafaq is used for both white and red, but uncertainty about the time leads to precaution: one should delay prayer until certainty. The story of al-Khalil observing whiteness in Mecca is explained away as atmospheric whiteness, not the twilight proper.

Key Terms
الشفق (al-shafaq): The twilight after sunset; disputed whether it is the red glow or the white glow after it.
الشفق الأحمر (al-shafaq al-ahmar): The red twilight that appears immediately after sunset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi view, when does Maghrib time end?
A) At sunset
B) At the disappearance of the red twilight
C) At the disappearance of the white twilight
D) At midnight

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi view is that Maghrib time ends with the disappearance of the red twilight, despite a strong minority view for the white twilight.

Recommended Times for Daily Prayers (Mustahabb Awqat)
Commentary on prayer timing preferences with proofs and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mustahabb timings for Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, and Maghrib prayers and identify the conditions (gender, season, location, weather) that modify these preferences.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice defines prayer timing preferences: isfar for men's Fajr, ibrad for Zuhr in summer, delay Asr until sun yellows, and hasten Maghrib.

The prayer times are fixed by the shari'ah within a range, but within that range some moments are better than others. This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings on recommended (mustahabb) timings for four prayers, drawing on the commentary of al-Tahtawi. Understanding these preferences helps a Muslim optimize the reward of his prayer by following the Prophet's example (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer and its preferred timing
For each prayer (Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib), determine whether the recommended action is to hasten (ta'jil) or delay (ta'khir) the prayer within its time.
Start with Fajr: isfar (delay until clear daylight) for men; taghlis (early darkness) for women.
2
Apply the exceptions
Note the conditions that alter the default preference: e.g., for Fajr, men in Muzdalifah should do taghlis; for Zuhr, delay in summer but hasten in winter; for Asr, delay on clear days but hasten on cloudy days; for Maghrid, always hasten except for valid excuses.
These exceptions are derived from the Prophet's practice and the hadith evidence.
3
Recall the prophetic proof (dalil)
For each ruling, cite the relevant hadith, e.g., 'أبردوا بالظهر' for ibrad, the description of the hypocrite's prayer for delaying Asr beyond the change, and Jibril's demonstration for Maghrib.
The proofs establish these preferences as recommended, not obligatory.
4
Distinguish between mustahabb and makruh
Identify the boundary where recommendation ends and dislike begins. For Asr, delay is mustahabb only as long as the sun remains white; delaying until the sun turns yellow is makruh tahrimi.
This boundary is the critical refinement in al-Tahtawi's commentary.
5
Consider special cases: women, pilgrims, weather
Review the rulings for women (taghlis always recommended), pilgrims in Muzdalifah (taghlis for Fajr to have time for wuquf), and cloudy days (modify default to avoid uncertainty).
These nuances show the depth of Hanafi fiqh in addressing real-life scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة كان كمن أعتق ثمان رقاب من ولد اسمعيل وزاد الثواب الإنتظار فرض وفي الأول لنفل والأسفار بالفجر مستحب سفراً وحضراً (للرجال) إلا في مزدلفة للحاج فإن التغليس لهم أفضل لواجب الوقوف بعده بها كما هو في حق النساء دائماً لأنه أقرب للستر وفي غير الفجر الإنتظار إلى فراغ الرجال عن الجماعة قوله : (لانتظار فرض) علة للزيادة. قوله : (سفراً وحضرا) شتاء وصيفاً منفرداً ومؤتماً وإماماً . قوله : الواجب الوقوف بعده أي للتفرغ لواجب الوقوف قوله : (كما هو في حق النساء دائماً) وقيل الأفضل لهن الانتظار في كل الصلوات مطلقاً كما في النهر عن القنية (و) يستحب الإبراد بالظهر (في الصيف) في كل البلاد لقوله : أبردوا بالظهر فإن شدة الحر من فيح جهنم والجمعة كالظهر (و) يستحب (تعجيله) أي الظهر (في الشتاء) وفي الربيع والخريف لأنه عليه السلام كان يعجل الظهر بالبرد (إلا) في يوم غيم) خشية وقوعه قبل وقته (فيؤخر) استحباباً (فيه) أي يوم الغيم إذ لا كراهة في وقته فلا يضر تأخيره (و) يستحب (تأخير) صلاة (العصر) صيفاً وشتاءً لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يؤخر العصر ما دامت الشمس بيضاء نقية وليتمكن من النفل قبله (ما لم تتغير (الشمس) بذهاب ضوئها فلا يتحير فيه البصر هو الصحيح، والتأخير إلى التغير مكروه تحريماً قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: تلك صلاة المنافقين ثلاثاً يجلس أحدكم حتى لو اصفرت الشمس وكانت بين قرني الشيطان ينقر كنقر الديك لا يذكر الله إلا قليلا، ولا يباح التأخير لمرض وسفر (و) يستحب (تعجيله) أي العصر (في يوم الغيم) مع تيقن دخولها خشية الوقت المكروه (و) يستحب (تعجيل) صلاة (المغرب) صيفاً وشتاءاً، ولا يفصل بين الأذان والإقامة فيه إلا بقدر ثلاث آيات أو جلسة خفيفة لصلاة جبريل عليه السلام بالنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بأول الوقت في اليومين، وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام : «إن أمتي لن يزالوا بخير ما لم يؤخروا المغرب إلى اشتباك النجوم مضاهاة لليهود فكان تأخيرها مكروهاً إلا في يوم غيم) وإلا من عذر سفر أو مرض وحضور مائدة والتأخير قليلاً لا يكره وتقدم المغرب، ثم
Book of Prayer: He was like one who freed eight slaves from the children of Ishmael, and the reward of waiting for the obligatory prayer increases, and for the voluntary [prayer] increases [less]. And making Fajr at daybreak is recommended whether traveling or at home (for men) except in Muzdalifah for the pilgrim, for performing it in deep darkness is better for them to fulfill the obligatory standing after it, as is the case for women always because it is more concealing. And for other than Fajr, waiting until men finish the congregation [is recommended]. (And) it is recommended to delay Zuhr (in summer) in all regions due to his saying: 'Delay Zuhr, for the intensity of heat is from the exhalation of Hell,' and Friday is like Zuhr. (And) it is recommended to hasten it, i.e., Zuhr (in winter) and in spring and autumn because he (peace be upon him) used to hasten Zuhr in cool weather. (Except on a cloudy day) fearing it occurs before its time, so (it is delayed) recommendedly (on that day) for there is no dislike in its time, so delaying it does not harm. (And) it is recommended to delay the Asr prayer summer and winter because he (peace be upon him) used to delay Asr as long as the sun was white and clear, and to enable the voluntary prayer before it (as long as the sun has not changed) by its light fading so that the sight does not become confused—this is the correct view. And delaying until change is prohibitively disliked. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'That is the prayer of the hypocrites, three times: one of you sits until the sun becomes yellow and is between the two horns of Satan, then he pecks like a rooster, not remembering Allah except a little.' And delaying due to illness or travel is not permissible. (And) it is recommended to hasten it, i.e., Asr (on a cloudy day) with certainty of its entry, fearing the disliked time. (And) it is recommended to hasten the Maghrib prayer summer and winter, and no separation should be made between the adhan and iqamah for it except by the measure of three verses or a light sitting, due to the prayer of Jibril (peace be upon him) with the Prophet (peace be upon him) at the beginning of time on the two days. And he (peace be upon him) said: 'My community will continue to be in good as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars are numerous, imitating the Jews.' So delaying it is disliked except on a cloudy day) or due to an excuse of travel, illness, or being at a meal, and slight delay is not disliked.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi covers the recommended (mustahabb) timings for the five daily prayers, focusing on Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, and Maghrib. The commentary is based on the matn of Maraqi al-Falah. For Fajr, the preferred practice for men is isfar (praying at clear daylight) whether traveling or at home, except for pilgrims in Muzdalifah where taghlis (praying in deep darkness) is better. For women, taghlis is always recommended for greater modesty. For Zuhr, ibrad (delaying until the heat subsides) is mustahabb in summer everywhere, based on the hadith 'Delay Zuhr, for the intensity of heat is from the exhalation of Hell.' In winter, spring, and autumn, hastening Zuhr is recommended. On cloudy days, it is recommended to delay Zuhr slightly to ensure the time has entered. For Asr, it is mustahabb to delay it as long as the sun remains white and pure, allowing time for voluntary prayers. Delaying until the sun changes color (yellowing) is makruh tahrimi, and the hadith about the prayer of the hypocrites is cited. On cloudy days, it is recommended to hasten Asr to avoid the disliked time. For Maghrib, hastening is recommended at all times, with no delay between adhan and iqamah except for a brief pause. Delaying is makruh except for valid excuses. The commentary follows the Hanafi school throughout.

Key Terms
تغليس (taghlis): Praying Fajr in deep darkness before dawn.
إبراد (ibrad): Delaying Zuhr prayer until the intensity of heat subsides.
إسفار (isfar): Praying Fajr at clear daylight when the dawn is well-established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) As early as possible after the time enters
B) Delay until the sun becomes yellow
C) Delay as long as the sun remains white and clear
D) Delay until just before sunset

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes specific mustahabb timings for each prayer, with clear boundaries where delay becomes disliked, based on prophetic hadiths.

Definition and Legal Status of the Adhan
Definition, proof, and superiority of adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of adhan, identify its ruling as sunnah muakkadah, and explain why imamah is superior to adhan.

Core Idea
The adhan is a confirmed sunnah, not a duty; leading prayer holds greater merit.

This lesson establishes the foundational understanding of the adhan: its linguistic and legal meaning, its proof from Quran and Sunnah, and its Hanafi ruling. It also clarifies a key debate within the school: whether the adhan or imamah is superior, settling with the Hanafi preference for imamah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Find the phrase that gives the linguistic and legal meaning of adhan. Note that it is a specific announcement.
2
Locate the proof
Identify the statement that says adhan is established by the Book and Sunnah. The Quranic verse (62:9) is cited as a proof.
The verse is zanni al-dalalah – it implies the adhan but does not specify its form.
3
Determine the ruling
From the Hanafi position box, adhan is sunnah muakkadah. This means it is highly emphasized but not obligatory. Determine why it is not fard.
Because the evidence is ahad, not mutawatir.
4
Analyze the superiority dispute
Read the statement about ikhtilaf in superiority. State the Hanafi position that imamah is superior, and identify the evidence (prophetic practice and Umar's statement).
This affects the choice of a muezzin vs imam.

هنيهة، ثم قام فقال مثل مقالته الأولى، وقال في آخره: قد قامت الصلاة مرتين. قال عبدالله بن زيد فمضيت إلى رسول الله فأخبرته بذلك فقال: رؤيا حق ألقها على بلال فإنه أندى منك صوتاً، فألقيتها عليه، فقام على أعلى سطح بالمدينة فجعل يؤذن فسمعه عمر رضي الله عنه، وهو في بيته فأقبل إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في إزار يهرول، فقال : يا رسول الله والذي بعثك بالحق نبياً لقد رأيت مثل ما رأى إلا أنه سبقني، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : ان وروي سبعة من الصحابة رأوا تلك الرؤيا في تلك الليلة واختلف في هذا الملك فقيل جبريل، وقيل غيره وثبت الأذان بأمره وأما الرؤيا فسبب على أنه يحتمل مقارنة الوحي لها ويؤيده المنيفة أول من أحدث أذان إثنين معاً بنو أمية وأول ما زيدت الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعد الأذان على المنارة في زمن حاجي بن الأشرف شعبان بن حسين بن محمد بن قلاوون بأمر المحتسب نجم الدين الطنيدي، وذلك في شعبان سنة إحدى وتسعين، وسبعمائة كذا الأوائل للسيوطي، والصواب من الأقوال أنها بدعة حسنة، وكذا تسبيح المؤذنين في الثلث الأخير من الليل، وحكى بعض المالكية فيه خلافاً وأن بعضهم منع ذلك أفاده في النهر. قوله : وشرع في السنة الأولى على الراجح، وقبل ذلك كانوا يصلون بالمناداة في الطرق الصلاة الصلاة أو الصلاة جامعة فيجتمع الناس فلما صرفت القبلة أمر بالأذان، قوله: (في المدينة المنورة) بيان لمحل مشروعيته قوله : (وسببه) أي البقائي كما سبق. قوله: (ومنه) أي من
Book of Prayer. Regarding the elite and the adhan is an announcement for the common people. Discussion about it from the perspective of its establishment, its nomenclature, its superiority, its linguistic and legal interpretation, the cause of its legislation, its condition, its ruling, its pillar, its description, its manner, the place it was legislated, its time, what is required from its listener, and what reward is prepared for its performer. Its establishment is by the Book and the Sunnah. Its nomenclature is 'adhan' because it is from the pattern of taf'il. There is disagreement about its superiority; according to us, the imamah is superior to it. Its linguistic meaning is announcement, and legally a specific announcement. The cause of its legislation is the consultation of the Companions regarding a sign by which they would know the time of prayer with the Prophet. It was legislated in the first year of the Hijrah, and it is said sealed the adhan, so praise be to Allah, and it is most established [؟] at the time of the Prophet's prayer [؟] so they would not miss the congregation. One said: strike the naqus; he said: that is for the Christians. One said: al-shabur, which is the horn; he said: that is for the Jews. One said: strike the duff; he said: that is for the Romans. One said: kindle a fire; he said: that is for the Magians. One said: raise a banner; when people saw it they would inform one another; that did not please him, so their opinions did not agree on anything. Then the Messenger of Allah stood up concerned. Abdullah ibn Zayd said: I spent the night concerned due to the concern of the Messenger of Allah. While I was between sleep and wakefulness, one came to me wearing two green garments, and he stood on a wall—a piece of wall—and in his hand was a naqus. I said: Will you sell me this? He said: What will you do with it? I said: We will strike it at our prayer. He said: Shall I guide you to something better than that? I said: Yes. So he faced the qiblah standing and said: Allahu Akbar... then he paused, then stood and said the like of his first statement, and at the end said: Qad qamat al-salah twice. Abdullah ibn Zayd said: I went to the Messenger of Allah and informed him of it. He said: A true dream; recite it to Bilal, for he has a stronger voice than you. So I recited it to him, and he stood on the highest roof in Madinah and began to call the adhan. Umar heard him while in his house, so he came to the Messenger of Allah dragging his lower garment, saying: O Messenger of Allah, by Him who sent you with the truth as a Prophet, I saw the same as he saw, except that he preceded me. The Messenger of Allah said: ... And it is narrated that seven Companions saw that dream on that night. There is disagreement about this angel: some said Jibril, others said other. The adhan was established by his command. As for the dream, it is a cause, as it is possible that revelation accompanied it. This is supported by what is narrated that when Umar saw the adhan, he came to inform the Prophet but found revelation had preceded him with it. Some said: it was established only by the teaching of Jibril on the night of Isra when the Prophet led the prophets and angels in prayer, but it was not acted upon until after this dream, because they thought it was specific to that prayer. It is like the iqamah, among the special characteristics of this ummah. What is narrated that when Adam descended to earth and felt lonely, Jibril called the adhan does not negate this specificity, because the intended meaning is the specificity of prayer that is legislated. In al-Durr al-Manifah: The first to introduce two adhans together were Banu Umayyah. The first to add salat upon the Prophet after the adhan on the minaret was in the time of Haji ibn al-Ashraf Sha'ban ibn Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn Qalawun, by order of the muhtasib Najm al-Din al-Tanidi, in Sha'ban 791 AH. This is from al-Awa'il of al-Suyuti. The correct opinion is that it is a good innovation. Similarly, the glorification of the mu'adhdhin in the last third of the night. Some Malikis narrate a difference, and some of them forbade it; reported in al-Nahr. His saying: It was legislated in the first year, according to the most correct view. Before that, they used to pray by calling out in the streets: 'as-salah, as-salah' or 'as-salah jamiah', so people would gather. When the qiblah was changed, the adhan was commanded. His saying: 'in Madinah al-Munawwarah' explains the place of its legislation. His saying: 'and its cause' i.e., the permanent cause as previously. His saying: 'and from it' i.e., from
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah discusses the adhan (call to prayer) in detail. The passage type is a commentary that expands on the matn's headings regarding the adhan's definition, proof, superiority, cause of legislation, and historical account. The author first notes that the adhan is a notification for the common people, while the imamah is for the elite. He explains that the adhan is established by the Quran (e.g., verse 62:9) and Sunnah, and that its name 'adhan' is derived from the pattern taf'il, meaning announcement. According to the Hanafi school, the imamah is superior to the adhan, and the iqamah is also superior, as the Prophet and the rightly-guided caliphs consistently performed imamah. The cause of legislation was the Companions' consultation to find a way to know prayer times; various suggestions (naqus, horn, fire, banner) were rejected, leading to the Prophet's concern. Then Abdullah ibn Zayd's dream about the adhan is narrated, including the angel's instruction and the words of the adhan. The Prophet confirmed it as a true dream and instructed Bilal to give the adhan. Umar also had the same dream. There is disagreement about whether the angel was Jibril or another. The adhan was established by divine command, with the dream serving as a cause. Some say it was taught on the night of Isra. The adhan and iqamah are unique to this ummah. Later historical additions (second adhan, salat upon the Prophet, tahajjud glorification) are discussed as good innovations (bid'ah hasanah). The passage ends with comments on the timing and place of legislation.

Key Terms
أذان (adhan): Linguistically: announcement; legally: a specific announcement indicating the entry of prayer time, with prescribed words.
الإمامة (al-imamah): Leading the congregational prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, the adhan is:
A) Fard kifayah
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Wajib
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The adhan is a sunnah muakkadah, not an obligation, and imamah holds greater legal merit.

The Cause of Adhan Legislation and Historical Innovations
Historical narrative of the adhan's legislation and later innovations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recount the historical cause of the adhan's legislation (the dream of Abdullah ibn Zayd) and distinguish between established practice and later good innovations (bid'ah hasanah).

Core Idea
The adhan was revealed through a true dream; later additions like salat upon the Prophet are good innovations, not corruptions.

This lesson delves into the historical context behind the adhan's legislation. The Companions' consultation, the Prophet's concern, and the dream of Abdullah ibn Zayd illustrate how the adhan was divinely guided. We also examine later additions to the adhan practice and the Hanafi concept of bid'ah hasanah.

Guided Path
1
Follow the cause of legislation
Read the narrative of the Companions' suggestions and the Prophet's concern. Note that none of the proposals (naqus, horn, fire, banner) were accepted.
2
Analyze the dream of Abdullah ibn Zayd
Identify the angel's instruction and the wording of the adhan. Note that the Prophet confirmed it as a true dream.
3
Understand the role of revelation
The passage discusses whether the adhan was taught by Jibril on the night of Isra or through the dream. The dream served as a cause, but the adhan was established by divine command.
4
Identify later innovations
Read about the introduction of two adhans, salat upon the Prophet, and tahajjud glorification. The passage classifies these as bid'ah hasanah.

Disliked and Invalid Adhan from Various Persons
Lists disliked and invalid adhan by various persons, with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which types of persons and practices render the adhan disliked or invalid according to the Hanafi school, and explain the intra-school differences regarding purity and minor's adhan.

Core Idea
Adhan is a sacred announcement; it is disliked or invalid when performed by those lacking purity, credibility, or proper form.

The adhan is a collective obligation and a vital call to prayer. The Hanafi school outlines specific conditions for its validity and desirability. This passage enumerates several categories of persons whose adhan is either disliked (makruh) or invalid, along with the subtle differences within the school regarding some cases, such as the adhan of one without wudu and of a minor who understands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories
Group the disliked/invalid adhan cases by the underlying reason: purity (muhdith, junub), intellect (minor, mad, imbecile), behavior (intoxicated, sinner), gender (woman), and posture (seated).
Some categories overlap (e.g., fasiq may also lack credibility).
2
Determine the ruling for each
For each case, decide whether the adhan is merely disliked (makruh) or invalid (batil). Note that the passage sometimes uses 'makruh' to mean invalid (e.g., woman).
Pay attention to the commentary's clarifications.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi differences
Identify where the school has multiple narrations: the adhan of the muhdith (disliked in one narration, valid in zahir al-riwayah) and the minor who understands (valid in the apparent narration, but some say invalid).
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is given in the commentary.
4
Examine the proofs
Review the hadith cited: 'Only one with wudu should call the adhan' and 'Let the best among you call the adhan.' Understand how these support the rulings.
These are ahad hadith, but they are relied upon due to agreement with other principles.

كتاب الصلاة فيه ۱۹۹ الصلاة يا (مصلين قوموا إلى الصلاة ويكره التلحين وهو التطريب والخطأ في الإعراب وأما تحسين الصوت بدونه فهو مطلوب (و) يكره (إقامة المحدث، وأذانه) لما روينا ولما من الدعاء لما لا يجيب بنفسه واتبعت هذه الرواية لموافقتها نص الحديث وإن صحح عدم كراهة أذان المحدث (و) يكره أذان الجنب رواية واحدة كإقامته (و) يكره، بل لا أذان (صبي لا يعقل) وقيل والذي يعقل أيضاً لما روينا ومجنون) ومعتوه (وسكران) لفسقه وعدم تمييزه بالحقيقة (و) أذان (امرأة) لأنها إن فخضت صوتها أخلت بالإعلام وإن الشرح ببعض تغيير قوله : (والخطأ في الإعراب ويقال له لحن ويطلق اللحن على الفطنة، والفهم لما لا يتفطن له غيره كما في العناية، والسنة وصلها بصلاة من يقيم ويروى أنها لا تكره الأول هو المذهب كما في البحر والنهر. قوله : (وأذانه لما (روينا) من قوله : لا يؤذن إلا متوضى. قوله : (لما لا يجيب أي لعبادة لا يحببها بنفسه فعائد الصلة محذوف. قوله : (واتبعت هذه الرواية) وهي رواية الحسن عن الأمام كما في القهستاني عن التحفة إلا أن النقص بالجنابة أفحش كما في السراج قوله: (وان صحح الخ) وهو ظاهر الرواية والمذهب كما في الدرر . قوله: (كإقامته) لأنها أقوى من الأذان كما في البحر والنهر. قوله : (بل لا يصح أذان صبي لا يعقل) لأنه لا يلتفت إلى أذانه كالمجنون ونحوه، فربما ينتظر الناس الأذان المعتبر، والحال أنه معتبر في نفس الأمر فيخرج الوقت، وهم ينتظرون فيؤدي إلى تفويت الصلاة، وفساد الصوم إذا كان في الفجر، أو الشك في صحة المؤدى، أو إيقاعها في وقت مكروه كما في البحر والنهر. قوله : (وقيل والذي يعقل أيضاً ظاهر الرواية صحته بدون كراهة لأنه من أهل الجماعة كما في السراج والبحر . قوله : (لما روينا من قوله وه : ليؤذن لكم خياركم اهـ من الشرع قوله : (الفسقه) الأولى حذفه ليعم ما لو سكر من مباح ذكره السيد قوله : (بالحقيقة) الباء زائدة أي لعدم تمييزه حقيقة الأذان عن غيرها قوله : (وأذان (امرأة) قال في السراج : إذا لم يعيدوا أذان المرأة فكأنهم صلوا بغير أذان، وجزم به في البحر والنهر ، وهذا يفيد عدم الصحة ويمكن أرادته هنا لأنهم قد يطلقون الكراهة على عدم الصحة كما في أذان المجنون والصبي الغير العاقل. قوله : (لأنه عورة) ضعيف والمعتمد أنه فتنة فلا تفسد برفع صوتها صلاتها ومثل المرأة الخنثى المشكل. قوله: (وأذان فاسق هو الخارج عن أمر الشرع بارتكاب كبيرة كذا في الحموي. قوله : (لأن خبره لا يقبل الخ) فلم يوجد الإعلام المقصود الكامل قوله : (وأذان قاعد) أي إلا لنفسه لعدم الحاجة إلى الإعلام وأما الإقامة فتكره بلا قيام مطلقاً.
The book of prayer. Page 199. The call: 'O prayer! O worshippers! Rise for prayer.' And it is disliked to melodize (al-taghrib) and to make grammatical errors. As for beautifying the voice without that, it is desired. And it is disliked: the iqamah of the one without wudu and his adhan, due to what we have narrated, and because it is a supplication for something he does not answer himself. This narration was followed because it agrees with the text of the hadith, although the correctness of non-dislike of the adhan of the one without wudu is authentic. And it is disliked: the adhan of the junub, unanimously, like his iqamah. And it is disliked, rather no [valid] adhan from a minor who does not understand, and it is said also one who understands, due to what we have narrated. And [the adhan of] a madman, an imbecile, and an intoxicated person for his transgression and lack of real discernment. And [the adhan of] a woman, because if she raises her voice she commits sin since it is 'awrah. And [the adhan of] a sinner, because his report is not accepted in religious matters. And [the adhan of] a seated person, for opposing the description of the descending angel except for himself. The commentary: with some change, his saying: 'And grammatical error' is called 'lahn', and 'lahn' is also applied to acumen and understanding that which others do not perceive, including the hadith: 'Perhaps some of you are more acute in argument than others.' His saying: 'As for beautifying the voice without that' i.e. without what was mentioned of melodization and grammatical error. As for tafkhim of the lam of Allah, it is permissible because it is the language of the people of Hijaz and those near them, while the people of Basra use tarqiq. From Abu Mujahid: he chooses tafkhim after a fatha or damma and tarqiq after a kasra. Its completion is in al-Kafi. His saying: 'It is disliked the iqamah of the one without wudu' due to the necessary separation between the iqamah and the prayer by engaging in wudu, as in al-'Inaya. The sunnah is to connect it with the prayer of the one who establishes it, and it is narrated that it is not disliked; the first is the madhhab as in al-Bahr and al-Nahr. His saying: 'and his adhan' due to what we narrated from his saying: 'Only one with wudu should call the adhan.' His saying: 'because it is a supplication for something he does not answer himself', meaning an act of worship he does not perform himself, so the relative pronoun is omitted. His saying: 'This narration was followed' which is the narration of al-Hasan from the Imam as in al-Qahistani from al-Tuhfa, except that the deficiency with janabah is more severe as in al-Siraj. His saying: 'although the correctness of non-dislike is authenticated' and it is the apparent narration and the madhhab as in al-Durar. His saying: 'like his iqamah' because it is stronger than the adhan as in al-Bahr and al-Nahr. His saying: 'Rather no [valid] adhan from a minor who does not understand' because his adhan is not heeded like a madman and the like; perhaps people wait for the valid adhan, while it is considered valid in itself, so time may exit, and they are waiting, leading to loss of prayer, invalidation of fasting if at Fajr, or doubt in the validity of what was performed, or performing it in a disliked time as in al-Bahr and al-Nahr. His saying: 'And it is said also one who understands' the apparent narration is its validity without dislike because he is from the people of the congregation as in al-Siraj and al-Bahr. His saying: 'due to what we narrated from his saying: 'Let the best among you call the adhan for you' from the Shari'a. His saying: 'his transgression' it is better to delete it to include even if he became intoxicated from a permissible source, mentioned by al-Sayyid. His saying: 'by reality' the ba' is extra, i.e., lacking real discernment of the adhan from other things. His saying: 'and [the adhan of] a woman' said in al-Siraj: If they do not repeat the woman's adhan, it is as if they prayed without an adhan, and it is decided in al-Bahr and al-Nahr, and this indicates non-validity, and it is possible he meant here because they sometimes apply 'dislike' to non-validity, as in the adhan of the madman and the minor who does not understand. His saying: 'because it is 'awrah' is weak, and the relied-upon is that it is fitna, so raising her voice does not invalidate her prayer, and similar is the ambiguous hermaphrodite. His saying: 'and [the adhan of] a sinner' he is one who exits from the command of Shari'a by committing a major sin, as in al-Hamawi. His saying: 'because his report is not accepted' so the intended complete notification is not found. His saying: 'and [the adhan of] a seated person' i.e. except for himself due to no need for notification, and as for the iqamah, it is disliked absolutely without standing.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating several cases where the adhan or iqamah is either invalid or disliked (makruh). The matn lists: melodious singing (taghbir) and grammatical errors in the call are disliked; beautifying the voice without these is encouraged. Then it covers the adhan and iqamah of one without wudu (disliked but valid according to some narrations), the adhan of a junub (unanimously disliked), the adhan of a minor who does not understand (invalid, and also for one who understands according to some), the adhan of a madman, imbecile, and intoxicated person (disliked and invalid), the adhan of a woman (disliked and some say invalid), the adhan of a sinner (disliked because his report is unreliable), and the adhan of a seated person (disliked except for himself). The commentary (hashiya) provides proofs and explanations: for example, the adhan of a woman is disliked because her voice is 'awrah or a fitna; the adhan of a sinner is not accepted because his report is rejected; the adhan of a seated person follows the example of the angel descending. The commentator also notes differences within the school, such as the view that the adhan of a minor of understanding is valid without dislike. The overall ruling is that adhan is a religious announcement requiring credibility and proper form; deviations from these make it deficient.

Key Terms
التلحين (al-taghrib): Singing or melodizing the call to prayer in a way that alters the correct recitation.
المحدث (al-muhdith): A person without wudu (ritual purity for prayer).
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, what is the ruling on the adhan of a woman?
A) Valid and recommended
B) Disliked (makruh) and some say invalid
C) Invalid without exception
D) Valid but with slight dislike

Key Takeaway
The adhan's validity depends on the caller's credibility and purity; many cases are merely disliked, but some (like woman and non-discerning minor) are invalid in the mufta bihi view.
