Taharah — Purification
intermediate
15 min
Conditions of Purity of the Place of Prayer
Commentary on rulings regarding purity of place and barriers during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for purity of the place of prayer for each limb and explain why contact with impurity invalidates prayer even if placing that limb is not obligatory.

Core Idea
Contact with impurity is like carrying it: even non-obligatory limbs invalidate prayer if placed on unchecked impurity.

This lesson refines a key Hanafi ruling: while purity of the place of prayer is required, the obligation depends on actual contact. Tahtawi's commentary on Maraqi al-Falah clarifies how barriers, placement, and duration affect validity, and resolves the seeming contradiction that non-obligatory limbs still require purity when placed. We will walk through the specific conditions for feet, hands, knees, and forehead, and understand the underlying principle that contact with impurity is equivalent to carrying it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the limbs and their conditions
List the limbs discussed: feet, hands, knees, forehead. For each, note that purity is required when the limb is placed on the ground during prayer.
Feet: required under one or both. Hands and knees: required only if placed. Forehead: required on the soundest narration.
2
Understand the proof: contact equals carrying
The commentary establishes that placing a limb on impurity is like carrying impurity, which invalidates prayer. This principle applies even if placing that limb is not obligatory (fardh).
This is the core reasoning (ta'lil) that resolves the apparent contradiction.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference on duration
If a person moves from a pure place to an impure one, the prayer is invalid only if he stays for the duration of a pillar (Abu Yusuf) or actually performs the pillar (Muhammad). The chosen view is Abu Yusuf's.
This shows how the same principle is applied with subtle variation.
4
Apply the rule to barriers and carrying
A barrier (thick cloth, felt, dust) that prevents contact with impurity makes the prayer valid. Carrying impurity indirectly (e.g., holding a rope with an impure end) invalidates if the impure part moves with the worshipper.
These cases illustrate the principle that direct contact or movement transfers the ruling.
5
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf for hands and knees
The opposing view (based on an irregular narration) would permit impurity under palms and knees. The Hanafi position, confirmed by the majority, requires purity when placed. The practical difference: if someone prays with impurity under his hand, his prayer is invalid according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.
This is a clear example of inter-madhhab khilaf with a concrete consequence.

الذي يصلي عليه فلو بسط شيئاً رقيقاً يصلح ساتراً للعورة وهو ما لا يرى منه الجسد جازت صلاته وإن كانت النجاسة رطبة فألقي عليهما لبداً، أو ثنى ما ليس ثخيناً أو كبسها بالتراب فلم يجد ريح النجاسة جازت صلاته وإذا أمسك حبلاً مربوطاً به نجاسة أو بقي من طرف طاهر ولم يتحرك الطرف النجس بحركته صحت وإلا فلا كما لو أصاب رأسه خيمة نجسة وجلوس صغير يستمسك في حجر المصلى، وطير متنجس على رأسه لا يبطل الصلاة إذا لم تنفصل منه نجاسة مانعة لأن الشرط الطهارة (من) نجس غير معفو عنه) وتقدم بيانه (حتى) أنه يشترط طهارة (موضع القدمين فتبطل الصلاة بنجس مانع تحت أحدهما، أو بجمعه فيهما تقديراً في الأصح وقيامه على قدم صحيح مع الكراهة، وانتقاله مكان عن طاهر لنجس ولم يمكث به مقدار ركن لا تبطل به وإن مكث قدره بطلت على المختار (و) منها طهارة موضع اليدين والركبتين على الصحيح لافتراض السجود على سبعة أعظم واختاره الفقيه أبو الليث، وأنكر ما قيل من عدم افتراض طهارة موضعها ولأن رواية جواز مع نجاسة موضع الكفين والركبتين شاذة (و) منها طهارة موضع الجبهة على الأصح من الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة، وهو قولهما رحمهم الله ليتحقق السجود عليها لأن
قوله: (أو بجمعه) معطوف على محذوف معلوم من المقام تقديره بنجس مانع بإنفراده تحت أحدهما. قوله : ( تقديراً) أي بالحرز والظن قوله لا تبطل به الصلاة لأن المكث اليسير على النجس القليل كالمكث الكثير مع النجس القليل معفو عنه، وحكم الانكشاف مع الزمن كحكم المكث مع النجس أفاده الشرح . قوله : (وإن مكث قدره) أي وإن لم يؤده. قوله : (على المختار) هو قول أبي يوسف، وقال محمد : لا تفسد إلا إذا أداه بالفعل. قوله : (على الصحيح) صححه الحلبي، وصاحب العيون. قوله : (الإفتراض السجود على سبعة أعظم) ظاهره أنه إذا لم يضع اليدين أو الركبتين أو إحداهما أن تكون الصلاة فاسدة وليس كذلك، بل العلة في الفساد أن وضع العضو على النجاسة بمنزلة حملها، فيفسد وإن كان الموضع غير فرض قال في الخانية : إذا كانت النجاسة في موضع السجود، أو الركبتين، أو اليدين فإنها تجمع، وتمنع ولا يجعل كأنه لم يضع ذلك العضو بخلاف ما لو صلى رافعاً إحدى قدميه فإنه يجوز، ولو وضع القدم على نجاسة لا يجوز، ولا يجعل كأنه لم يضع اهـ. قال الكمال : وهذا يفيد أنّ عدم إشتراط طهارة مكان اليدين والركبتين محله إذا لم يضعهما أما إذا وضعهما، أو وضع إحداهما اشترطت فليحفظ اهـ . قال الحلبي : فعلم أنه لا فرق بين الركبتين واليدين، وبين موضع السجود، والقدمين في أنّ النجاسة المانعة في مواضعها مفسدة للصلاة، وهو الصحيح لأن إتصال العضو بالنجاسة بمنزلة حملها، وإن كان وضع ذلك العضو ليس بفرض اهـ، هذه النقول تدل على أن وضعها ليس فرضاً، ولكنها إذا وضعت إشترطت طهارة مواضعها، فليتأمل. بقي الكلام فيما إذا وضع ما يكره وضعه كالذراعين هل يفترض طهارة موضعهما الظاهر نعم لأنه بوضعهما على النجاسة يعد حاملاً لها قوله: (واختاره الفقيه أبو الليث) الذي ذكره بعد في هذا الباب أنّ الذي إختاره الفقيه وضع إحدى اليدين وإحدى الركبتين وشيء من أطراف القدمين فليتأمل قوله : (وأنكر ما قيل) لا يلزم من إنكاره ذلك قوله بإفتراض وضعها. قوله (شاذة) ذكر ذلك صاحب العيون، وهذا لا ينافي إن وضعهما غير واجب أي غير فرض في ظاهر الرواية كما ذكره صاحب البحر .
He who prays upon [a place], if he spreads a thin cloth that suffices as a cover for the private parts, meaning from which the body is not seen, his prayer is valid. And if the impurity is wet, and he throws a felt cloth onto it, or doubles something not thick, or covers it with dust, and does not perceive the smell of impurity, his prayer is valid. And if he holds a rope tied to an impurity, or remains on a pure side, and the impure side does not move with his movement, it is valid; otherwise not. Likewise if a dirty tent touches his head, or a small child who holds himself sits in the lap of the one praying, or a bird with impurity sits on his head, it does not invalidate the prayer if no impurity that prevents (i.e., beyond the pardonable amount) separates from it, because the condition is purity from unpardonable impurity. And its explanation preceded. (Thus) that purity of the place of the feet is required, so the prayer is invalidated by a preventing impurity under one of them, or by combining them (the two feet) in it (a single impure spot) by estimation according to the most correct view. And his standing on a single foot is valid with dislike. And his moving from a pure place to an impure one: if he does not stay for the duration of a pillar, it does not invalidate; if he stays that long, it invalidates according to the chosen view. And (another condition) is purity of the place of the hands and knees according to the sound view, because prostration is prescribed on seven limbs. The faqih Abu al-Layth chose this, and he rejected what was said about the lack of obligation of purity of their place, and because the narration permitting impurity under the palms and knees is irregular. And (another condition) is purity of the place of the forehead according to the sounder of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa, and it is the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) so that prostration is realized upon it because... His statement: 'or by combining them' is coordinated with an omitted element understood from the context, i.e., by a preventing impurity alone under one of them. His statement: 'by estimation' means by estimation and supposition. It does not invalidate prayer because brief staying on little impurity is like long staying with little impurity which is pardoned. His statement: 'if he stays that long' means even if he does not perform (the pillar deliberately). His statement: 'according to the chosen view' is the view of Abu Yusuf, while Muhammad said it does not become invalid unless he performs it (the pillar) actually. His statement: 'according to the sound view' was deemed sound by al-Halabi and the author of al-Uyun. His statement: 'the prescription of prostration on seven limbs' outwardly indicates that if he does not place his hands or knees or one of them, the prayer is invalid, but this is not the case. Rather, the cause of invalidity is that placing the limb on impurity is like carrying it, so it invalidates even if the place is not obligatory (to place). Al-Khaniyah states: If impurity is under the place of prostration, or the knees, or the hands, it gathers and prevents (prayer), and it is not as if he did not place that limb. Al-Kamal said: This indicates that the non-requirement of purity for the place of hands and knees applies when he does not place them; but if he places them, or one of them, purity is required. Al-Halabi said: So it is known that there is no difference between the knees and hands, and the place of prostration and the feet, in that preventing impurity in their places invalidates prayer, and this is the sound view because contact of the limb with impurity is like carrying it, even if placing that limb is not obligatory. The rest of the discussion about placing disliked limbs like the forearms, the apparent ruling is that purity of their place is required because by placing them on impurity he becomes a carrier of impurity. His statement: 'and the faqih Abu al-Layth chose'... the one he chose, as mentioned later in this chapter, is placing one hand and one knee and some of the tips of the feet. His statement: 'and he rejected what was said' does not imply that he holds that placing them is obligatory. His statement: 'irregular' was mentioned by the author of al-Uyun, and this does not contradict that placing them is not obligatory, i.e., not fardh in the apparent narration as mentioned by the author of al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah clarifies the conditions of purity of the place where the worshipper's body parts come into contact during prayer. It begins by discussing cases where an intervening barrier exists between the impurity and the worshipper: if the worshipper spreads a thin cloth that conceals the private parts but does not transmit impurity, the prayer is valid. If the impurity is wet and a thick barrier (like felt) is placed over it, or if the impurity is covered with dust so that no smell is perceived, the prayer is also valid. However, if the barrier is thin and the impurity's smell can be detected, prayer is not allowed. Similarly, holding a rope with an impure end is permissible only if the impure end does not move with the worshipper's motion; otherwise, it is considered carrying impurity. Touching an impure tent or having an impure child or bird on one's person does not invalidate prayer if no actual impurity separating from them touches the worshipper. The commentary then delves into the requirement of purity for specific body parts: the feet, hands, knees, and forehead. For the feet, prayer is invalid if there is a preventing impurity under one foot, or under both by estimation (if the impurity covers the area of both feet). Standing on one foot is permissible but disliked. If the worshipper moves from a pure place to an impure one, brief standing (less than a pillar) is excused, but staying for the duration of a pillar invalidates prayer according to Abu Yusuf's view (the chosen one). For the hands and knees, the sound view requires purity because prostration is prescribed on seven limbs. However, this requirement applies only if the worshipper actually places them on the ground; if he does not place them, purity is not required. The same applies to the forehead: purity is required on the sounder narration from Abu Hanifa and is the view of the two companions. The commentary resolves an apparent contradiction: even though placing the hands and knees is not obligatory (fardh) in the prayer, if one does place them on impurity, it is considered carrying impurity and invalidates the prayer. This is based on the principle that contact with impurity is akin to carrying it. The passage also discusses the view of Abu al-Layth and the irregularity of a narration that would permit impurity under the palms and knees. Overall, this commentary refines the understanding of the ruling: the key is not whether the limb is an obligatory position but whether it contacts impurity, thereby making the worshipper a carrier of impurity.

Key Terms
نجاسة مانعة (najasah mani'ah): Impurity that exceeds the amount forgiven (less than quarter of a limb for light impurity, dirham for heavy impurity).
حمل النجاسة (haml al-najasah): Carrying impurity on one's body or clothing during prayer, which invalidates prayer if the impurity is preventing.
موضع السجود (mawdi' al-sujud): The place where the forehead is placed during prostration; its purity is required according to the soundest narration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what invalidates prayer when a person moves from a pure place to an impure one?
A) Moving to an impure place automatically invalidates prayer.
B) Staying on the impure place for the duration of a pillar (Abu Yusuf's view).
C) The impurity must be heavy and exceed a dirham.
D) The impurity must be under the forehead only.

Key Takeaway
Purity of place is required for any limb that contacts the ground during prayer, even if placing that limb is not obligatory, because contact with impurity is equivalent to carrying it.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Purity of the Place of Prostration
Explaining the requirement of purity for the prostration place and the intra-Hanafi dispute on the nose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preponderant Hanafi view on the obligation of placing the nose in prostration and explain the ruling when impurity is present on the nose.

Core Idea
Placing both forehead and nose in prostration is wajib; impurity less than a dirham on the nose does not invalidate prayer.

In this lesson, we examine a critical refinement from Hashiya al-Tahtawi regarding the condition of purity of the prostration place. The focus is on the nose placement dispute: is it obligatory to place the nose on a pure surface? We'll see the preponderant view and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Prostration is a pillar of prayer, and the place of prostration must be pure. The dispute centers on whether placing the nose on the ground is obligatory or merely recommended.
The preponderant view (rajih) makes it wajib; the weaker view (marjuh) considers it sunnah.
2
State the preponderant Hanafi view
The mufta bihi position is that combining both forehead and nose in prostration is wajib. Placing only the nose is insufficient and results in karaha tahrimiyya.
This view is supported by the hadith of prostrating on seven limbs, with the nose included in the forehead.
3
Understand the weaker view
Some early Hanafi authorities considered only the forehead as fard, making the nose optional. According to this view, placing the nose is not required, but combining both is still recommended.
Al-Tahtawi follows the preponderant view.
4
Apply the ruling to impurity
If the nose touches impurity less than a dirham (approx. palm-sized), the prayer is valid by consensus. If the impurity is greater, the prayer must be repeated on a clean place.
The text mentions a riwaya from Abu Yusuf allowing a repeat on a clean place.
5
Note the evidence
The ruling is derived from Quran 74:4 ('And your garments purify') extended by qiyas to the place of prostration, since prayer has no existence without a place. The hadith of seven limbs also supports the inclusion of the nose.
The dalala of the verse is zanni, but the extension is based on the illa of necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
للصلاة
الفرض، وإن كان يتأدى بمقدار الأرنبة على القول المرجوح يصير الوضع معدوماً حكماً بوجوده على النجس ولو أعاده على طاهر في ظاهر الرواية ولا يمنع نجاسة في محل أنفه مع طهارة باقي المحال بالاتفاق لأن الأنف أقل من الدرهم ويصير كأنه اقتصر على الجبهة مع الكراهة، وطهارة المكان ألزم من الثوب المشروط نصاً بالدلالة إذ لا وجود بدون مكان، وقد توجد بدون ثوب، ولا يضر وقوع ثوبه على نجاسة لا تعلق به حال سجوده
قوله: (ليتحقق السجود عليها علة لإشتراط طهارة موضعها. قوله: (لأن الفرض الخ) علة لمحذوف ينبغي التصريح به تقديره وهذا على كلا القولين أي إشتراط طهارة موضعها لازم على القول الراجح بإفتراض وضعها، وعلى القول المرجوح بعدم إفتراضه لأنه الخ. قوله : (على القول المرجوح وهو أن الجمع بين الجبهة والأنف واجب وإنه يكره الإقتصار على أحدهما. قوله : (يصير الوضع معدوماً) حذف جملة هنا لا بد من ذكرها وقد ذكرها في الشرح فقل : ولكن إذا وضع الجبهة. مع الأرنبة يقع الكل فرضاً كما إذا طول القراءة على القدر المفروض فيصير الخ .اهـ. والمعنى أن إشتراط طهارة موضع الجبهة فرض على القول المرجوح لكن إذا وضعت بالفعل لأن وضعها بوصف بعد تحققه بأنه فرض كالقراءة فإنها توصف بالوجوب، أو السنية فيما زاد على قدر الفرض، ولكن إذا وقعت في الصلاة وصفت بالإفتراض قوله : ( في ظاهر الرواية وروي عن أبي يوسف جوازها إن أعاده على طاهر. قوله : (مع الكراهة) أي التحريمية لأن وضع الأنف واجب وإذا وضعه على نجاسة كأنه لم يضعه. قوله : ( وطهارة المكان أي والجسد وهذا منه بيان للدليل على إشتراط طهارة هذه الأشياء. قوله: (المشروط نصاً في قوله تعالى : وثيابك فطهر ) [المدثر / ٧٤]. قوله: (بالدلالة) متعلق بألزم يعني أنه ثبت كون طهارته ألزم بدلالة النص ودلالة النص كل معنى يفهمه العالم بالوضع من النص المذكور لإشتراكه معه في العلة، ولكونه أولى بالحكم منه قوله : (إذ لا وجود الخ) علة لكونه ألزم بالدلالة قوله : (حال سجوده) متعلق بوقوع ثوبه . تنبيه : إنما اشترطت الطهارة في الصلاة لأنها مناجاة مع الرب عز وجل فيجب أن يكون المصلي على أحسن الأحوال وذا في طهارته، وطهارة ما يتصل به من الثوب والمكان أفاده الشرح. قوله : (ومنها سترة العورة ولو بماء كدر ، أو ورق شجر، أو طين وليس لستر الظلمة إعتبار كما في القهستاني كالستر بالزجاج كما في القنية، ولا يضر تشكل العورة بالتصاق الساتر الضيق بها كما في الحلبي والعورة في اللغة كل ما يستقبح ظهوره مأخوذة من العور، وهو النقص، والعيب، والقبح ومنه عور العين وكلمة عوراء أي قبيحة، وسيمت السوأة عورة لقبح ظهورها، وغض الأبصار عنها، وكل شيء يستره الإنسان أنفة أو حياء فهو عورة والنساء عورة كما في كتب
اللغة. قوله: (للإجماع على إفتراضه) أي في الصلاة أما الستر في الخلوة فصحح الحلبي وجوب الستر فيها، وصحح الشارح عدمه فقد اختلف التصحح قوله: (ولا يضر نظرها من جيبه لأنه يحل له مسها والنظر إليها ولكنه خلاف الأدب كما في النهر، واختار البرهان الحلبي أن تلك الصلاة مكروهة وإن لم تفد، ومقابل الصحيح ما عن بعض المشايخ من اشتراط ستر عورته عن نفسه وفرع عليه أنها لو كانت لحيته كثيفة وستر بها زيقه صحت وإلا فلا. قوله : (لأن التكلف لمنعه أي لمنع نظر الناظر . قال في الشرح : لأن ستر العورة على وجه لا يمكن الغير النظر إليها إذا تكلف مما يؤدّي إلى الحرج .اهـ. قوله: (والثوب الحرير الخ) جعل الكلام فيما إذا صلى فيه وأما إذا صلى عليه، فقال القهستاني من كتاب الحظر معزياً بالصلاة الجواهر ما نصه وتجوز الصلاة على السجادة من الأبريسم لأن الحرام هو اللبس أما الإنتفاع بسائر الوجوه، فليس بحرام .اهـ. قوله وللمغصوب) نقل في الفتاوي الهندية عن مختارات النوازل الصلاة في أرض مغصوبة جائزة ولكن يعاقب بظلمه، فما كان بينه وبين الله تعالى يثاب، وما كان بينه وبين العباد يعاقب .اهـ. قوله : (مع الكراهة أي التحريمية ذكره السيد، وفي السراج، والقهستاني تكره الصلاة في الثوب الحرير والثوب المغصوب، وإن صحت، والثواب إلى الله تعالى قوله : (من أحسن ثيابه مراعاة للفظ الزينة في الآية، ويستحب أن تكون سالمة من الخروق. قوله قميص وإزار وعمامة هذا للرجل، وفي المرأة قميص، وخمار، وسراويل، ويكفي له الصلاة فيما يشمل عامة جسدها لما روى عبادة بن الصامت رضي الله عنه قال : صلى بنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في شملة قد توشح بها عقدها بين كتفيه اهـ، ويكفي للمرأة درع ضيق ومقنعة. قوله : ( ويكره في إزار مع القدرة عليها) وكذا يكره أن يصلي في السراويل وحده لما روي أن النبي نهى أن يصلي الرجل في ثوب ليس على عاتقه منه شيء في الشرح وظاهر التعبير بالنهي أن الكراهة تحريمية . قوله : (إستقبال القبلة) هي بالكسر لغة مطلق الجهة. قال الجوهري : يقال : من أين قبلتك أي من أين جهتك، وما لكلامه قبلة أي جهة، وشرعاً كما في القهستاني جهة يصلي نحوها من في الأرض السابعة إلى السماء السابعة مما يحاذي الكعبة أي أو جهتها وغلب هذا الإسم على هذه الجهة حتى صار كالعلم لها، وصارت معرفة عند الإطلاق، وإنما سميت بذلك لأن الناس يقابلونها في صلاتهم، وتسمى أيضاً محراباً لأنّ مقابلها يحارب النفس والشيطان وكانت أول الإسلام إلى بيت المقدس لكن كان ، وهو بمكة لا يستدير الكعبة بل يجعلها بينه وبين بيت المقدس كما صححه
كذا
The Book of Prayer. For prayer, the obligatory act, even if performed by the amount of the tip of the nose according to the weaker opinion, the placement becomes considered non-existent by its existence on impurity, and if he repeats it on a clean place according to the apparent narration, impurity in the place of his nose does not prevent the validity of prayer along with the purity of the rest of the places by consensus, because the nose is less than a dirham, and it becomes as if he restricted himself to the forehead with dislike. And the purity of the place is more binding than the garment, as stipulated textually by indication, since there is no existence without a place, and it may exist without a garment. And it does not harm if his garment falls on impurity that is not attached to it during his prostration. He said: (so that prostration is realized on it) is the reason for the condition of purity of its place. He said: (because the obligatory act, etc.) is the reason for an omitted phrase that should be stated explicitly, its appreciation: and this according to both opinions, i.e., the condition of purity of its place is necessary according to the preponderant opinion of presuming its placement, and according to the weaker opinion of not presuming it because, etc. He said: (according to the weaker opinion, which is that combining the forehead and nose is obligatory, and it is disliked to restrict to one of them). He said: (the placement becomes non-existent) a sentence is omitted here that must be mentioned, and it has been mentioned in the commentary, so say: but when he places the forehead with the tip of the nose, the whole occurs as obligatory, just as if he lengthens the recitation beyond the obligatory amount, then it becomes, etc. The meaning is that the condition of purity of the place of the forehead is obligatory according to the weaker opinion, but when it is placed actually, because its placement with the attribute after its realization is obligatory, like recitation, which is described as obligatory or recommended for what is beyond the obligatory amount, but when it occurs in prayer, it is described as obligatory. He said: (in the apparent narration, and it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that it is permissible if he repeats it on a clean place). He said: (with dislike) i.e., prohibitive dislike, because placing the nose is obligatory, and if he places it on impurity, it is as if he did not place it. He said: (and purity of the place) i.e., and the body, and this is an explanation of the evidence for the condition of purity of these things. He said: (stipulated textually in His saying: 'And your garments purify' [Al-Muddaththir/74]). He said: (by indication) is attached to 'more binding', meaning that it is established that its purity is more binding by indication of the text, and the indication of the text is every meaning understood by the scholar of the placement from the mentioned text due to its sharing with it in the cause, and because it is more deserving of the ruling than it. He said: (since there is no existence, etc.) is the cause for it being more binding by indication. He said: (during his prostration) is attached to 'his garment falls'. Note: purity is only required in prayer because it is a private conversation with the Lord, may He be exalted, so the one praying must be in the best state, and that is in his purity, and the purity of what is connected to him of the garment and place, as stated in the commentary. He said: (And among them is covering the private parts) even with cloudy water, or leaves of a tree, or mud, and covering by darkness is not considered, as in al-Qahistani, like covering with glass, as in al-Quniya. And the formation of the private parts by the tight covering sticking to it does not harm, as in al-Halabi. And the private parts in language are everything that is considered ugly to appear, derived from 'awr, which is deficiency, defect, and ugliness, including 'awr of the eye and the word 'awra' meaning ugly. And the private parts were called 'awrah due to the ugliness of their appearance and lowering the eyes from them. And everything that a person covers out of shame or modesty is a private part, and women are a private part, as in the books of language. He said: (due to consensus on its obligation) i.e., in prayer. As for covering in seclusion, al-Halabi corrected the obligation of covering in it, and the commentator corrected its non-obligation, so there is disagreement in the correction. He said: (And it does not harm if she sees it from his collar) because it is permissible for him to touch her and look at her, but it is contrary to etiquette, as in al-Nahr. And al-Burhan al-Halabi chose that that prayer is disliked even if it is not invalid, and the opposite of the correct is what is from some shaykhs of the condition of covering his private parts from himself, and he branched on it that if his beard is thick and he covers his collar with it, it is valid, otherwise not. He said: (because the effort to prevent it, i.e., to prevent the look of the viewer). He said in the commentary: because covering the private parts in a way that others cannot look at it, if effort is made, leads to hardship. He said: (And the silk garment, etc.) he made the speech about praying in it, but as for praying on it, al-Qahistani said from the book of restrictions, attributing to the prayer of the jewels, its text: and prayer on a silk prayer mat is permissible because what is forbidden is wearing, while benefit in other ways is not forbidden. He said: (And the usurped) it is narrated in al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya from Mukhtarat al-Nawazil: prayer in a usurped land is permissible, but he is punished for his oppression; what is between him and Allah is rewarded, and what is between him and people is punished. He said: (with dislike) i.e., prohibitive dislike, mentioned by al-Sayyid, and in al-Siraj and al-Qahistani: prayer in a silk garment and a usurped garment is disliked, though valid, and the reward is with Allah. He said: (from the best of his garments) observing the word 'adornment' in the verse, and it is recommended that they be free from holes. He said: shirt, waist wrapper, and turban, this for a man, and for a woman: shirt, head cover, and trousers, and it suffices for him to pray in something that covers most of his body, as narrated by 'Ubada ibn al-Samit, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, prayed with us in a shawl that he had wrapped around, tying it between his shoulders, and it suffices for a woman a tight chemise and a veil. He said: (And it is disliked to pray in a waist wrapper with the ability to wear something else) and similarly, it is disliked to pray in trousers alone, as narrated that the Prophet forbade a man to pray in a garment with nothing from it on his shoulder, in the commentary, and the apparent expression of prohibition indicates that the dislike is prohibitive. He said: (Facing the qibla) which, with kasra, in language is an absolute direction. Al-Jawhari said: it is said: from where is your qibla? i.e., from where is your direction, and what is your speech's qibla? i.e., direction, and legally as in al-Qahistani: a direction towards which the one on the seventh earth to the seventh heaven prays, which corresponds to the Ka'ba, i.e., or its direction, and this name became dominant for this direction until it became like a proper noun for it, and became definite when mentioned absolutely, and it was only so named because people face it in their prayer, and it is also called mihrab, because facing it fights the soul and the devil, and at the beginning of Islam it was towards Bayt al-Maqdis, but he, while in Mecca, did not face the Ka'ba, but made it between him and Bayt al-Maqdis, as corrected by so-and-so.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the commentary on Maraqi al-Falah, addressing the conditions for prayer. It covers three main requirements: purity of the place of prostration (specifically the nose), covering the private parts (awrah), and facing the qibla. The author discusses internal Hanafi disputes, such as whether placing the nose on the ground is obligatory (rajih) or merely recommended (marjuh). He explains that impurity on the nose less than a dirham is excused by consensus, but if the nose is placed on impurity, the placement is void, and the prayer must be repeated on a clean place according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya). For covering awrah, he emphasizes ijma on its obligation in prayer, but notes a dispute about covering in seclusion. He also addresses issues like praying in silk or usurped garments, which are permissible but makruh tahrimi, and the recommendation to wear three garments. Regarding qibla, he defines it legally as the direction from the seventh earth to the seventh sky aligned with the Ka'ba, and notes the historical shift from Bayt al-Maqdis. The commentary ensures that students grasp the juristic nuances and the evidence from Quran (e.g., 74:4) and ijma.

Key Terms
عورة (awrah): The parts of the body that must be covered in prayer; for men from navel to knees, for women entire body except face, hands, feet.
القبلة (al-qibla): The direction of the Ka'ba in Mecca, which must be faced during prayer. For those in the seventh earth to seventh heaven, it is the direction corresponding to the Ka'ba.
كراهة تحريمية (karaha tahrimiyya): A prohibition close to haram; an act that must be avoided, though the prayer remains valid if performed. The performer is sinful unless necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preponderant Hanafi view (mufta bihi), what is the ruling on combining the forehead and nose in prostration?
A) It is recommended (sunnah) to combine them.
B) Combining both is obligatory (wajib); restricting to one is makruh tahrimi.
C) Only the forehead is obligatory; the nose is optional.
D) Both are optional; only the forehead matters for validity.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, prostration must include both forehead and nose on a pure place; small impurities are excused, but the preponderant view is that both are wajib.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
8 min
Covering Awrah and Facing Qibla
Explaining the conditions of covering awrah and facing qibla for prayer validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the necessary conditions for covering awrah and facing qibla in prayer, and state the rulings on valid substitutes and makruh cases.

Core Idea
Covering awrah is obligatory by ijma; facing the qibla is obligatory for all on earth to sky aligned with the Ka'ba.

This lesson covers the second and third conditions: covering the private parts and facing the qibla. We'll see the consensus on awrah, permissible substitutes, and the definition of qibla, as well as rulings on silk and usurped garments.

Guided Path
1
State the obligation
Covering awrah is wajib in prayer by ijma (consensus). Facing the qibla is also wajib based on Quran and Sunnah.
The awrah for a free woman is her entire body except face, hands, and feet; for a man, from navel to knees.
2
Describe valid substitutes
If proper garments are unavailable, one may cover with cloudy water, leaves, mud, etc. Darkness is not considered coverage.
Tight clothing that shows the form of the awrah is permissible, as it still covers.
3
Identify makruh practices
Praying in a silk garment, a usurped garment, or alone in a waist wrapper is makruh tahrimi. The prayer is valid but sinful.
Silk is forbidden for men to wear, but praying on a silk mat is permissible.
4
Define the qibla
The qibla is the direction of the Ka'ba; for those in the seventh earth to seventh heaven, it is the direction aligned with the Ka'ba.
The qibla is now the Ka'ba in Mecca; it was initially Bayt al-Maqdis, but was changed.
5
Note the evidence
The obligation of covering awrah is proven by ijma. The obligation of facing qibla is from Quran and Sunnah.
The commentary cites no specific verse for qibla in this passage, but refers to the consensus of scholars.

الفرض، وإن كان يتأدى بمقدار الأرنبة على القول المرجوح يصير الوضع معدوماً حكماً بوجوده على النجس ولو أعاده على طاهر في ظاهر الرواية ولا يمنع نجاسة في محل أنفه مع طهارة باقي المحال بالاتفاق لأن الأنف أقل من الدرهم ويصير كأنه اقتصر على الجبهة مع الكراهة، وطهارة المكان ألزم من الثوب المشروط نصاً بالدلالة إذ لا وجود بدون مكان، وقد توجد بدون ثوب، ولا يضر وقوع ثوبه على نجاسة لا تعلق به حال سجوده

بالنهي أن الكراهة تحريمية . قوله : (إستقبال القبلة) هي بالكسر لغة مطلق الجهة. قال الجوهري : يقال : من أين قبلتك أي من أين جهتك، وما لكلامه قبلة أي جهة، وشرعاً كما في القهستاني جهة يصلي نحوها من في الأرض السابعة إلى السماء السابعة مما يحاذي الكعبة أي أو جهتها وغلب هذا الإسم على هذه الجهة حتى صار كالعلم لها، وصارت معرفة عند الإطلاق، وإنما سميت بذلك لأن الناس يقابلونها في صلاتهم، وتسمى أيضاً محراباً لأنّ مقابلها يحارب النفس والشيطان وكانت أول الإسلام إلى بيت المقدس لكن كان ، وهو بمكة لا يستدير الكعبة بل يجعلها بينه وبين بيت المقدس كما صححه
كذا
The Book of Prayer. For prayer, the obligatory act, even if performed by the amount of the tip of the nose according to the weaker opinion, the placement becomes considered non-existent by its existence on impurity, and if he repeats it on a clean place according to the apparent narration, impurity in the place of his nose does not prevent the validity of prayer along with the purity of the rest of the places by consensus, because the nose is less than a dirham, and it becomes as if he restricted himself to the forehead with dislike. And the purity of the place is more binding than the garment, as stipulated textually by indication, since there is no existence without a place, and it may exist without a garment. And it does not harm if his garment falls on impurity that is not attached to it during his prostration. He said: (so that prostration is realized on it) is the reason for the condition of purity of its place. He said: (because the obligatory act, etc.) is the reason for an omitted phrase that should be stated explicitly, its appreciation: and this according to both opinions, i.e., the condition of purity of its place is necessary according to the preponderant opinion of presuming its placement, and according to the weaker opinion of not presuming it because, etc. He said: (according to the weaker opinion, which is that combining the forehead and nose is obligatory, and it is disliked to restrict to one of them). He said: (the placement becomes non-existent) a sentence is omitted here that must be mentioned, and it has been mentioned in the commentary, so say: but when he places the forehead with the tip of the nose, the whole occurs as obligatory, just as if he lengthens the recitation beyond the obligatory amount, then it becomes, etc. The meaning is that the condition of purity of the place of the forehead is obligatory according to the weaker opinion, but when it is placed actually, because its placement with the attribute after its realization is obligatory, like recitation, which is described as obligatory or recommended for what is beyond the obligatory amount, but when it occurs in prayer, it is described as obligatory. He said: (in the apparent narration, and it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that it is permissible if he repeats it on a clean place). He said: (with dislike) i.e., prohibitive dislike, because placing the nose is obligatory, and if he places it on impurity, it is as if he did not place it. He said: (and purity of the place) i.e., and the body, and this is an explanation of the evidence for the condition of purity of these things. He said: (stipulated textually in His saying: 'And your garments purify' [Al-Muddaththir/74]). He said: (by indication) is attached to 'more binding', meaning that it is established that its purity is more binding by indication of the text, and the indication of the text is every meaning understood by the scholar of the placement from the mentioned text due to its sharing with it in the cause, and because it is more deserving of the ruling than it. He said: (since there is no existence, etc.) is the cause for it being more binding by indication. He said: (during his prostration) is attached to 'his garment falls'. Note: purity is only required in prayer because it is a private conversation with the Lord, may He be exalted, so the one praying must be in the best state, and that is in his purity, and the purity of what is connected to him of the garment and place, as stated in the commentary. He said: (And among them is covering the private parts) even with cloudy water, or leaves of a tree, or mud, and covering by darkness is not considered, as in al-Qahistani, like covering with glass, as in al-Quniya. And the formation of the private parts by the tight covering sticking to it does not harm, as in al-Halabi. And the private parts in language are everything that is considered ugly to appear, derived from 'awr, which is deficiency, defect, and ugliness, including 'awr of the eye and the word 'awra' meaning ugly. And the private parts were called 'awrah due to the ugliness of their appearance and lowering the eyes from them. And everything that a person covers out of shame or modesty is a private part, and women are a private part, as in the books of language. He said: (due to consensus on its obligation) i.e., in prayer. As for covering in seclusion, al-Halabi corrected the obligation of covering in it, and the commentator corrected its non-obligation, so there is disagreement in the correction. He said: (And it does not harm if she sees it from his collar) because it is permissible for him to touch her and look at her, but it is contrary to etiquette, as in al-Nahr. And al-Burhan al-Halabi chose that that prayer is disliked even if it is not invalid, and the opposite of the correct is what is from some shaykhs of the condition of covering his private parts from himself, and he branched on it that if his beard is thick and he covers his collar with it, it is valid, otherwise not. He said: (because the effort to prevent it, i.e., to prevent the look of the viewer). He said in the commentary: because covering the private parts in a way that others cannot look at it, if effort is made, leads to hardship. He said: (And the silk garment, etc.) he made the speech about praying in it, but as for praying on it, al-Qahistani said from the book of restrictions, attributing to the prayer of the jewels, its text: and prayer on a silk prayer mat is permissible because what is forbidden is wearing, while benefit in other ways is not forbidden. He said: (And the usurped) it is narrated in al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya from Mukhtarat al-Nawazil: prayer in a usurped land is permissible, but he is punished for his oppression; what is between him and Allah is rewarded, and what is between him and people is punished. He said: (with dislike) i.e., prohibitive dislike, mentioned by al-Sayyid, and in al-Siraj and al-Qahistani: prayer in a silk garment and a usurped garment is disliked, though valid, and the reward is with Allah. He said: (from the best of his garments) observing the word 'adornment' in the verse, and it is recommended that they be free from holes. He said: shirt, waist wrapper, and turban, this for a man, and for a woman: shirt, head cover, and trousers, and it suffices for him to pray in something that covers most of his body, as narrated by 'Ubada ibn al-Samit, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, prayed with us in a shawl that he had wrapped around, tying it between his shoulders, and it suffices for a woman a tight chemise and a veil. He said: (And it is disliked to pray in a waist wrapper with the ability to wear something else) and similarly, it is disliked to pray in trousers alone, as narrated that the Prophet forbade a man to pray in a garment with nothing from it on his shoulder, in the commentary, and the apparent expression of prohibition indicates that the dislike is prohibitive. He said: (Facing the qibla) which, with kasra, in language is an absolute direction. Al-Jawhari said: it is said: from where is your qibla? i.e., from where is your direction, and what is your speech's qibla? i.e., direction, and legally as in al-Qahistani: a direction towards which the one on the seventh earth to the seventh heaven prays, which corresponds to the Ka'ba, i.e., or its direction, and this name became dominant for this direction until it became like a proper noun for it, and became definite when mentioned absolutely, and it was only so named because people face it in their prayer, and it is also called mihrab, because facing it fights the soul and the devil, and at the beginning of Islam it was towards Bayt al-Maqdis, but he, while in Mecca, did not face the Ka'ba, but made it between him and Bayt al-Maqdis, as corrected by so-and-so.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the commentary on Maraqi al-Falah, addressing the conditions for prayer. It covers three main requirements: purity of the place of prostration (specifically the nose), covering the private parts (awrah), and facing the qibla. The author discusses internal Hanafi disputes, such as whether placing the nose on the ground is obligatory (rajih) or merely recommended (marjuh). He explains that impurity on the nose less than a dirham is excused by consensus, but if the nose is placed on impurity, the placement is void, and the prayer must be repeated on a clean place according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya). For covering awrah, he emphasizes ijma on its obligation in prayer, but notes a dispute about covering in seclusion. He also addresses issues like praying in silk or usurped garments, which are permissible but makruh tahrimi, and the recommendation to wear three garments. Regarding qibla, he defines it legally as the direction from the seventh earth to the seventh sky aligned with the Ka'ba, and notes the historical shift from Bayt al-Maqdis. The commentary ensures that students grasp the juristic nuances and the evidence from Quran (e.g., 74:4) and ijma.

Key Terms
عورة (awrah): The parts of the body that must be covered in prayer; for men from navel to knees, for women entire body except face, hands, feet.
القبلة (al-qibla): The direction of the Ka'ba in Mecca, which must be faced during prayer. For those in the seventh earth to seventh heaven, it is the direction corresponding to the Ka'ba.
كراهة تحريمية (karaha tahrimiyya): A prohibition close to haram; an act that must be avoided, though the prayer remains valid if performed. The performer is sinful unless necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying in a usurped garment (without the owner's permission)?
A) The prayer is invalid because the garment is unlawful.
B) The prayer is valid but makruh tahrimi; the person is sinful for using it.
C) The prayer is valid and not disliked because necessity allows it.
D) The prayer is invalid unless the person repents and repeats it.

Key Takeaway
Covering awrah and facing qibla are obligatory conditions for prayer; makruh acts like praying in silk or usurped garments do not invalidate the prayer.

Rulings on Covering and Clothing in Prayer
Commentary on the conditions of satr and recommended clothing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on covering the awrah in prayer, the validity of prayer in silk and usurped garments, and the recommended clothing for men and women.

Core Idea
Covering awrah is wajib in prayer; silk and usurped garments are valid but makruh tahrimi.

This lesson explores the conditions of satr (covering) during prayer according to the Hanafi school. We will examine the obligation to cover, the permissibility and dislike of praying in certain fabrics, and the sunnah attire for men and women. The commentary by al-Tahtawi clarifies key distinctions, such as the difference between covering from others and covering from oneself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on covering the awrah
The passage states that covering the awrah is wajib in prayer by consensus. Note: there is a difference of opinion on whether it is wajib in privacy (al-Halabi said yes, the commentator said no).
The mufta bihi is that it is wajib in prayer, not necessarily in privacy.
2
Distinguish covering from others vs. from oneself
The commentator clarifies that covering the awrah in a way that prevents all possible views causes hardship, so it is not required. A minority view required covering from oneself (e.g., using one's beard to cover a hole), but this is not the relied-upon position.
The mufta bihi is that covering from oneself is not required.
3
State the ruling on silk and usurped garments
Prayer in a silk garment or a usurped garment is valid but makruh tahrimi (prohibited dislike). The same applies to praying on usurped land. Using a silk prayer rug is permissible because the prohibition is on wearing.
The prayer is valid but the person is sinful for wearing silk or using usurped property.
4
Describe the recommended clothing
For men: it is mustahabb to pray in three garments: shirt (qamis), waist-wrapper (izar), and turban (imama). For women: shift (qamis), headcover (khimar), and trousers (sarawil). It is recommended to wear one's best garments, observing the Qur'anic 'zinah'.
It is sufficient for a woman to wear a shift and headcover that cover her entire body.
5
Explain the dislike of praying in only an izar or trousers
It is makruh tahrimi for a man to pray in only an izar or only trousers when he is able to wear something over his shoulders, based on the prophetic prohibition. The expression 'prohibition' indicates tahrimi dislike.
This applies when one has the ability to cover the shoulders; otherwise, the prayer is valid.

Source Text

Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (hashiya) on the rulings of covering (satr) and clothing in prayer. It begins by addressing the issue of a woman looking at a man's awrah: the earlier position stated that it does not harm because it is permissible for the husband to touch and look at his wife, but it is contrary to good manners. However, Burhan al-Halabi held that the prayer is disliked even if not invalidated. A minority view required the person to cover from himself, e.g., if a man had a thick beard, covering his opening with it would be sufficient. The text then addresses the ruling on praying in a silk garment: it is valid with tahrimi dislike. Similarly, a usurped garment and usurped land: prayer is valid but one is sinful. The recommended clothing for a man is three garments: shirt, izaar, and turban. For a woman: shift, headcover, and trousers. It is disliked to pray in only an izaar or trousers while able to wear something over the shoulders, based on a prophetic prohibition. This concludes the discussion of covering conditions before moving to the next condition: facing the Qibla.

Key Terms
ستر العورة (satr al-awrah): Covering the private parts from the navel to the knee for men, and entire body except face and hands for women during prayer.
كراهة تحريمية (karahah tahrimiyyah): A level of dislike close to prohibition; the act is sinful but the prayer is valid and does not require repetition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
B) The prayer is valid but disliked (makruh tahrimi)
C) The prayer is valid and there is no dislike
D) The prayer is invalid only if the garment is pure silk

Key Takeaway
Covering the awrah is wajib for prayer; silk and usurped garments are valid but makruh tahrimi, and the recommended attire for men is three garments and for women shift, headcover, and trousers.

Sincerity (Ikhlas) in Prayer and Combining Intentions
Definition of sincerity and rules for combining intentions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of ikhlas, distinguish between riya that negates reward and riya that reduces reward, and apply the Hanafi rule that a single initial intention suffices for combining multiple acts of worship.

Core Idea
Sincerity is a secret between you and your Lord; initial intention suffices for all subsequent parts of worship.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi defines the essence of sincerity (ikhlas) in prayer and clarifies the effect of showing-off (riya). It then provides practical rules for combining multiple intentions in acts like ghusl, wudu, and supererogatory prayers. Understanding these points guards your worship from losing reward and helps you perform multiple devotions efficiently.

Guided Path
1
Define ikhlas and riya
Identify the definitions from the passage: ikhlas is a secret between servant and Lord; riya is performing worship for people. Note that riya can be total (no prayer without audience) or partial (improving performance for them).
Ikhlas is not a pillar of worship but a condition for full reward.
2
Determine the effect of riya on obligatory acts
The passage says 'There is no riya in obligatory acts regarding the dropping of the obligatory duty.' Understand this: the obligation is still fulfilled despite riya, but reward is affected.
If one would not pray without an audience, he gets no reward; if he would have prayed anyway but improved for show, he loses reward only for the improvement.
3
Identify the conditions for a valid intention
The passage lists four conditions: Islam, discernment (tamyiz), knowledge of what is intended (ilm al-munwa), and no contradiction between the intention and the act. List them and give an example of each.
For example, tamyiz means a child who distinguishes but has not reached puberty can still make a valid intention for nafl acts.
4
Apply the rule of initial intention to combined acts
Work through the examples: a single ghusl can cover janabah, Eid, and Friday; a single wudu can cover sleep, backbiting, and eating camel meat; one can intend multiple supererogatory prayers together. The principle is that if the acts are means or supererogatory, one intention at the start covers them all.
This does not apply to obligatory prayers – you cannot combine two fard prayers with one intention.
5
Recognize the Hanafi position on sufficiency of initial intention
The mu‘tamad view is that for acts of worship consisting of actions (like prayer or wudu), the intention at the beginning suffices for the entire act. There is no need to renew niyyah for each part.
This contrasts with the view of some other schools (like the Shafi‘is) who consider the intention must be present for each distinct part.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ويتحقق الإخلاص فيها أي في الصلاة، والإخلاص بينك سر وبين ربك لا يطلع عليه ملك فيكتبه ولا شيطان فيفسده ولا هوى فيميله ذكره الحموي، وذلك بأن تريده تعالى بطاعته ولا تريد سواه، وفي الخلاصة : لا رياء في الفرائض اهـ وفي البزازية شرع بالإخلاص، ثم خالطه الرياء، فالعبرة للسابق ولا رياء في الفرائض في حق سقوط الواجب اهـ وحقيقة الرياء هو أنه إن خلا عن الناس لا يصلي، وإن كان عند الناس يصلي، فهذا لا ثواب له لأنه أشرك بعبادة ربه، ولو أحسنها لأجلهم فله ثواب الأصل لا الإحسان، ثم إنه إن جمع بين عبادات الوسائل في النية صح كما لو اغتسل الجنابة، وعيد وجمعة إجتمعت ونال ثواب الكل، وكما لو توضأ لنوم، وبعد غيبة وأكل لحم جزور، وكذا يصح لو نوى نافلتين أو أكثر كما لو نوى تحية مسجد، وسنة وضوء، وضحى، وكسوف، والمعتمد أن العبادات ذات الأفعال يكتفي بالنية في أوّلها، ولا يحتاج إليها في كل جزء إكتفاء بإنسحابها عليها، ويشترط لها الإسلام والتمييز والعلم بالمنوى، وأن لا يأتي بمناف بين النية، والمنوي.
His saying: 'And sincerity is realized in it, that is, in prayer. And sincerity is a secret between you and your Lord; no angel can see it to write it, no devil can spoil it, and no desire can turn it away.' Al-Hamawi mentioned this. That is, you intend Him by His obedience and do not intend anyone else. And in al-Khulasah: 'There is no showing-off (riya) in obligatory acts.' And in al-Bazzaziyyah: 'One begins with sincerity, then showing-off mixes with it; consideration is given to the earlier state. And there is no showing-off in obligatory acts regarding the dropping of the obligatory duty.' The reality of showing-off is that if one is alone without people, he does not pray; but if people are present, he prays. Such a person has no reward because he associated others with his worship of his Lord. If he performed it well for their sake, he gets the reward of the basic act, not the improvement. Then, if one combines acts of worship that are means in his intention, it is valid, such as if he takes a bath for janabah, and the two Eids and Friday coincide, and he attains the reward of all. Similarly, if he performs wudu for sleep, for backbiting, and for eating camel meat, it is valid. Likewise, if he intends two or more supererogatory prayers, such as intending tahiyyat al-masjid, sunnah of wudu, Duha, and eclipse prayer. The relied-upon view is that for acts of worship consisting of actions, the intention at the beginning suffices, and there is no need for intention in each part, as it is included over all. For it, Islam, discernment, knowledge of the intended, and the absence of something contradictory between the intention and the intended are required.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the concept of sincerity (ikhlas) in prayer and provides rules for combining multiple intentions. Sincerity is described as a secret between the servant and the Lord, immune from external interference. The author quotes al-Hamawi and others to emphasize that the root of showing-off (riya) is performing worship solely for people. If one begins with sincerity and later shows off, the earlier sincere intention is considered. Obligatory acts are generally free from riya in the sense that they fulfill the obligation regardless of intention, but reward depends on sincerity. The practical rule is that combining multiple acts of worship under a single intention is valid if they are means or supererogatory acts. Examples: a single ghusl can serve multiple purposes like janabah and Eid; a single wudu can serve multiple intentions like sleep and camel meat consumption. For supererogatory prayers, one can intend tahiyyat al-masjid, sunnah wudu, Duha, and eclipse all together. The relied-upon (mu'tamad) position is that once the intention is made at the start, it suffices for the entire act; there is no need to renew intention for each part. The conditions for a valid intention include Islam (being a Muslim), discernment (being of sound mind), knowledge of what is intended (at least in general terms), and no contradiction between the intention and the intended act.

Key Terms
الإخلاص (al-ikhlas): Purity of intention in worship, doing it solely for Allah without any worldly motive.
الرياء (al-riya): Showing off in worship by performing it for the sake of people rather than Allah.
النية (al-niyyah): Intention; for acts of worship, it is the mental resolve to perform a specific act for Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a person begins an obligatory prayer with sincerity but then mixes in some showing-off?
A) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) The earlier sincerity is considered, and the prayer is valid with reward.
C) The prayer is valid but no reward is given.
D) Only the later part is considered.

Key Takeaway
Sincerity is between you and Allah; initial intention covers all parts of worship; riya may reduce but not invalidate obligatory acts.

Takbir Tahrimah: Condition not Pillar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on takbir tahrimah being a condition vs pillar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies takbir tahrimah as a condition (shart) rather than a pillar (rukn), and apply the thamarah (practical consequence) to specific scenarios.

Core Idea
Takbir tahrimah is a condition for prayer, not a pillar—its omission does not invalidate but its advance is permissible.

In this passage, we delve into an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal nature of the opening takbir (takbir tahrimah). While all agree that saying 'Allahu Akbar' at the beginning of prayer is essential, the precise classification—whether it is a condition (shart) or a pillar (rukn)—has significant practical implications. The majority Hanafi view, held by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, considers it a condition, while Muhammad al-Shaybani considers it a pillar. Understanding the distinction helps you evaluate the validity of prayer in various edge cases.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the two conflicting positions within the Hanafi school: the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold it as a condition (shart), while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds it as a pillar (rukn).
Also note that Imam al-Shafi'i agrees with Muhammad.
2
Analyze the evidence for shart
Examine the Quranic proof (Surah al-A'la, 87:15) used by the two shaykhs. The conjunction 'and' or 'then' between 'mention' and 'pray' indicates separation, so the takbir is distinct from the prayer itself.
Also consider the logical argument that conditions can be performed before the act.
3
Analyze the evidence for rukn
Understand Muhammad's analogy: since takbir is a prescribed recitation in the standing posture, it resembles Quranic recitation, which is a pillar.
The Hanafi response refutes this analogy.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
Apply the difference to four concrete scenarios given in the text: carrying impurity, facing away from qibla, uncovering awrah, and performing takbir before time. Note how the ruling changes based on the classification.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Conclude that the relied-upon position in the school is that of the two shaykhs (shart), as affirmed by the verifying scholars (al-muhaqqiqun).
This is the view adopted for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يشترط (التحريمة) وليست ركنا وعليه عامة المشايخ المحققين على الصحيح والتحريم جعل قوله: (لتتميز العبادة عن العادة) أو يتميز بعض العبادة عن بعض الأمثال الأول الإمساك عن المفطرات فإنه يكون لعدم الحاجة إليه، أو للحمية فلا يمتاز الصوم عنه إلا بالنية، ومثال الثاني في الصلاة مثلاً فإنها تكون فرضاً وواجباً، ونفلاً فشرعت فيها النية ليتميز بعضها عن بعض، وفي المجتبي وغيره من عجز عن إحضار القلب في النية، أو يشك في النية يكفيه اللسان كذا في الشرح . قوله : ( ويشترط التحريمة هو قول الشيخين لقوله تعالى وذكر اسم ربه فصلی، فإنه عطف الصلاة عليها العطف يقتضي المغايرة، وليس من عطف الكل على الجزء فإنه إنما يكون لنكتة بلاغية وهي غير ظاهرة هنا قوله وليست ركناً) أشار به إلى خلاف محمد فإنه يقول بركنيتها لأنها ذكر مفروض في القيام، فكانت ركناً كالقراءة، وتظهر الثمرة فيما إذا كان حاملاً لنجاسة مانعة، فألقاها عند فراغه منها أو كان منحرفاً عن القبلة فاستقبلها، أو مكشوف العورة فسترها بعمل يسير أو شرع في التكبير قبل ظهور الزوال، ثم ظهر عند الفراغ، فعندهما تجوز صلاته لوجود الأركان مستجمعة للشروط، وتقدم الشرط جائز بالإجماع، وعبارة البرهان، وإنما اشترط لها ما اشترط للصلاة لا باعتبار ركنيتها، بل باعتبار إتصالها بالقيام الذي هو ركنها، وقد منع ذلك الزيلعي وعند محمد، والشافعي لا تجوز لأنها ركن، وقد أداه المنافي، أو قبل الوقت وجاز بناء النفل على تحريمة الفرض مع الكراهة عندهما لأن النفل مطلقاً صلاة، والفرض صلاة مخصوصة ففي الفرض معنى النفل، وزيادة لأن الخاص يتضمن العام، فكان العقد على الفرض متضمناً للعقد على النقل، ولأنّ الشرط لا يشترط تحصيله لكل صلاة كالطهارة، بل يصح شرط الفرض للنفل، ولا يجوز عند القائل بالركنية، وأما بناء الفرض على تحريمة فرض آخر، أو على تحريمة نقل فظاهر المذهب، والجمهور منعه، وأما بناء النقل على تحريمة نقل آخر فلا شك في صحته إتفاقاً لأن الكل صلاة واحدة. قوله: (وعليه عامة المشايخ وهو قول المحققين من مشايخنا بدائع، وهو المعتبر من المذهب منية المصلي.
The opening takbir (tahrimah) is a condition, not a pillar, and upon this are the generality of the verified scholars according to the correct view. The tahrimah makes [the prayer] forbidden [to worldly matters]. His saying: 'To distinguish worship from habit' or to distinguish some acts of worship from others. Example of the first: refraining from nullifiers [of fast] may be due to lack of need or for diet, so fasting is only distinguished from it by intention. Example of the second: in prayer, for instance, it may be obligatory, mandatory, or supererogatory, so intention is legislated to distinguish some from others. In al-Mujtaba and others: whoever is unable to bring the heart into intention or doubts his intention, the tongue suffices him, as in the commentary. His saying: 'And the tahrimah is required' is the view of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) due to His saying, exalted is He: 'And mention the name of his Lord and pray.' For He connected prayer to it; connection implies difference, and it is not connection of the whole to the part, for that is only for a rhetorical nuance which is not apparent here. His saying: 'And it is not a pillar' refers to the disagreement of Muhammad, for he says it is a pillar because it is a recitation prescribed in standing, so it is a pillar like recitation. The practical consequence appears in the case of one carrying an impure substance that prevents [validity], and he throws it away upon finishing the takbir; or if he was turned away from the qibla and then faced it; or if his awrah was exposed and he covered it with a slight action; or if he began the takbir before the appearance of zawal (noon) and then it appeared upon finishing. According to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) his prayer is valid because the pillars are found with conditions, and the precedence of a condition is permissible by consensus. The expression of al-Burhan: 'It is only required for what is required for prayer, not by virtue of its being a pillar, but by virtue of its connection to the standing which is its pillar.' Al-Zayla'i has prohibited that. According to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, it is not valid because it is a pillar and he has performed something contradictory or before the time. And it is permissible to base supererogatory prayer on the tahrimah of obligatory prayer with disapproval according to them (the two shaykhs), because supererogatory is absolutely prayer, and obligatory is specific prayer, so in the obligatory there is the meaning of supererogatory and more, because the specific includes the general. So the contract on the obligatory implicitly includes the contract on the supererogatory. Also because a condition is not required to be obtained for every prayer like purification, but the condition of the obligatory is valid for the supererogatory. It is not permissible according to the one who says it is a pillar. As for basing obligatory prayer on the tahrimah of another obligatory, or on a supererogatory tahrimah, the apparent school and the majority forbid it. As for basing supererogatory on another supererogatory tahrimah, there is no doubt of its validity unanimously, because all is one prayer. His saying: 'And upon this are the generality of the shaykhs and it is the view of the verifiers among our shaykhs in al-Bada'i, and it is the relied upon of the school in Munyat al-Musalli.'
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal nature of the opening takbir (takbir tahrimah) in prayer. The author establishes that the correct Hanafi position, held by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs), is that takbir tahrimah is a condition (shart) for the validity of prayer, not a pillar (rukn). The evidence is drawn from the Quranic verse 'And mention the name of your Lord and pray' (Surah al-A'la, 15), where the conjunction 'and' (waw) indicates a distinction between the mention (dhikr) and the prayer, showing that the takbir is separate from the prayer itself—it is a prerequisite, not an integral part. Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam al-Shafi'i, however, consider it a pillar, arguing that it is a prescribed recitation in the standing posture, analogous to Quranic recitation. The practical consequence (thamarah) of this difference is illustrated with scenarios: if someone performs the takbir while carrying an impurity, then discards it immediately after; or if they face a direction other than the qibla during takbir and then turn correctly; or if they cover their awrah during takbir with a slight action; or if they begin the takbir before the entry of zuhr time and finish after it—according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the prayer is valid because the pillars were performed while fulfilling all conditions, and advancing a condition (like tahrimah) before its time is permissible by consensus. Muhammad and al-Shafi'i would rule the prayer invalid because the takbir (a pillar) was performed in a state of deficiency. The passage also discusses the permissibility of combining intentions: building a supererogatory prayer on the tahrimah of an obligatory prayer is allowed with slight dislike according to the two shaykhs, because the specific (obligatory) includes the general (supererogatory). Building a supererogatory on another supererogatory is unanimously valid. The relied-upon position (mu'tamad) in the school is that takbir tahrimah is a condition, not a pillar, as stated by the verifying scholars.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying 'Allahu Akbar') that makes worldly actions forbidden during prayer.
شرط (shart): A condition that must be present for validity but is not an integral part of the act.
ركن (rukn): A pillar or integral part of the act; omission invalidates it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on the legal nature of takbir tahrimah?
A) It is a pillar (rukn) according to all Hanafis.
B) It is a condition (shart) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
C) It is neither a condition nor a pillar.
D) It is a pillar according to Abu Hanifa but a condition according to Muhammad.

Key Takeaway
Takbir tahrimah is a condition (shart) for prayer according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, not a pillar (rukn), with significant practical consequences for the validity of prayer in edge cases.

The First Condition of Takbir Tahrimah: Concurrency with Intention
Condition of muqaranah between takbir and niyyah, with actual and legal concurrency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of muqaranah, distinguish actual from legal concurrency, and apply the ruling to the follower's intention timing.

Core Idea
A valid takbir requires the intention to be concurrent — either at the same moment or without any disruptive action in between.

This passage explains the first of twelve conditions for the validity of the takbir tahrimah (the opening 'Allahu Akbar' of prayer). The key requirement is that the intention (niyyah) must be concurrent with the takbir. Hanafi fiqh permits two forms of concurrency: actual (at the same instant) and legal (advanced before the takbir, provided no distracting action intervenes). This lesson unpacks both types and clarifies the special rules for followers (muqtadi) in congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its ruling
Read the opening sentence: the first condition for validity of takbir tahrimah is that it be concurrent with the intention, either actually or legally. Understand that this is a condition (shart), not a pillar.
The condition is based on consensus (ijma') regarding actions that break continuity.
2
Define actual concurrency (haqiqi)
Actual concurrency means the intention occurs at the very moment one begins uttering the takbir. This is the preferred practice. The text also discusses whether concurrency is achieved if the intention comes after some letters of 'Allahu Akbar'; the apparent view is yes.
Actual concurrency is best but not strictly required.
3
Define legal concurrency (hukmi)
Legal concurrency means the intention is made before the takbir, but without any action that indicates disinterest (i'rad), such as eating, drinking, or speaking. Walking to the prayer place or performing wudu does not break the connection.
The intention can be advanced even before the prayer time, as long as it remains intact.
4
Apply the rule to the follower's intention (iqtida')
The passage discusses whether a follower can advance his intention to follow the imam before the imam's takbir. Some Bukhara scholars disallow it; the preferred view is that the follower intends when the imam takes his position for imamate.
The difference between advancing intention for prayer itself (which is allowed) and advancing intention for following (restricted) requires further analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويشترط لصحة التحريمة إثنا عشر شرطاً ذكرت منها سبعة متناً والباقي شرحاً فالأول من شروط صحة التحريمة أن توجد مقارنة للنية حقيقة أو حكماً بلا فاصل) بينها وبين النية بأجنبي يمنع الإتصال للإجماع عليه كالا كل والشرب والكلام فأما المشي للصلاة، والوضوء حقيقة هو قوله: (أن توجد مقارنة للنبة حقيقة) مثال المقارنة حقيقة أن ينوي مقارناً للشروع بالتكبير، وهو الأفضل بإجماع أصحابنا، وانظر هل تكون تلك المقارنة ولو وجدت بعد ذكر بعض حروف الإسم الكريم أو ذكر كله قبل الفراغ من أكبل والظاهر نعم وحرره قوله : (أو حكماً) مثال المقارنة الحكمية أن يقدم النية على الشروع قالوا : لو نوى عند الوضوء أنه يصلي الظهر مثلاً، ولم يشتغل بعد النية بعمل يدل على الأعراض كأكل وشرب وكلام ونحوها ثم انتهى إلى محل الصلاة، ولم تحضره النية جازت صلاته بالنية السابقة، ويجوز تقديمها على الوقت كسائر الشروط ما لم يوجد ما يقطعها، ونقل ابن أمير حاج عن أبي هريرة بن هبيرة إشتراط دخول الوقت للنية المتقدمة عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله ، وينبغي أن يكون وقت نية الإمامة عند الشروع وإن لم يقتد به أحد لأنه قد يقتدي به من لا يراه من الملائكة والجن أفاده الحموي، خلافاً لما في الأشباه من أنه ينبغي أن يكون وقت إقتداء أحد به لا قبله وأما نية المأموم الإقتداء ففي القهستاني، ولا يجوز تقديم نية إقتدائه عن تحريمة الإمام عند بعض أئمة بخارى، وصحح، وقيل ينوي بعد قول الإمام الله قبل قوله أكبر، والذي عليه عامة العلماء أنه ينوي حين وقف الإمام موقف الإمامة وهو أجود كما في النظم اهـ، ويطلب الفرق بين صحة تقديم نية الصلاة وهي فرض دون تقديم نية الإقتداء على هذا الوقت، وهو كذلك، والذي ذكره الشارح في الإمامة جواز تقديمها فالحكم فيهما
For the validity of the tahrimah, twelve conditions are required; seven are mentioned in the matn and the remainder in the commentary. The first of the conditions for the validity of the tahrimah is that it be concurrent with the intention, either actually or legally, without any foreign interruption between it and the intention that prevents connection, by consensus—such as eating, drinking, or speaking. As for walking for prayer or performing wudu, that does not break continuity. His saying: 'that it exists concurrent with the intention actually' – an example of actual concurrency is that he intends while starting the takbir, and this is the best by consensus of our companions. Consider whether this concurrency occurs even if it is after pronouncing some letters of the noble name or after pronouncing all of it before finishing the takbir; the apparent view is yes, and it is clarified. His saying: 'or legally' – an example of legal concurrency is that he advances the intention before starting. They said: if he intends at the time of wudu that he will pray zuhr, for example, and after the intention he does not engage in an action indicating disinterest, like eating, drinking, speaking, etc., then he proceeds to the prayer place and the intention is not present in his mind, his prayer is valid with the previous intention. It is permissible to advance it before the time of prayer like other conditions, as long as nothing cuts it off. Ibn Amir Hajj reported from Abu Hurayra ibn Hubayra that the condition of the entry of time for the advanced intention is from Abu Hanifa. The time for the intention of imamate should be upon starting, even if no one follows him, because he may be followed by unseen beings like angels and jinn—this is from al-Hamawi, contrary to what is in al-Ashbah that it should be at the time someone actually follows him, not before. As for the follower's intention to follow, it is stated in al-Qahistani that according to some scholars of Bukhara, it is not permissible to advance the intention of following before the imam's tahrimah, and it is corrected. Some say he intends after the imam says 'Allah' before saying 'Akbar'. The predominant view of the scholars is that he intends when the imam takes the position of imamate, and this is best as in al-Nazm. The difference between the validity of advancing the intention of prayer, which is obligatory, and the non-validity of advancing the intention of following at this time should be sought. It is as stated. The commentator mentioned in the section on imamate the permissibility of advancing it, so the ruling is the same in both matters.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the first of twelve conditions for the validity of takbir tahrimah: concurrency (muqaranah) with the intention. The condition is that the takbir and the intention must be simultaneous either in actual fact (haqiqah) or in legal consideration (hukman), without any foreign element interrupting their connection. Eating, drinking, or speaking break the continuity, but walking to the prayer place or performing wudu does not. Actual concurrency means the intention is made at the same moment as pronouncing the takbir; this is considered the best practice by consensus of Hanafi scholars. Legal concurrency occurs when the intention is made before the takbir, provided no action showing disinterest (like eating or speaking) occurs in between. An example: if one intends at the time of wudu that he will pray zuhr, and after wudu goes directly to prayer without any distractions, the prayer is valid even if he does not consciously recall the intention at the moment of takbir. The intention can be made before the prayer time, as long as it remains intact. However, there is a difference regarding the intention for following the imam: the follower cannot advance his intention of following (iqtida) before the imam begins his takbir; the recommended time is when the imam takes his position for prayer. The passage discusses various opinions on the exact timing for the follower's intention, with the preferred view being that the follower intends when the imam stands in the place of imamah. The commentator (sharih) is quoted as permitting advancing the intention for the imamate, which seems to conflict with the earlier restriction; the author notes that the ruling is the same in both cases, implying that the follower's intention can also be advanced under specific conditions, but this requires further clarification.

Key Terms
المقارنة (al-muqaranah): Temporal concurrence between the takbir and the intention; either actual (at the same moment) or legal (without disruptive interval).
النية المتقدمة (al-niyyah al-mutaqaddimah): Intention made before the act of worship, which remains valid as long as no action indicating disinterest occurs.
الإقتداء (al-iqtida): The follower's intention to pray behind the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following actions breaks the legal concurrency (muqaranah hukmiyyah) between an advanced intention and the takbir?
A) Walking to the prayer place.
B) Performing wudu.
C) Speaking a word unrelated to prayer.
D) Sitting quietly in the mosque.

Key Takeaway
The takbir tahrimah is valid if the intention is concurrent with it, either actually or legally, provided no action indicating disinterest intervenes.
