Prayer on a Thick Felt (Lubbad) with Mixed Purity
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying on a lubbad with pure top and impure bottom and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Thickness transforms one object into two: prayer on the pure top of a thick felt is valid even if the bottom is impure.

Impurity on a surface does not always invalidate the entire object. This lesson unpacks the principle of 'like two garments' applied to a thick felt carpet (lubbad). You will see how Abu Hanifa and Muhammad differ from Abu Yusuf on the conceptual separation of layers, and which view is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the ruling
Read the first sentence: prayer on a lubbad whose upper surface is pure and lower is impure. The ruling is that prayer is valid (tajuz). Identify the hukm level: sahih.
The Arabic 'تجوز الصلاة' indicates permissibility/validity.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The text gives the reason: 'because due to its thickness it is like two garments' and 'like two things on top of each other'. This is qiyas: the thickness allows conceptual splitting into two independent layers.
The illa is thickness (thikhanah) that permits separation.
3
Spot the intra-Hanafi dispute
The phrase 'cinda huma khilafan li-Abi Yusuf' shows that Abu Yusuf disagrees. He considers the lubbad as one connected object, so impurity in any part affects the whole.
Abu Yusuf's view is that prayer would be invalid.
4
Determine the mufta bili
The text states the position of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) first, and later scholars like Shaykh Abu Bakr al-Iskafi prefer it. The hashya indicates that both views have weight, but the first is relied upon.
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في متعلقات الشروط وفروعها (تجوز الصلاة) أي تصح (على لبد) بكسر اللام وسكون الباء الموحدة وجهه الأعلى طاهر (و) ووجهه (الأسفل (نجس) نجاسة مانعة لأنه لثخانته كثوبين وكلوح ثخين يمكن فصله لوحين وأسفله نجس تجوز الصلاة على الطاهر منه عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف لأنه كشيئين فوق بعضهما (و) تصح الصلاة (على ثوب طاهر وبطانته نجسة إذا كان غير مضرب لأنه كثوبين فوق بعضهما (و) تصح (على طرف طاهر) أو ثوب (وإن تحرك الطرف النجس بحركته لأنه ليس ملتبساً به (على الصحيح ولو تنجس أحد طرفي عمامته) أو ملحفته (فألقاه) أي الطرف النجس (وأبقى الطاهر على رأسه ولم يتحرك النجس بحركته جازت صلاته لعدم تلبسه به (وإن تحرك) الطرف النجس بحركته (لا تجوز صلاته لأنه حامل لها حكما إلا إذا لم يجد غيره للضرورة (وفاقد ما يزيل به (النجاسة المانعة يصلي معها ولا إعادة عليه لأنّ التكليف بحسب الوسع (ولا) إعادة (على فاقد ما يستر عورته ولو حريراً فإنه إن وجد الحرير لزمه الصلاة فيه لأنّ فرض الستر أقوى من منع لبسه في هذه الحالة (أو) كان (حشيشاً أو طيناً) أو ماء كدراً يصلي داخله بالإيماء لأنه ساتر في الجملة ( فإن وجده) أي الساتر (ولو بالإباحة و) الحال أن ربعه طاهر لا تصح صلاته عارياً) على الأصح كالماء الذي أبيح للمتيمم إذ لا يلحقه المانية، وربع الشيء يقوم مقام كله في مواضع منها هذا ولم تقم ثلاثة أرباعه النجسة مقام
A chapter on related conditions and their branches. (Prayer is permissible) meaning valid (on a lubbad) with kasr of lam and sukun of ba, its upper surface is pure, (and) its (lower surface (is impure) with preventing impurity, because due to its thickness it is like two garments, and a thick block that can be separated into two planks, and its lower part is impure, prayer is valid on the pure part according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) contrary to Abu Yusuf because it is like two things on top of each other. (And) prayer is valid (on a garment with pure outer and impure lining if it is not quilted, because it is like two garments on top of each other. (And) prayer is valid (on a pure edge) or garment (even if the impure edge moves with his movement, because he is not wearing it, according to the correct view. And if one end of his turban or his wrap becomes impure, and he casts it aside, i.e., the impure end, and keeps the pure on his head, and the impure does not move with his movement, his prayer is permissible due to not wearing it. And if the impure end moves with his movement, his prayer is not permissible because he is carrying it in effect, unless he finds no other due to necessity. (And one who lacks what removes preventing impurity prays with it and no repeat is required because obligation is according to capacity. (And no) repeat (on one who lacks what covers his private parts, even if silk, for if he finds silk, he must pray in it because the obligation of covering is stronger than the prohibition of wearing it in this situation. (Or if it is) grass or mud or cloudy water, he prays inside it with ishara because it covers to some extent. (Then if he finds it) i.e., the cover (even by permission and his quarter is pure, his prayer while naked is not valid) according to the most correct view, like water that is permitted for tayammum, since no obligation of giving it (by the owner) applies to him, and a quarter of a thing stands in place of the whole in some places, among them this, and its three impure quarters do not stand in its place.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This is a section (fasl) from Kitab al-Salah in the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah, dealing with the related conditions and branches of prayer. The passage presents several rulings on how impurity affects the validity of prayer when it is on a thick item like a felt carpet (lubbad), a garment with lining, or a turban. The key principle is that if the item is thick enough to be considered two separate layers, then each layer is treated independently. Therefore, praying on the pure top of a lubbad is valid even if the bottom is impure, according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, considering it as one entity. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as indicated by the preference of two prominent later scholars. Similarly, a garment with pure outer and impure lining is valid if it is not quilted (ghayr mudarab), because the outer and lining are like two separate garments. For a turban or wrap with one impure end, if the impure end is cast aside and does not move with the wearer, prayer is valid; if it moves, it becomes as if carrying impurity, invalidating prayer unless there is no alternative (darurah). The passage also covers cases of necessity: one who cannot find water to remove impurity prays with the impurity and does not repeat; one who cannot find covering for the 'awrah must use even silk if available, because covering obligation outweighs silk prohibition. If one finds only grass, mud, or cloudy water, he prays inside them with gestures (isha'rah) because they provide partial covering. Finally, if a person finds a cover (even by permission) and a quarter of it is pure, he cannot pray naked, because a pure quarter suffices for covering; the three impure quarters are disregarded. The hashya explains that this is analogous to water for tayammum: when water is given as a gift, there is no obligation to accept the gift, but if it is present, tayammum is invalid. Similarly, if a pure quarter cover is available, naked prayer is invalid.

Key Terms
لبد (lubbad): A thick felt or carpet, often made of wool, with a pure upper surface and impure lower surface.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bili of the Hanafi school, which of the following is true regarding prayer on a lubbad (thick felt) whose upper surface is pure and lower surface is impure?
A) The prayer is invalid because the impurity is on the same object.
B) The prayer is valid because the thickness makes it like two separate garments.
C) The prayer is valid only if the impure part is covered.
D) The prayer is invalid according to all Hanafi imams.

Key Takeaway
Thickness of a surface can legally split an object into separate layers; the pure part alone suffices for valid prayer.

Impure Garments and Turbans: When Movement Matters
Rulings on mixed-purity garments and the effect of movement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling for a garment with pure outer and impure lining and state when an impure end of a turban invalidates prayer.

Core Idea
A garment with clean outer and impure lining is valid if not quilted; an impure turban end that moves with the wearer invalidates prayer.

Impurity on a garment does not always invalidate prayer, especially when the impure part is separate from the worshipper's body. This lesson examines two sub-rules: the case of a garment with pure outer and impure lining (if not quilted), and the case of a turban or wrap where one end is impure but cast aside. The key factor is whether the impure part moves with the worshipper's movements.

Guided Path
1
Examine the garment with lining
Read the rule: prayer is valid on a garment whose outer is pure and lining is impure, provided the garment is not quilted (ghayr mudarab). The reason: the outer and lining are like two separate garments on top of each other.
If it is quilted (mudarab), the two layers become one, so the impurity would affect the whole.
2
Analyze the turban case
If one end of a turban is impure and the wearer casts it aside, keeping the pure part on the head, prayer is valid as long as the impure end does not move with the wearer's movement.
Movement means the impure part is effectively carried (حامل لها حكماً), which invalidates prayer.
3
Identify the exception for necessity
If the impure part moves but the person has no other cloth, prayer is valid due to necessity (darurah).
Necessity overrides the general prohibition.
4
Generalize the principle
The underlying principle: an impurity that is not in contact with the worshipper and does not move with him does not affect the prayer. If it moves with him, it is as if he is carrying it.
This is similar to the lubbad case: separation in space or connection matters.

Source Text

Necessity and Covering in Prayer: Impurity, Awrah, and the Quarter Rule
Rulings on necessity and the quarter rule for covering.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for praying with unavoidable impurity, for covering the awrah with silk or grass, and for the quarter rule that prevents naked prayer.

Core Idea
When removal or covering is impossible, prayer is valid without repeating; covering with silk is obligatory if necessary; a quarter pure cover prevents naked prayer.

Sometimes a worshipper cannot remove impurity from his garment or find proper covering for his awrah. This lesson covers the rulings of necessity: praying with impurity when no water is available, using silk or grass for covering, and the important rule that if even a quarter of a cover is pure, one must use it and cannot pray naked.

Guided Path
1
First ruling: inability to remove impurity
The text says: one who cannot find anything to remove preventing impurity prays with it and does not repeat. This is based on the principle that obligation is according to capacity.
No qada required even if the impurity remains.
2
Second ruling: covering the awrah
If one cannot find a cover, but finds silk, he must pray in silk because the obligation of covering outweighs the prohibition of wearing silk. If only grass, mud, or cloudy water is available, he prays inside them with gestures (isharah) because they provide partial covering.
The priority: covering obligation > prohibition of silk.
3
Third ruling: the quarter rule
If a person finds a cover (even by permission) and a quarter of it is pure, he cannot pray naked. A quarter stands in place of the whole; the three impure quarters are disregarded.
This is analogous to water for tayammum: if pure water is available in any amount, tayammum is invalid.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The initial takbir (Allahu Akbar) that commences the prayer, making what was previously permissible (like eating, talking) forbidden.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is true according to the text?
A) If a person finds a cover that is half pure and half impure, he must pray naked.
B) If a quarter of a cover is pure, the person must use it and cannot pray naked.
C) If a cover is impure entirely, the person should pray naked.
D) The quarter rule does not apply; any pure part suffices regardless of size.

Key Takeaway
Necessity permits prayer with impurity and without ideal covering, but if even a quarter pure cover exists, one must use it and cannot pray naked.

8 min
Necessity Permits Prayer with Impurity
Commentary on rulings for one lacking means to purify or cover

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for one who cannot remove impurity or find a pure cover, and identify when necessity overrides normal prohibitions.

Core Idea
Necessity overrides prohibition: one prays with impurity if no means to remove it.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on prayer when one is unable to remove impurity or find a proper covering. The passage from Al-Tahtawi's Hashiya clarifies that necessity can relax certain obligations, such as using impure cloth or even silk, and that one must still pray with the best possible posture. Understanding these rulings prevents unnecessary repetition of prayers and clarifies the hierarchy of obligations under constraint.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act in question is performing salah while carrying an impurity on one's body or clothing. Normally, this invalidates the prayer.
Default: carrying impurity (even if the impure part moves) is not permissible.
2
State the exception for necessity
When one has no alternative cloth or means to remove the impurity, the prayer becomes valid and does not require repetition. The basis is 'obligation according to capacity'.
Key principle: التكليف بحسب الوسع (obligation according to capacity).
3
Analyze the case of lacking cover
If one lacks any covering for the 'awrah, even silk, grass, mud, or turbid water can be used as a cover. Using silk is required because the obligation of covering outweighs the prohibition of silk for men.
Silk is normally haram for men, but necessity makes it wajib to use.
4
Compare praying in impure garment vs naked
When one has only a completely impure garment, it is better to pray in it (with bowing and prostration) than to pray naked with gestures, because it allows the full ritual posture.
Preference: covering even with impurity is superior to exposing the 'awrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطرف النجس بحركته لا تجوز صلاته لأنه حامل لها حكما إلا إذا لم يجد غيره للضرورة وفاقد ما يزيل به النجاسة المانعة يصلي معها ولا إعادة عليه لأن التكليف بحسب الوسع ولا إعادة على فاقد ما يستر عورته ولو حريراً فإنه إن وجد الحرير لزمه الصلاة فيه لأن فرض الستر أقوى من منع لبسه في هذه الحالة أو كان حشيشاً أو طيناً أو ماء كدراً يصلي داخله بالإيماء لأنه ساتر في الجملة فإن وجده أي الساتر ولو بالإباحة والحال أن ربعه طاهر لا تصح صلاته عارياً على الأصح كالماء الذي أبيح للمتيمم إذ لا يلحقه المانية وربع الشيء يقوم مقام كله في مواضع منها هذا ولم تقم ثلاثة أرباعه النجسة مقام صح وهو دون كله للزوم الستر وسقوط حكم النجاسة بطهارة الربع وخير إن ظهر أقل من ربعه والصلاة فيه أفضل للستر وإتيانه بالركوع والسجود وإن صلى عرياناً بالإيماء قاعداً الأول أو قائماً جاز وهو دونهما في الفضل لأن من ابتلي ببليتين يختار أهونهما وإن تساوتا تخير وصلاته في ثوب نجس الكل أحب من صلاته عرياناً لما قلنا. تنبيه: قال في الدراية: لو ستر عورته بجلد ميتة غير مدبوغ وصلى معه لا تجوز بخلاف الثوب المتنجس لأن نجاسة الجلد أغلظ بدليل أنها لا تزول بالغسل ثلاثاً بخلاف نجاسة الثوب اهـ قلت فيه نظر لأنه يظهر بما هو أهون من غسله كتشميسه أو جفافه بالهواء ولو وجد ما يستر بعض العورة وجب يعني لزوم استعماله أي الاستتار به ويستر القبل والدبر إذا لم يستر إلا قدرهما فإن لم يستر إلا أحدهما قيل يستر الدبر لأنه أفحش في حالة الركوع والسجود وقيل بستر القبل لأنه يستقبل به القبلة ولأنه لا يستتر بغيره والدبر
The impure part with its movement: his prayer is not permissible because he is carrying it [the impurity] legally, except if he does not find other [cloth] out of necessity. And the one who lacks what to remove [with it] the preventing impurity prays with it and no repetition upon him because obligation is according to capacity. And no repetition upon one who lacks what to cover his nakedness, even if silk, for if he finds silk, praying in it is incumbent upon him because the obligation of covering is stronger than the prohibition of wearing it in this situation. Or if it is grass or mud or turbid water, he prays inside it with gestures because it is covering in some respect. For if he finds that cover, even by permission, and the condition is that a quarter of it is pure, his prayer naked is not valid according to the correct view, like the water that is permissible for the one performing tayammum, since no obligation of gratitude attaches to it. And a quarter of a thing stands in place of the whole in some places including this, and three quarters of it impure did not stand in place. It is valid but inferior to the whole due to the necessity of covering and the removal of the ruling of impurity by the purification of a quarter. And he is given a choice if less than a quarter is pure: praying in it is better for covering and performing bowing and prostrating, and if he prays naked with gestures sitting it is first, or standing it is permissible, and it is inferior to them in virtue because one afflicted with two afflictions chooses the lighter of them. If they are equal, he chooses. And his prayer in a completely impure garment is more beloved than his prayer naked due to what we said. Note: Al-Diraya said: If he covers his nakedness with the skin of a carcass not tanned and prays in it, it is not permissible, unlike an impure garment, because the impurity of skin is heavier, as it does not go away by washing three times, unlike the impurity of a garment. I say: This is debatable because it can be removed by something easier than washing, like drying in the sun or air. And if he finds something that covers part of the nakedness, it is obligatory to use it for covering, and he covers the front and rear if it covers only that much; if it covers only one, it is said that he covers the rear because it is more obscene in the state of bowing and prostrating, and it is said to cover the front because he faces the qiblah with it and because it is not covered by anything else.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) on the rulings of salah when one is unable to remove impurity or find a proper cover. The hashiya author, Al-Tahtawi, comments on the matn of Maraqi al-Falah. The first ruling states that moving a part of the body that is impure renders prayer invalid because one is legally carrying the impurity, unless no other cloth is available (necessity). Then the ruling for one lacking water to remove impurity: he prays with the impurity and does not repeat, as obligation is according to capacity. Similarly, one lacking a cover must use even silk if found, because covering is stronger than the prohibition of silk in this case. If only grass, mud, or turbid water is available, he prays inside it with gestures. If he finds a cloth with only a quarter pure, he must use it and cannot pray naked. The quarter suffices legally. If less than a quarter is pure, he has a choice: praying in it is better, but praying naked with gestures sitting or standing is allowed but less virtuous. The author then discusses covering with impure items: praying in a completely impure garment is better than naked because it allows bowing and prostrating. A note from Al-Diraya about skin of a carcass is critiqued. Finally, the ruling on finding only a partial cover: he must use it, and if it covers only one area, there is a difference of opinion on whether to cover the front or rear, with the author leaning towards covering the rear as it is more obscene in bowing and prostrating.

Key Terms
حامل للنجاسة حكما (hāmil li-l-najāsah ḥukman): One who carries impurity legally because the impurity moves with the part, even if not directly touching.
فاقد ما يزيل به النجاسة (fāqid mā yuzīl bihi al-najāsah): One who lacks any substance (water, etc.) to remove impurity.
ربع الشيء يقوم مقام كله (rub‘ al-shay’ yaqūmu maqām kullihi): A quarter of a thing stands in place of the whole in certain rulings, such as covering the body or hair removal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a person who lacks any covering for the 'awrah and finds a silk garment?
A) He may not wear silk, so he must pray naked with gestures
B) He must wear the silk because covering is obligatory
C) He may choose between silk and naked, but silk is better
D) He must delay prayer until he finds non-silk cloth

Key Takeaway
In cases of necessity, the obligation to cover the 'awrah overrides the prohibition of impurity and silk, and one prays with the best available means.

Covering with Partially Pure Cloth and the Rear vs Front Dispute
Commentary on rulings for one lacking means to purify or cover

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi 'quarter rule' for covering and explain the internal dispute on covering the front or rear when only partial cover is available.

Core Idea
A quarter of a cloth suffices legally for covering; if less, one has a choice. The rear is preferred over the front due to greater exposure during prostration.

This lesson delves into the nuances of covering when only a partially pure cloth is available. The Hanafi principle that 'a quarter of a thing stands in place of the whole' is central to determining when one must use the cloth versus when one may pray naked. Additionally, the internal Hanafi dispute on whether to cover the front or rear when only one can be covered illustrates how legal reasoning weighs factors such as modesty and direction.

Guided Path
1
State the quarter rule
If a cloth has at least a quarter of its area pure, one must use it for covering. The prayer naked is invalid. This is analogous to water for tayammum: a quarter pure suffices.
Quarter rule: ربع الشيء يقوم مقام كله.
2
Analyze the case of less than a quarter pure
If less than a quarter is pure, the person has a choice: praying in the cloth (better) or praying naked with gestures (permissible but less virtuous).
Choice is based on choosing the lighter of two afflictions.
3
Examine the comparison with carcass skin
Al-Tahtawi criticizes Al-Diraya's claim that skin of a carcass is heavier impurity; he argues it can be purified by sun/air, so the ruling may differ.
This is a critical refinement: the hashiya corrects an earlier view.
4
Address the partial cover dispute
If the cloth only covers either the front or rear, two views exist: cover the rear (more obscene during prostration) or cover the front (faces the qiblah). The text leans towards rear.
Internal Hanafi ikhtilaf; no tarjih given by Tahtawi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
While no explicit tarjih, the reasoning that the rear is more obscene in prostration suggests preference. In practice, covering the rear is recommended.
Mufta bihi: cover both if possible; if not, cover the rear.

Prayer with a Partially Pure Garment: The Quarter Rule and Refinement on Impurity Severity
Commentary on prayer with partial purity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a garment with at least one quarter pure is considered pure for prayer, explain the choice when less than one quarter is pure, and compare the impurity of a garment to that of untanned animal skin.

Core Idea
When a garment is less than one quarter pure, you may choose to pray in it or naked; the impurity of untanned animal skin is more severe than that of a garment.

When a garment is partially impure, the Hanafi school sets a threshold: if at least one quarter of it is pure, the garment is considered pure for prayer. If less than one quarter is pure, the worshipper faces a choice between praying in the garment or praying naked with gestures. This passage from al-Tahtawi's commentary unpacks the reasoning behind this rule and refines it by comparing the impurity of garments with that of untanned animal skin, offering a critical perspective within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is prayer (salah) performed while wearing a garment that is partially impure. The ruling is that the prayer is valid if at least one quarter of the garment is pure. If the pure portion is less than one quarter, the person has a choice: pray in the garment (preferable) or pray naked with gestures.
This ruling is based on the obligation to cover the 'awrah (wajib) and the principle of choosing the lesser harm.
2
Understand the Quarter Condition
The 'quarter' refers to one quarter of the garment's entire fabric area. The reasoning is that covering the 'awrah is obligatory, and the impurity is considered waived if at least one quarter is pure. This is a specific Hanafi position, not shared by all schools.
The quarter measure is a legal convention (taqdir shar'i) to standardise the purity assessment.
3
Recognise the Choice and Its Preference
When the pure portion is less than one quarter, the worshipper may choose to pray in the garment (with bowing and prostration) or pray naked (with gestures, sitting or standing). The preferred option is to pray in the garment because it covers the 'awrah and allows full performance of the prayer. If equal in harm, the worshipper may choose freely.
The choice is only valid if there is no alternative; if a pure garment is available, it must be used.
4
Examine the Refinement: Untanned Animal Skin vs. Impure Garment
The commentary cites al-Diraya: covering the 'awrah with untanned skin of a dead animal invalidates the prayer because its impurity (najasa ghaliza) is more severe than that of a normal impure garment. Al-Tahtawi objects, arguing that the skin's impurity can be removed by methods easier than washing, such as exposing to sunlight or air-drying, so it should not be considered worse.
This is a critical refinement: the commentator re-evaluates the basis of comparison between the two types of impurity.
5
Distinguish the Two Impurities
The impurity of a garment is light (najasa khafifa) and can be removed by washing once. The impurity of untanned animal skin is severe (najasa ghaliza) but can be purified by alternative methods. The commentator argues that the severity is not absolute; thus, covering with such skin may be permissible under necessity.
This refinement shows the dynamic nature of Hanafi fiqh: later scholars may critique earlier rulings based on new understandings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة صح وهو دون كله للزوم الستر وسقوط حكم النجاسة بطهارة الربع وخير إن ظهر أقل من ربعه والصلاة فيه أفضل للستر وإتيانه بالركوع والسجود وإن صلى عرياناً بالإيماء قاعداً الأول، أو قائماً جاز وهو دونهما في الفضل لأنّ من ابتلي ببليتين يختار أهونهما وإن تساوتا تخير وصلاته في ثوب نجس الكل أحب من صلاته عرياناً لما قلنا . تنبيه : قال في الدراية : لو ستر عورته بجلد ميتة غير مدبوغ وصلى معه لا تجوز بخلاف الثوب المتنجس لأن نجاسة الجلد أغلظ بدليل أنها لا تزول بالغسل ثلاثاً بخلاف نجاسة الثوب اهـ قلت فيه نظر لأنه يظهر بما هو أهون من غسله كتشميسه أو جفافه بالهواء ولو وجد ما يستر بعض العورة وجب يعني لزوم استعماله أي الاستتار به ويستر القبل والدبر إذا لم يستر إلا قدرهما فإن لم يستر إلا أحدهما قيل يستر الدبر لأنه أفحش في حالة الركوع والسجود وقيل بستر القبل لأنه يستقبل به القبلة ولأنه لا يستتر بغيره والدبر قاعداً . لما منها هذا ومنها حلق ربع الرأس، أو تقصيره في الإحلال من الحرام، والجناية عليه. قوله : ولم تقم الخ جواب عن سؤال حاصله لماذا اعتبرتم الربع الطاهر ، وقلتم بطهارة كله حكماً، ولم تعتبروا ثلاثة أرباعه النجسة، وتحكموا بنجاسة جميعه، والنظر اعتبار الأكثر فأجاب عنه بأن الستر لازم وحكم النجاسة ساقط شرعاً بطهارة الربع للزوم الستر فلذا اعتبر الربع. قوله: وخير إن طهر أقل من ربعه حاصله أنه بالخيار بين أن يصلي فيه، وهو الأفضل أن يصلي عرياناً وبين يومي بالركوع والسجود وهو يليه في الفضل لما فيه من ستر العورة المغلظة أو قائماً عرياناً بركوع وسجود وهو دونهما في الفضل، أو مومياً، وهذا دونهما، وظاهر الهداية منعه فإنه قال في الذي لا يجد ثوباً، فإن صلى قائماً أجزاء لأن في القعود ستر العورة الغليظة، وفي القيام أداء هذه الأركان فيميل إلى أيهما شاء. قال الزيلعي، ولو كان الإيماء جائزاً حالة القيام استقام الكلام اه قاله السيد قوله : لأن من ابتلي ببليتين كالصلاة في ثوب نجس بركوع وسجود، وصلاته عرياناً قاعداً يومي قوله : يختار أهونهما كما لو كانت المرأة، إذا صلت قائمة ينكشف ربع عضو منها وإن صلت جالسة إستترت تصلي جالسة لأن ترك القيام أهون كذا في الشرح، وكذا يصلي في الثوب النجس في الصورة السابقة. قوله: وان تساوتا تخير كما في مسألة المتن، فإنه لو استتر فانه فرض الطهارة، ولو صلى عرياناً فإنه فرض الستر، وكل منهما من الشروط فيخير قوله: لما قلنا من إتيانه بالركوع والسجود، وستر العورة. قوله : قلت فيه نظر إلخ في النظر نظر لأن الغسل أهون من التشميس، ووضعه في الهواء لأنه ليس المراد مطلق تشميس، ووضع بل هما مقيدان بإزالة النتن، والفساد وقد يستغرق ذلك اليوم الكامل والأكثر بخلاف الغسل، فتأمل قوله : لأنه أفحش قال في التعليل يفيد أنه لو صلى بالإيماء تعين ستر القبل، ثم بعده الفخذ، ثم بطن المرأة وظهرها، ثم يستتر بالإليتين وفيه تأمل لأنه يستتر بالفخذين ووضع اليدين فوقهما وندب صلاة العاري جالساً بالإيماء ماذا رجليه نحو القبلة لما فيه من الستر فإن صلى العاري قائماً بالإيماء أو قائماً آتياً بالركوع والسجود صح لإتيانه بالأركان فيميل إلى أيهما شاء، والأفضل الأول، ولو صلى عارياً ناسياً ساتراً اختلف في صحتها
The book of prayer. It is valid and below all [covering] necessitates concealing and the ruling of impurity is removed by the purification of one quarter. And he has a choice if less than one quarter is pure. Praying in it is better for covering and performing bowing and prostration. And if he prays naked with gestures sitting, first, or standing, it is permissible, and it is below them in merit because one afflicted with two trials chooses the lesser of them; and if they are equal, he chooses. And his prayer in a garment entirely impure is more beloved than his prayer naked, for what we said. A note: He said in al-Diraya: If he covers his awrah with the skin of a dead animal not tanned and prays with it, it is not valid, unlike the impure garment because the impurity of the skin is worse, evidenced by the fact that it is not removed by washing three times, unlike the impurity of the garment. End. I say there is consideration in it because it becomes apparent with what is easier than washing it, like exposing it to the sun or drying it in the air. And if he finds what covers part of the awrah, it is obligatory, meaning necessary, to use it, i.e., to cover with it, and he covers the front and back if it covers only that much. If it covers only one of them, it is said he covers the back because it is more obscene in the state of bowing and prostration, and it is said he covers the front because he faces the qibla with it and because it is not covered otherwise, and the back is covered by sitting. [Includes commentary on why one quarter is considered, the choice when less than one quarter, the preference, the discussion of the two afflictions, the equality and choice, the note about washing vs. sun, and the ruling on which part to cover first. Then: It is recommended for the naked person to pray sitting with gestures stretching his legs towards the qibla due to the covering it entails. If the naked person prays standing with gestures or standing performing bowing and prostration, it is valid due to performing the pillars, so he tends to whichever he wishes, and the first is better. And if he prays naked forgetfully having a cover, there is disagreement on its validity.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (hashiya) on the ruling of prayer for one who lacks a pure or sufficient garment. The commentator explains the legal options: if a garment is less than one quarter pure, the person has a choice between praying in it (better) or praying naked with gestures. The principle is choosing the lesser harm between impurity and nudity. A note clarifies that covering with untanned animal skin is invalid due to its severe impurity, unlike a mere impure cloth. When only partial covering is available, covering the private parts is obligatory, and the order of priority (back or front) is discussed. The commentary also details the preferred posture for naked prayer (sitting with legs stretched towards qibla) and the validity of standing prayer. The Hanafi position is that covering the 'awrah is necessary, and when impossible, the person chooses the option that minimizes infraction.

Key Terms
العورة (al-awrah): The parts of the body that must be covered in prayer; for a man, between navel and knees.
الربع (al-rubu): One quarter of the garment; used as the minimum pure portion for the garment to be considered pure for prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person has a garment that is less than one quarter pure, what is the preferred option for prayer?
A) Pray naked standing with gestures
B) Pray in the garment with bowing and prostration
C) Pray naked sitting with gestures
D) Delay the prayer until a pure garment is found

Key Takeaway
When a garment is less than one quarter pure, the Hanafi school allows a choice; praying in the garment is preferred over nudity, but if untanned animal skin is available, its impurity may be considered less severe under some conditions.

The Male Awrah: Definition, Limits, and Evidentiary Basis
Definition of male awrah with evidence and practical consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the male awrah (navel to knee inclusive), cite the hadith evidence, and distinguish the degrees of reproach for different body parts.

Core Idea
The male awrah is from navel to knee inclusive, and the knee is explicitly part of it based on the hadith.

This passage defines the male awrah (عورة) in the Hanafi school and its boundaries. It establishes that the awrah extends from the navel to the end of the knee, including the knee itself, supported by a direct hadith. The commentary also details the varying degrees of strictness in covering different segments of the awrah, from the knee (light) to the private parts (severe), and addresses exceptions for young children.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition of awrah
Locate the phrase 'ما افترض ستره' (what covering is obligatory). The awrah is defined linguistically and legally; the legal definition is given by the Lawgiver.
Awrah linguistically means deficiency or ugliness; legally it means what must be covered.
2
Determine the boundaries of the male awrah
Find the statement 'عورة الرجل ما بين سرته إلى ركبته' and note the preposition 'إلى' (to). The author explains that 'إلى' for limit includes the knee as a precaution, and the second hadith ('الركبة من العورة') makes it explicit.
The preposition 'إلى' in Hanafi usul can include or exclude the limit; here precaution and direct evidence ensure inclusion.
3
Examine the evidence for the knee's inclusion
The hadith 'الركبة من العورة' is cited. Confirm that this is a dalil naqli (textual evidence) used to establish the ruling.
This hadith is the primary proof for the Hanafi position that the knee is part of the awrah.
4
Analyze the gradations in covering severity
The passage discusses different degrees of reproach for exposure: knee (gentle reproach), thigh (harsh reproach), private parts (order to cover and discipline), and area between navel and pubis (gentle reproach, no discipline due to ijtihad).
These gradations reflect the relative strength of evidence and customary practice.
5
Note the exception for young children
The text states that a very small child has no awrah, citing the Prophet's (ﷺ) interaction with his grandsons.
This exception is based on explicit practice and is limited to very young children.

السراج الصغير جداً لا تكون له عورة، ولا بأس بالنظر إليها، ومسها لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يقبل ذكري الحسن والحسين في صغرهما، وكان يأخذ أحدهما من ذكره، ويجره والصبي يضحك كذا في الفتاوى اهـ وفي احتياطاً ولأن الغاية تدخل في المغيا بالي كما هو في آية الوضوء وهذا بقطع النظر عما يؤخذ من الحديث الثاني، وإلا فهو صريح في دخولها .
And the awrah of a man, free or slave, is what is between the navel and the end of the knee in the apparent narration. It is called awrah because of the ugliness of its appearance and the lowering of gazes from it linguistically, and in Islamic law, it is what covering is obligatory. The Lawgiver defined it by his saying: 'The awrah of a man is what is between his navel to his knee,' and by his statement, peace be upon him: 'The knee is part of the awrah.' And it adds to him, i.e., to the man, the knee, then the rest is equal as in Sakb al-Anhar and others. His saying: 'And it is said he covers the front,' he said in al-Nahr: and the apparent is that the disagreement is about preference. His saying: 'And in it is contemplation,' i.e., in the second reasoning. His saying: 'Because he covers himself with the thighs,' etc., it can be said the meaning of 'it is not covered otherwise' is that it is not covered without difficulty. And covering with the thighs involves hardship, and covering with the hands negates another act of worship, which is placing them during the ruling of standing under the navel, so contemplate. His saying: 'Stretching his legs towards the qibla,' this is what is in al-Dhakhira, and in Munyat al-Musalli he sits as he sits in prayer during tashahhud, and upon it there is difference for man and woman. He said in al-Bahr: What is apparent is its preference and that it is better because it achieves greater covering not achieved by the second posture, along with its being free from doing what is not preferable, which is stretching legs towards qibla without need. And the disagreement is about preference. His saying: 'And if the naked prays...' remains a fourth matter mentioned in al-Bahr and al-Nahr from Multaqa al-Bihar, which is prayer sitting with bowing and prostration. His saying: 'What is between the navel,' i.e., what is parallel to that from all sides, and it is said its beginning is from the navel, and it is said from the hairline. And the word 'man' indicates that a young boy is not like that. He said in al-Siraj: A very small child has no awrah, and there is no harm in looking at it or touching it, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, used to kiss the private parts of al-Hasan and al-Husayn when they were small, and would take one by his penis and drag him while the boy laughed, as in al-Fatawa. And in al-Bahr from al-Zahiriyya: The ruling of awrah regarding the knee is lighter than regarding the thigh. Its fruit is that if he sees another with his knee uncovered, he reproaches gently and does not contend if he insists; but if he sees him with thigh uncovered, he reproaches harshly and does not harm if he insists; and if he sees his private part uncovered, he orders him to cover it and disciplines him if he insists; and if he sees what is between the navel and the pubic area uncovered, he reproaches gently and contends if he insists but does not discipline him, because it is a matter of ijtihad due to al-Fadli's statement that it is not awrah due to workers' custom of exposing it, even if it is weak. His saying: 'Due to the ugliness of its appearance,' it is from al-awr, which is deficiency, ugliness, and flaw. His saying: 'To his knees,' the face of deduction from it is that the word 'to' indicates a limit, so the knee is the limit, and the limit may be included or excluded, and the place is of precaution, so we ruled its inclusion out of precaution, and because the limit is included in the limited, as in the verse of wudu', and this apart from what is taken from the second hadith, otherwise it is explicit in its inclusion.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling on the male awrah in the Hanafi school. The commentator establishes the definition from the apparent narration: from the navel to the end of the knee, explicitly including the knee via the hadith 'the knee is part of the awrah.' The commentary then discusses the difference in severity of exposure: the knee is lighter than the thigh, and the area between navel and pubic region is subject to ijtihad. Practical consequences for admonition are given: gentle for knee, harsh for thigh, and requiring discipline for private parts. The commentary also clarifies that the awrah of a very young child is not established, citing a hadith. The Hanafi position is that covering the awrah is obligatory, and the knee is included as a precaution and based on the hadith.

Key Terms
العورة (al-awrah): The area of the body that must be covered in and out of prayer; for a man, from navel to knee including the knee.
الركبة (al-rukbah): The knee; is part of the awrah in Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Hanafi school defines the male awrah as from the navel to the end of the knee, inclusive, based on explicit hadith and precautionary principle.

'Awrah of the Free Woman's Forearm in Salah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on forearm 'awrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on the forearm of a free woman in salah and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The forearm is 'awrah in salah, though Abu Hanifa differed; the later school's tarjih made it the mufta bihi.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi disagreement: whether a free woman's forearm must be covered during salah. The position of the Sahibayn and later authorities (Zahir al-Riwayah) classifies it as 'awrah, while Abu Hanifa held it is not due to necessity of service. Understanding how the school resolved this illustrates the operation of tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
Determine that the ruling concerns the condition of covering 'awrah in salah, which is a shart (condition) for validity.
Covering 'awrah is fard; exposing a quarter of a limb that is 'awrah invalidates salah.
2
Locate the disputed body part
The forearm (dhirac) of a free woman is the point of dispute. Identify whether it is considered 'awrah or not.
Face and hands are agreed exceptions; the forearm is between the elbow and wrist.
3
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa: the forearm is not 'awrah. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and the later authorities (Zahir al-Riwayah): it is 'awrah.
The matn says 'wa dhirac al-hurrah 'awrah fi zahir al-riwaya wa hiya al-asahh wa 'an Abi Hanifa laysa bi 'awrah'.
4
Analyse the evidence for each side
Abu Hanifa reasoned by analogy with the face and hands, as the forearm is also needed for service. The Sahibayn relied on general proofs that whatever is not face or hands is 'awrah.
The commentary mentions that some later scholars distinguished between prayer and outside prayer, saying it is 'awrah in prayer but not outside.
5
Determine the tarjih (preferred view)
The mufta bihi is that the forearm is 'awrah, based on the soundness of Zahir al-Riwayah and the adoption of later Hanafi authorities like al-Marghinani.
The fatwa is that uncovering a quarter of the forearm invalidates salah. Some earlier opinions allowed it with karahah, but the relied-upon view is impermissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
(الأمة) القنة وأم الولد المدبرة والمكاتبة، والمستسعاة عند أبي حنيفة لوجود الرق (البطن والظهر) لأن لهما مزية فصدرها وثديها ليسا من العورة للحرج (وجميع بدن الحرة عورة إلا وجهها وكفيها باطنهما وظاهرهما في الأصح ، وهو المختار وذراع الحرة عورة في ظاهر الرواية وهي الأصح وعن أبي حنيفة ليس بعورة (و) إلا (قدميها) في أصح الروايتين باطنهما وظاهرهما لعموم الضرورة ليسا من العورة فشعر الحرة حتى المسترسل عورة في الأصح وعليه الفتوى فكشف ربعه يمنع صحة الصلاة، ولا يحل النظر إليه مقطوعاً منها في الأصح

كذلك
قوله: (والمستسعاة) يعني معتقة البعض، وأما المرهونة إذا أعتقها الراهن، هو معسر فإنها حرة إتفاقاً . قوله : (عند أبي حنيفة وقالا : هي حرة مديونة قوله: (البطن، والظهر) وأما الجنب فإنه تبع للبطن كذا في القنية والأوجه أن ما يلي البطن تبع له كما في البحر يعني، وما يلي الظهر تبع له كما في تحفة الأخيار والخنثى المشكل الرقيق كالأمة والحر كالحرة. قوله: ( لأن لهما مزية) أي في الاشتهاء، والمراد أن لهما دخل في الشهوة، وفيه أن الثديين أعظم دخلاً من هذه الحيثية، والأولى في الاستدلال ما في الشرح أن عمر كان يضرب الإماء أن تقنعن، ويقول: ألق عنك الخمار يا دفار، وكانت جواريه تخدمن الضيفان كاشفات الرؤوس مضطربات الثديين. قال بعض الفضلاء بحثاً وظاهر ذلك أنه يكره التقنع للأمة، لكن بالنسبة لزمن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه، أما في زماننا فينبغي أن يجب التقنع لا سيما في الإماء البيض لغلبة الفسق فيه قوله : (للحرج من حيث أنها تباع وتشرى، وتخرج لحاجة مولاها في ثياب مهنتها عادة، فاعتبر حالها بذوات المحارم في حق جميع الرجال. قوله : (وجميع بدن الحرة) أي جسدها قوله : (إلا) وجهها ومنع الشابة من كشفه لخوف الفتنة لا لأنه عورة. قوله: (وهو المختار) وإن كان خلاف ظاهر الرواية قوله : (وعن أبي حنيفة ليس بعورة) واختاره في الاختيار للحاجة للكشف للخدمة كما في البحر . قال الكمال: وصحح بعضهم أنه عورة في الصلاة لا خارجها ولا تلازم بين كونه ليس بعورة، وجواز النظر إليه لأن حل النظر منوط بعدم خشبة الشهوة مع إنتفاء العورة ولذا حرم النظر إلى وجهها ووجه الأمرد إذا شك في الشهوة ولا عورة اهـ وفي الزاهدي عن الشيخين أن الذراع لا يمنع جواز الصلاة لكن يكره كشفه ككشف القدم قهستاني قوله : (باطنهما، وظاهرهما) أي في الصلاة، وخارجها، وقال الأقطع في شرحه الصحيح أنهما عورة لظاهر الخبر، وفي الاختيار الصحيح أن القدم ليست بعورة في الصلاة وهي عورة خارجها. قال في الشرح، والتحقيق أن القدم ليست بعورة في الصلاة كما ذكرنا قوله : (في (الأصح احترز عن رواية المنتفى أنه ليس بعورة، وبه قال عبد الله البلخي قال في النهر والحاصل أن له اعتبارين فهو من البدن في حق العورة، وليس منه في حق الغسل اهـ يعني إذا كان مضفوراً قوله ولا يحل النظر إليه مقطوعاً منها في الأصح) وقيل : يحل كما يحل النظر إلى ريقها، ودمها. كشعر عانته، وذكره المقطوع
The Book of Salah. (The enslaved woman) includes the absolute slave, umm walad, mudabbara, mukataba, and the one who is mukatab seeking freedom by working at Abu Hanifa due to the presence of slavery. (The belly and back) because they have a special quality; her chest and breasts are not part of the 'awrah due to hardship. (And all of the free woman's body is 'awrah except her face and her hands, both palms and their outsides in the soundest opinion, and it is the chosen view. And the forearm of a free woman is 'awrah in the apparent riwaya and it is the soundest, and from Abu Hanifa it is not 'awrah. (And) except (her feet) in the soundest of the two riwayas, both their soles and uppers, due to general necessity, they are not 'awrah. So the hair of a free woman, even the hanging part, is 'awrah in the soundest opinion and upon it is the fatwa, so uncovering a quarter of it prevents the validity of prayer, and it is not permissible to look at it when cut from her in the soundest opinion. It is likewise. His saying: (al-mustas'at) means the one who is partially freed. As for the mortgaged one, if the mortgagor frees her and he is insolvent, then she is free by agreement. His saying: (according to Abu Hanifa and they said: she is free but indebted) His saying: (the belly and back) and as for the side, it follows the belly. Likewise in al-Quniya, and the proper view is that what is adjacent to the belly follows it as in al-Bahr, meaning, and what is adjacent to the back follows it as in Tuhfat al-Akhyar. And the ambiguous hermaphrodite: if slave, like an enslaved woman; if free, like a free woman. His saying: (because they have a special quality) i.e. in desire, and the intended meaning is that they have an effect in arousing desire, and in it that the breasts have a greater effect from this perspective, and the better in evidence is what is in the Sharh that Umar used to strike the slave women to cover (their heads), saying: 'Throw off the headcover, O Dafar,' and his female servants used to serve guests with heads uncovered and breasts swaying. Some virtuous scholars said as research: the apparent is that covering the head is disliked for the enslaved woman, but that is relative to the time of Umar may Allah be pleased with him. As for our time, it is incumbent to cover, especially for white slave women due to widespread immorality. His saying: (due to hardship because she is bought and sold, and goes out for her master's needs in clothes of her usual work, so her case is considered like that of mahram women in relation to all men. His saying: (and all the body of the free woman) i.e. her body. His saying: (except) her face, and preventing a young woman from uncovering it due to fear of temptation, not because it is 'awrah. His saying: (and it is the chosen) even if it contradicts the apparent riwaya. His saying: (and from Abu Hanifa it is not 'awrah) and he chose it in al-Ikhtiyar due to the need for uncovering for service as in al-Bahr. Al-Kamal said: Some scholars corrected that it is 'awrah in prayer not outside it, and there is no correlation between it not being 'awrah and permissibility of looking at it, because permissibility of looking is conditional upon absence of fear of desire along with absence of 'awrah, so looking at her face and the face of a beardless youth is prohibited when there is doubt about desire, and there is no 'awrah. And in al-Zahidi from the two shaykhs that the forearm does not prevent the validity of prayer, but uncovering it is disliked like uncovering the foot (Qahistani). His saying: (both their palms and their outsides) i.e. in prayer and outside it. And al-Aqta' said in his Sharh that the correct opinion is that they are 'awrah due to the apparent hadith, and in al-Ikhtiyar as-sahih that the foot is not 'awrah in prayer and is 'awrah outside it. He said in the Sharh, and the investigation is that the foot is not 'awrah in prayer as we mentioned. His saying: (in (the soundest) he is cautious against the riwaya of al-Muntafa that it is not 'awrah, and Abdullah al-Balkhi said so. He said in an-Nahr: and the conclusion is that it has two considerations: it is from the body with respect to 'awrah, and not from it with respect to ghusl (meaning if it is plaited). His saying: (and it is not permissible to look at it when cut from her in the soundest opinion) and it is said: it is permissible just as it is permissible to look at her saliva and her blood. Like hair of her pubic area, and his (the man's) cut penis.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah, critically refining the rulings on 'awrah for enslaved and free women. The author begins by defining the types of enslaved women (amah, umm walad, mudabbara, mukataba, mustas'at) and states the position of Abu Hanifa that they all have the status of slaves regarding 'awrah. The belly and back are 'awrah because they incite desire, but the chest and breasts are not 'awrah due to hardship. The author supports this with a hadith of Umar who beat slave women for covering their heads. However, some later scholars note that in times of corruption, even enslaved women should cover. For free women, the entire body is 'awrah except the face and hands (palms and backs). The forearm is 'awrah according to the apparent riwaya, but Abu Hanifa differed, considering it not 'awrah. The feet are not 'awrah in the soundest riwaya due to necessity. The hair of a free woman is 'awrah, even the long hanging part, and uncovering a quarter of it invalidates prayer. Looking at cut hair is impermissible in the soundest view. The passage then comments on each part with references to various authorities and discusses the intra-Hanafi disagreements. The mufta bihi position is that the forearm is 'awrah in prayer, the feet are not, and hair is 'awrah. The author also discusses the distinction between 'awrah for prayer and for looking.

Key Terms
عورة (‘awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered during salah and in front of non-mahram.
ذراع (dhirac): Forearm, from elbow to wrist.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core compilations of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered the most authoritative transmission of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is not 'awrah, so it may be uncovered.
B) It is 'awrah, and uncovering a quarter of it invalidates salah.
C) It is 'awrah only outside salah, but in salah it is not.
D) It is makruh to uncover but salah remains valid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi holds that a free woman's forearm is 'awrah in salah, a decision reached through tarjih of the Sahibayn's view over Abu Hanifa's.

'Awrah of the Enslaved Woman in Salah
Ruling on 'awrah of enslaved women with a temporal refinement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the 'awrah of an enslaved woman in the Hanafi school and explain the basis for the distinction from a free woman.

Core Idea
An enslaved woman's 'awrah is only her belly and back, not her chest or breasts, due to hardship and customary work.

This lesson addresses the ruling on the 'awrah of enslaved women in salah, which is narrower than that of free women. The Hanafi school exempts the chest and breasts from the 'awrah due to the necessity of movement and work. However, the commentary from al-Tahtawi notes that in times of moral decay, even enslaved women should cover their heads. Understanding this distinction illuminates how the school balances textual evidence with custom and need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of enslaved women
The passage lists qinn (absolute slave), umm walad (mother of the master's child), mudabbara (promised freedom upon master's death), mukataba (who has a contract to buy freedom), and mustas'at (working for freedom). All are considered enslaved for 'awrah purposes.
Some like al-mustas'at are considered enslaved only according to Abu Hanifa; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ.
2
State the 'awrah parts for an enslaved woman
Only the belly (batn) and back (zahr) are 'awrah. The chest (sadr) and breasts (thady) are not 'awrah due to hardship (haraj).
The side follows the belly; the lower back follows the back.
3
Understand the basis: hardship (haraj)
Enslaved women are bought, sold, and perform manual labour, so requiring full coverage would cause hardship. They are likened to mahram women.
The passage cites the practice of Umar's female servants serving guests with uncovered heads and breasts.
4
Note the temporal refinement
Some later scholars (fudala') noted that in times of widespread immorality, even enslaved women should cover their heads. This is not a change in the ruling per se, but a precautionary measure.
The text says 'amma fi zamanina fayajibu al-taqannu' la siyma fi al-imma' al-bid.
5
Apply the ruling to prayer
In salah, an enslaved woman must cover her belly and back; if she uncovers more than a quarter of these, her prayer is invalid. The chest and breasts may be uncovered.
The same rule of a quarter applies to the exposed 'awrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
(الأمة) القنة وأم الولد المدبرة والمكاتبة، والمستسعاة عند أبي حنيفة لوجود الرق (البطن والظهر) لأن لهما مزية فصدرها وثديها ليسا من العورة للحرج (وجميع بدن الحرة عورة إلا وجهها وكفيها باطنهما وظاهرهما في الأصح ، وهو المختار وذراع الحرة عورة في ظاهر الرواية وهي الأصح وعن أبي حنيفة ليس بعورة (و) إلا (قدميها) في أصح الروايتين باطنهما وظاهرهما لعموم الضرورة ليسا من العورة فشعر الحرة حتى المسترسل عورة في الأصح وعليه الفتوى فكشف ربعه يمنع صحة الصلاة، ولا يحل النظر إليه مقطوعاً منها في الأصح
وهو
كذلك
قوله: (والمستسعاة) يعني معتقة البعض، وأما المرهونة إذا أعتقها الراهن، هو معسر فإنها حرة إتفاقاً . قوله : (عند أبي حنيفة وقالا : هي حرة مديونة قوله: (البطن، والظهر) وأما الجنب فإنه تبع للبطن كذا في القنية والأوجه أن ما يلي البطن تبع له كما في البحر يعني، وما يلي الظهر تبع له كما في تحفة الأخيار والخنثى المشكل الرقيق كالأمة والحر كالحرة. قوله: ( لأن لهما مزية) أي في الاشتهاء، والمراد أن لهما دخل في الشهوة، وفيه أن الثديين أعظم دخلاً من هذه الحيثية، والأولى في الاستدلال ما في الشرح أن عمر كان يضرب الإماء أن تقنعن، ويقول: ألق عنك الخمار يا دفار، وكانت جواريه تخدمن الضيفان كاشفات الرؤوس مضطربات الثديين. قال بعض الفضلاء بحثاً وظاهر ذلك أنه يكره التقنع للأمة، لكن بالنسبة لزمن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه، أما في زماننا فينبغي أن يجب التقنع لا سيما في الإماء البيض لغلبة الفسق فيه قوله : (للحرج من حيث أنها تباع وتشرى، وتخرج لحاجة مولاها في ثياب مهنتها عادة، فاعتبر حالها بذوات المحارم في حق جميع الرجال. قوله : (وجميع بدن الحرة) أي جسدها قوله : (إلا) وجهها ومنع الشابة من كشفه لخوف الفتنة لا لأنه عورة. قوله: (وهو المختار) وإن كان خلاف ظاهر الرواية قوله : (وعن أبي حنيفة ليس بعورة) واختاره في الاختيار للحاجة للكشف للخدمة كما في البحر . قال الكمال: وصحح بعضهم أنه عورة في الصلاة لا خارجها ولا تلازم بين كونه ليس بعورة، وجواز النظر إليه لأن حل النظر منوط بعدم خشبة الشهوة مع إنتفاء العورة ولذا حرم النظر إلى وجهها ووجه الأمرد إذا شك في الشهوة ولا عورة اهـ وفي الزاهدي عن الشيخين أن الذراع لا يمنع جواز الصلاة لكن يكره كشفه ككشف القدم قهستاني قوله : (باطنهما، وظاهرهما) أي في الصلاة، وخارجها، وقال الأقطع في شرحه الصحيح أنهما عورة لظاهر الخبر، وفي الاختيار الصحيح أن القدم ليست بعورة في الصلاة وهي عورة خارجها. قال في الشرح، والتحقيق أن القدم ليست بعورة في الصلاة كما ذكرنا قوله : (في (الأصح احترز عن رواية المنتفى أنه ليس بعورة، وبه قال عبد الله البلخي قال في النهر والحاصل أن له اعتبارين فهو من البدن في حق العورة، وليس منه في حق الغسل اهـ يعني إذا كان مضفوراً قوله ولا يحل النظر إليه مقطوعاً منها في الأصح) وقيل : يحل كما يحل النظر إلى ريقها، ودمها. كشعر عانته، وذكره المقطوع

Woman's Voice and Exposure of 'Awrah in Prayer
Commentary on 'awrah rulings for prayer including voice and exposure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman's voice in prayer and apply the threshold for exposure invalidating prayer.

Core Idea
A woman's voice is 'awrah only when modulated; exposure of a quarter of a limb for a pillar's duration invalidates prayer.

This lesson clarifies two connected 'awrah rulings in prayer: whether a woman's voice must be concealed and what amount of physical exposure breaks the prayer. The text from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah presents the relied-upon Hanafi position, including important intra-madhhab differences and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings covered
The passage addresses (1) the woman's voice as 'awrah and (2) the minimum exposure of 'awrah that invalidates prayer. Separate these two issues.
The voice ruling applies outside prayer as well; the exposure ruling is specific to prayer.
2
Analyze the voice ruling
Determine when a woman's voice is considered 'awrah. Note the distinction between normal speech and modulated (lengthened, softened) speech. Identify the proof (dalil) cited from earlier Hanafi works.
The relied-upon view is that modulated voice is 'awrah; normal speech is not.
3
Examine the exposure threshold
Find the threshold for exposure that invalidates prayer: a quarter of a limb lasting the duration of a pillar (three tasbihat). Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf considers a majority, and the mufta bihi is the quarter threshold due to caution.
This applies only when the exposure is unintentional; intentional exposure invalidates immediately.
4
Understand the conditions
The exposure must be without one's own action, with a covering present, and the scattered exposure adds up if it reaches a quarter of the smallest uncovered limb.
The same rules apply to rich and poor.
5
Apply the rulings
Practice: given a scenario, decide if the prayer is valid or invalid based on the rules. For example, a woman recites Quran in a normal tone – valid; a woman softly sings the adhan – not allowed.
Remember the distinction between normal and modulated voice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
كشعر عانته، وذكره المقطوع وتقدم في الأذان أنّ صوتها عورة وليس المراد مجرد كلامها، بل ما يحصل من تليينه وتمطيطه لا يحل سماعه وكشف . ربع عضو من أعضاء العورة) الغليظة، أو الخفيفة من الرجل والمرأة (يمنع صحة الصلاة مع وجود الساتر لا ما دون ربعه والركبة مع الفخذ عضو واحد في الأصح وكعب المرأة مع ساقها، وأذنها بانفرادها عن رأسها، وثديها المنكسر فإن كانت ناهداً فهو تبع لصدرها، والذكر بانفراده والأنثيين بلا ضمهما إليه في الصحيح وما بين السرة والعانة عضو كامل بجوانب البدن وكل ألية عورة
قوله : (إن صوتها (صورة) هو ما في النوازل، وجرى عليه في المحيط والكافي حيث عللا عدم جهرها بالتلبية بأن صوتها عورة. قال في الفتح : وعلى هذا لو قيل إذا جهرت بالقراءة في الصلاة فسدت كان متجهاً لكن قال ابن أمير حاج : الأشبه أنه ليس بعورة وإنما يؤدي إلى الفتنة، واعتمده في النهر أفاده السيد وظاهر هذا أن الخلاف في الجهر بالصوت، فقط لا تمطيطه، وتليينه وهو ينافي ما قاله المصنف ونقله المقدسي عن أبي العباس القرطبي في كتابه في السماع ونصه : ولا يظن من لا فطنة له أنا إذا قلنا صوت المرأة عورة أنا نريد بذلك كلامها لأن ذلك ليس بصحيح فإنا نجيز الكلام من النساء الأجانب، ومحاورتهن عند الحاجة إلى ذلك، ولا نجيز لهن رفع أصواتهن، ولا تمطيطها ولا تليينها، وتقطيعها لما في ذلك إستمالة الرجال إليهن، وتحريك الشهوات منهن ومن هذا لم يجز أن تؤذن المرأة اهـ . قوله : وكشف ربع عضو الخ) هذا بالنظر إلى الصلاة وإلا فحرمة الكشف، والنظر لا تتقيد بربع العضو بل القليل والكثير سواء كما في تحفة الأخيار. قوله : (الغليظة أو الخفيفة) هذا التقسيم بالنظر إلى النظر وإلا فالحكم في الصلاة متحد قوله : (يمنع صحة الصلاة) أي إذا كان قدر أداء ركن عند أبي يوسف ومحمد اعتبر أداء الركن حقيقة، والمختار قول أبي يوسف للإحتياط كما في الحلبي زاد في منية المصلي اعتبار أداء الركن مع سنته . قال شارحها البرهان الحلبي : وذلك مقدار ثلاث تسبيحات، وقال ابن أمير حاج وهذا تقييد غريب ووجهه قريب، وقيد بعضهم الكشف بكونه بغير صنعه أما لو كشفه بفعله فسدت للحال بلا خلاف قهستاني عن المنية، وعزاه في البحر إلى القنية، وجرى عليه صاحب الدر. قال في البحر : وهذا تقييد غريب، والمذهب الإطلاق واعلم أن الإنكشاف الكثير في الزمن القليل لا يمنع كالقليل في الكثير، ويمنع الكثير في الكثير ، واعتبار ربع العضو قولهما واعتبر أبو يوسف إنكشاف الأكثر وفي النصف عنه روايتان كما في الملتقى قوله : (مع وجود الساتر) قيد به لأن فاقده يصلى عارياً. قوله: (والركبة الفخذ عضو) وليست عضواً على حدة في الحقيقة إذ هي ملتقى عظم الفخذ والساق، قلت وينبغي أن يكون المرفق تبعاً للعضد، والرسخ تبعاً للذراع قاله بعض الفضلاء. قوله: (وكعب المرأة مع ساقها أي عضو، وكذا يقال فيما بعد. قوله : ( والأنثيين بلا ضمهما إليه) فإنهما معاً عضو واحد والصواب والانثيان بالألف قوله : (وكل آلية عورة)
والدبر ثالثهما في الصحيح ولو تفرق الانكشاف على أعضاء من العورة وكان جملة ما تفرق يبلغ ربع أصغر الأعضاء المنكشفة يعني التي انكشف بعضها (منع) صحة الصلاة إن طال زمن الانكشاف بقدر أداء ركن (وإلا ) أي وإن لم يبلغ ربع أصغرها أو بلغ ولم يطل زمن الانكشاف (فلا) يمنع الصحة للضرورة سواء الغني والفقير
The Book of Prayer. Like the hair of his pubic region, and his severed penis, and it has preceded in the call to prayer that her voice is 'awrah, and what is meant is not merely her speech, but rather what occurs of softening and lengthening it, it is not permissible to hear it. And uncovering a quarter of a limb from the 'awrah (the thick or thin) of the man and woman prevents the validity of prayer with the existence of a covering, not less than a quarter. The knee together with the thigh is one limb in the most correct view, and the woman's ankle together with her leg, and her ear separately from her head, and her sagging breast; if it is raised then it is a follower of her chest, and the penis alone, and the testicles without joining them to it in the correct view, and what is between the navel and the pubes is a complete limb including the sides of the body, and every buttock is 'awrah. His statement: (her voice) is what is in al-Nawazil, and al-Muhit and al-Kafi followed it where they reasoned her not reciting the talbiyah loudly by her voice being 'awrah. He said in al-Fath: On this, if it were said that if she recites loudly in prayer it becomes invalid, it would be sound, but Ibn Amir Haj said: The more appropriate is that it is not 'awrah but rather leads to fitna, and al-Nahr relied on it, as al-Sayyid said. The apparent meaning is that the difference is about loudness of voice only, not its lengthening and softening, and this contradicts what the author said and what al-Maqdisi quoted from Abu al-Abbas al-Qurtubi in his book on listening: 'One without understanding should not think that when we say a woman's voice is 'awrah we mean her speech, for that is not correct; indeed we permit conversation with foreign women when needed, but we do not permit them to raise their voices, nor to lengthen them, nor soften them, nor break them, because that attracts men and arouses desires. For this reason, a woman may not give the call to prayer.' End quote. His statement: 'And uncovering a quarter of a limb etc.' This is with respect to prayer, otherwise the prohibition of uncovering and looking is not restricted to a quarter of a limb, rather little and much are equivalent as in Tuhfat al-Akhyar. His statement: 'The thick or thin' This division is with respect to looking, otherwise the ruling in prayer is uniform. His statement: 'Prevents the validity of prayer' means if it is the amount of performing a pillar, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: the actual performance of the pillar is considered; the chosen view is the saying of Abu Yusuf due to caution, as in al-Halabi. In Munyat al-Musalli, it added: consideration of performing the pillar with its sunnah. Its commentator, Burhan al-Halabi, said: That is the measure of three tasbihat. Ibn Amir Haj said: This is a strange restriction but its reasoning is close. Some restricted uncovering to being without his action; if he uncovers it by his action, it invalidates immediately without disagreement, as in Qahistani from al-Munya, and al-Bahr attributed it to al-Qunyah, and the author of al-Durr followed it. He said in al-Bahr: This is a strange restriction; the madhhab is absolute. Know that much uncovering in a short time does not prevent, like little in much, and much prevents in much. The consideration of a quarter of a limb is their view; Abu Yusuf considered the majority uncovered, and about half there are two narrations from him, as in al-Multaqa. His statement: 'With the existence of a covering' He restricted it because the one lacking it prays naked. His statement: 'The knee and thigh are a limb' They are not a separate limb in reality, for the knee is the joint of the thigh and shin bones. I say: The elbow should be a follower of the upper arm, and the wrist a follower of the forearm, as some virtuous scholars said. His statement: 'The woman's ankle with her leg is a limb' and similarly for what follows. His statement: 'The testicles without joining them to it' For both together are one limb; the correct form is 'al-unthayan' with an alif. His statement: 'And every buttock is 'awrah.' The anus is the third of them in the correct view. And if the uncovering is scattered over limbs of the 'awrah and the total of what is scattered reaches a quarter of the smallest uncovered limbs, i.e., those which part of them was uncovered, it prevents the validity of prayer if the duration of uncovering is long enough to perform a pillar. Otherwise, i.e., if it does not reach a quarter of the smallest or reaches but the duration of uncovering is not long, it does not prevent validity due to necessity, whether rich or poor.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah, covering rulings on 'awrah and exposure in prayer. The author first addresses the woman's voice: it is considered 'awrah (to be concealed) only when modulated, lengthened, or softened in a way that arouses desire, not normal speech. This is based on the principle that her voice can be a source of fitna. There is an internal Hanafi difference: some later scholars (like Ibn Amir Haj and al-Nahr) consider it 'awrah only for loudness, not for mere modulation, but the relied-upon position (as per the matn) is that the modulated voice is 'awrah. Then the text discusses exposure during prayer: uncovering a quarter of an 'awrah limb with a covering present invalidates prayer if it lasts for the duration of performing a pillar (about three tasbihat, according to Abu Yusuf's view adopted for caution). The exposure must be without one's own action; if one intentionally uncovers, prayer is invalid immediately. There is a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the threshold: Abu Yusuf considers the majority uncovered, while Muhammad and Abu Hanifa consider a quarter. The preferred view is Abu Yusuf's due to caution. The passage defines what constitutes one limb: the knee with thigh, woman's ankle with leg, ear separately, testicles together as one, etc. Scattered exposure that totals a quarter of the smallest exposed limb also invalidates if it persists for a pillar's duration. This ruling applies to both rich and poor.

Key Terms
عورة ('awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered in prayer and from view of non-mahram. Includes the woman's voice when modulated.
ربع عضو (rub' 'udw): One quarter of a limb, used as threshold for exposure invalidating prayer (when exposure lasts a pillar's duration).
أداء ركن (ada' rukn): Performance of a pillar of prayer; used as measure of time for exposure to invalidate (about three tasbihat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the minimum amount of exposure of 'awrah that invalidates the prayer (according to the mufta bihi position)?
A) Any amount, even a little
B) A quarter of a limb, if it lasts for the duration of a pillar
C) More than half of a limb
D) The entire limb

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, covering 'awrah is a condition for valid prayer; a woman's voice is 'awrah only when modulated, and physical exposure invalidates only if it reaches a quarter of a limb for the duration of a pillar.

The Timing of Raising Hands During the Opening Takbir: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Details the timing of raising hands and its ruling for those with an excuse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi views on the timing of raising hands during the opening takbir, identify the mufta bihi view, and apply the ruling to those with an excuse.

Core Idea
Raise hands before takbir is the most correct view; if missed, prayer remains valid.

The act of raising hands (raf‘ al-yadayn) during the opening takbir is a well-established sunnah in the Hanafi school. However, an intra-Hanafi dispute exists regarding the precise moment of raising: before, with, or after the takbir. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the predominant view, explains the rational evidence, and provides a dispensation for those unable to raise fully due to illness or impairment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the act of raising hands is (a sunnah) and what the default ruling is (recommended, not obligatory).
Raising hands is from the 'adornment of prayer' but missing it does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Explore the three intra-Hanafi views on timing
State the three positions: 1) raise before takbir (al-ashahh), 2) raise simultaneously with takbir (Abu Yusuf, al-Tahawi), 3) raise after takbir (a minority view).
All views are narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him).
3
Analyze the evidence for the most correct view
The majority of Hanafi mashāyikh favour raising first because negation (of pride from other than Allah) precedes affirmation (of Allah’s greatness) in the takbīr.
The hadith of Ibn Umar also supports raising as an embellishment.
4
Apply the ruling to a person with an excuse
If someone is unable to raise both hands fully due to illness, they raise as much as possible, or with one hand only.
The sunnah is not waived entirely; it is reduced to the extent possible.
5
Determine the practical consequence if the sunnah is missed
If one forgets to raise until after completing the takbīr, they do not raise afterwards because the place has passed; the prayer is valid but the sunnah is lost.
According to a third opinion, they may raise if the interval is not long.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كفيه نحو القبلة، ولا يفرج أصابعه، ولا يضمها وإذا كان به عذر يرفع بقدر الإمكان والمرأة الحرة حذو منكبيها والأمة كالرجل كما تقدم (ثم كبر) هو الأصح فإذا لم يرفع يديه حتى فرغ من التكبير لا يأتي به لفوات محله وإن ذكره في أثنائه رفع (بلا مد) فإن مد همزة لا يكون شارعاً في الصلاة وتفسد به في أثنائها وقوله ( ناوياً) شرط لصحة التكبير (ويصح الشروع بكل ذكر خالص الله تعالى عن اختلاطه بحاجة الطالب وإن كره لترك الواجب وهو بجميع محله التوحيد ، وقيل : الإشارة إلى طرح أمورنا الدنيا خلفه والإقبال بكليته على الصلاة، وقيل ليستقبل بدنه، وعن ابن عمر رفع اليدين من زينة الصلاة بكل رفع عشر حسنات بكل إصبع حسنة كذا في العيني على البخاري، وفي هذا التعبير الإشارة إلى أنه يرفع يديه أولاً ثم يكبر، وصححه في الهداية، وفي القدوري يرفع يديه مع التكبير ، وهو المروي عن أبي يوسف والطحاوي، والذي عليه عامة المشايخ الأول، وهو الأصح لأن في الرفع نفي الكبرياء عن غير الله تعالى، وفي قوله : الله أكبر إثباتها له تعالى والنفي مقدم على الإثبات وقيل يرفع يديه بعد التكبير، والكل مروي عن النبي كما في البحر . قوله : ( وإذا كان به عذر يرفع بقدر الإمكان بالزيادة، أو النقص عن أو بإحدى اليدين دون الأخرى. قوله: (لا يأتي به لفوات محله) وينبغي أن يأتي به على القول الثالث ما لم يطل الفصل اهـ نهر .
His palms toward the qibla, and he does not spread his fingers nor join them. And if there is an excuse, he raises as much as possible. The free woman (raises to) her shoulders, and the slave woman is like the man as has preceded. (Then he says the takbir) is the most correct. So if he did not raise his hands until he finished the takbir, he does not perform it because its place has passed, and if he remembers during it, he raises. (Without elongation) for if he elongates the hamza, he does not become a person commencing prayer, and it invalidates during it. And his saying (with intention) is a condition for the validity of the takbir. (And it is valid to commence with any pure remembrance of Allah, free from mixing with the need of the seeker, even if disliked due to leaving the obligatory, and it is...) The oneness, and it is said: the indication is to throw our worldly matters behind and to turn completely to prayer, and it is said to face his body. And from Ibn Umar: raising hands is from the adornment of prayer; for every raising there are ten good deeds, for every finger a good deed, as in al-Ayni on al-Bukhari. In this expression is the indication that he raises his hands first then says the takbir, and it is declared correct in al-Hidayah. In al-Quduri, he raises his hands with the takbir, and it is narrated from Abu Yusuf and al-Tahawi. What the majority of mashayikh are upon is the first, and it is the most correct because in raising there is negation of pride from other than Allah, and in saying Allah Akbar there is affirmation of it for Him, and negation precedes affirmation. And it is said he raises his hands after the takbir, and all are narrated from the Prophet as in al-Bahr. His saying: (And if there is an excuse, he raises as much as possible) by increase or decrease or with one hand without the other. His saying: (He does not perform it because its place has passed) and he should perform it according to the third opinion as long as the interval is not long. End from al-Nahr.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi discusses the ruling of raising the hands during the opening takbir. It begins by stating the recommended position: one raises his hands with palms facing the qibla, fingers neither spread nor joined. If there is an excuse (e.g., sickness), he raises as much as possible. A free woman raises her hands to her shoulders, while a slave woman is like a man. Then the text explains the timing: the soundest view is that one first raises his hands and then says the takbir. If he delays raising until after completing the takbir, he should not raise them later, as the moment has passed. If he remembers during the takbir, he raises them. There is a difference of opinion: in al-Quduri, it is to raise with the takbir, transmitted from Abu Yusuf and al-Tahawi. However, the majority of mashayikh hold the first view, which is the correct one, because raising negates pride from other than Allah, while saying 'Allah Akbar' affirms it for Him, and negation precedes affirmation. Another view says to raise after the takbir; all are narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him). For the one with an excuse, he raises as much as possible, either more or less, or with one hand. If one does not raise due to missing the place, he should perform it according to the third opinion as long as the interval is not long.

Key Terms
كفيه نحو القبلة (kaffayhi nahwa al-qibla): His palms facing the qibla, a recommended posture for raising hands in prayer.
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands to the ears (men) or shoulders (women) during takbir.
عذر (udhr): An excuse (e.g., illness, injury) that permits reducing the sunnah to what is possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view in the Hanafi school, when should a person raise his hands during the opening takbir?
A) After saying the takbir
B) Simultaneously with the takbir
C) Before saying the takbir
D) Raising hands is not recommended in prayer

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of raising hands during the opening takbir is fulfilled by raising before saying the takbir; if missed, the prayer remains valid, and those with an excuse may raise as much as possible.
