Valid Shuru': Complete Dhikr and Language Permissibility
Ruling on shuru' conditions and language permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid shuru' and distinguish between the Hanafi rulings on non-Arabic in shuru' versus Quran recitation.

Core Idea
Shuru' requires a complete sentence of pure dhikr; non-Arabic is valid if unable, but even if able, it is permissible with prohibitive dislike.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the precise requirements for beginning the prayer (shuru'). While the takbir is the standard opening, any complete sentence of pure dhikr suffices. A key issue is the use of non-Arabic languages: the Hanafi school allows it when necessary, but discourages it when one is capable of Arabic. This ruling differs sharply from Quran recitation, where non-Arabic is invalid regardless of ability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shuru' (beginning salah). The ruling is sahih if a complete sentence of pure dhikr is uttered. If non-Arabic is used, validity depends on ability: if unable, valid; if able, valid but makruh tahrimi.
Pure dhikr means remembrance of Allah without any worldly request.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites ijma (consensus) on permissibility of non-Arabic for acts like talbiyah, salam, and oaths. By qiyas, the same principle applies to shuru' because both are forms of dhikr. Additionally, the principle that shuru' is based on pure dhikr, which is attainable in any language.
Contrast with Quran recitation, where a different dalil (Quran is name for wording and meaning) prohibits translation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'bi ghayr al-arabiyyah... ijma'ah' establishes definitive consensus on those four acts. The operative cause (illa) is that they are acts of dhikr or communication not requiring the exact Arabic wording of revelation.
Shuru' is analogized to these acts because its essence is dhikr, not recitation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi: Abu Hanifa holds shuru' valid with non-Arabic even if able, with karahah. The Sahibayn originally restricted it to the unable, but reportedly retracted. Cross-madhhab: Shafi'i school does not permit any translation in worship, including talbiyah and salam.
The retraction of the Sahibayn is a key point for tarjih.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's view: shuru' with non-Arabic is valid for all, with prohibitive dislike for the able. This is based on the consensus dalil and the fact that the Sahibayn eventually agreed.
For Quran recitation, however, the fatwa is on the Imam's first statement (recitation invalid in non-Arabic).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وإن قدر لا يصح شروعه بالفارسية ونحوها ولا قراءته بها في الأصح في قول الإمام الأعظم موافقة لهما لأن القرآن اسم للنظم والمعنى جميعاً وأما التلبية في الحج والسلامة من الصلاة والتسمية على الذبيحة والأيمان كره أي تحريماً مرتبط بقوله ويصح الشروع الخ قوله وفيه إشارة أي فيما ذكره من قوله ثم كبر فإن التكبير الله أكبر وهو جملة أو في قوله بكل ذكر فإن الذكر التام لا يكون إلا بجملة قوله وهو ظاهر الرواية والمختار در والأشبه كما في ابن أمير حاج وروى الحسن عن الإمام أنه يصير شارعاً بالمفرد وفي الدور ولو ذكر الإسم بلا صفة عند الإمام خلافاً لمحمد قوله وغيرها من الألسن هو الصحيح وخصه أبو سعيد البرادعي بالفارسية واستدل بحديث موضوع كما قاله القاري في الموضوعات لسان أهل الجنة العربية والفارسية الدرية وعلى قولهما من لم يعرفهما في حكم العاجز وتقدم قوله إن عجز الصحيح أنه يصح الشروع عنده بغير العربية ولو كان قادراً عليها مع الكراهة التحريمية للقادر لأن الشروع يتعلق بالذكر الخالص وهو يحصل بكل لسان وفي بعض الكتب ما يفيد أن صاحبيه رجعا إلى قوله هنا كرجوعه إلى قولهما في القراءة أفاده صاحب الدر ومر قوله في الأصح في قولي الإمام الأولى من قولي الإمام كما هو في بعض النسخ وبه عبر في الشرح وهذا ظاهر في القراءة لا في الشروع كما علمت وعلى هذا القول الفتوى قوله لأن القرآن إسم للنظم والمعنى جميعاً أي ومن قرأ بغير العربية فإنما أتى بالمعنى فقط قوله والأيمان معنى جواز الأيمان بغير العربية ولو مع القدرة عليها أنه إذا حلف بالله بالفارسية تنعقد يمينه وتلزمه الكفارة إذا حنث أفاده السيد فالأيمان في كلام المؤلف بفتح الهمزة جمع يمين
This is the book of salah. The apparent transmission is the utterance of takbir, and it contains an indication that for the validity of beginning [prayer], a complete sentence is necessary, such as 'Subhanallah' or 'La ilaha illallah' or 'Alhamdulillah'. And the beginning is also valid in Persian and other languages if one is unable [to pronounce] Arabic. But if able, his beginning in Persian or similar is not valid. And recitation [of Quran] in it [non-Arabic] is not valid in the most correct [view] of the Imam al-A'zam, agreeing with the two [companions], because the Quran is a name for both the wording and the meaning. As for the talbiyah in hajj, the salam from prayer, the tasmiyah over the slaughtered animal, and oaths, it is permissible in non-Arabic even with ability, by consensus. With every dhikr (with kasr of the dhal, what is by the tongue is intended; with damm, what is by the heart). He said: pure for Allah ta'ala from mixing it etc., so it is not valid with 'Allahumma ighfir li' because it seeks forgiveness, nor with 'La hawla wa la quwwata' because it seeks power, nor with 'Ma sha' Allahu kana' because it seeks repelling evil, nor with the basmalah because it seeks blessing. And there is no difference in the validity of shuru' between specific and common names like al-Karim and al-Jalil according to the most apparent and correct. He said: and it is disliked, i.e., prohibitively, connected to his statement 'and shuru' is valid'. He said: and in it is indication, i.e., in what he mentioned of his statement 'then he says takbir', for the takbir is 'Allahu akbar' which is a sentence, or in his statement 'with every dhikr', for complete dhikr is only a sentence. He said: it is the apparent transmission and the chosen view, and it is more appropriate as in Ibn Amir Hajj, and it is reported from al-Hasan from the Imam that he becomes a shari' with a single word, and in al-Durr, if he mentions the name without attribute, according to the Imam contrary to Muhammad. He said: and other languages is the correct view, and Abu Sa'id al-Baradi'i restricted it to Persian and argued with a fabricated hadith as al-Qari said in al-Mawdu'at: the language of the people of Paradise is Arabic and Persian al-Dariyyah, and according to them, whoever does not know them is like the incapable, and it preceded. He said: if incapable, the correct view is that shuru' is valid with non-Arabic even if he is able, with prohibitive dislike for the capable, because shuru' is connected to pure dhikr and it is attained in every language, and in some books it indicates that his two companions retracted to his view here as he retracted to their view in recitation, as stated by the author of al-Durr and it passed. He said: in the most correct of the two statements of the Imam, the first of the two statements of the Imam as in some copies, and it is expressed in the commentary, and this is apparent in recitation not in shuru' as you learned, and this is the fatwa. He said: because the Quran is a name for the wording and the meaning together, i.e., whoever recites in non-Arabic has only brought the meaning. He said: and oaths, meaning permissibility of oaths in non-Arabic even with ability, that if he swears by Allah in Persian, his oath is valid and the expiation is obligatory if he breaks it, as stated by al-Sayyid. So 'al-ayman' in the author's speech with fatha of hamza is plural of yamin.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hashiya on the conditions for beginning prayer (shuru'). The author explains that the opening utterance must be a complete sentence, like 'Subhanallah' or 'Alhamdulillah', and not merely a single word. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, the takbir 'Allahu Akbar' is the standard, but other complete dhikr suffices. A significant point is the permissibility of using Persian or other languages for this dhikr if one cannot pronounce Arabic; however, if one can, using non-Arabic is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi). This applies only to the opening dhikr, not to Quran recitation, where the stronger view from Imam Abu Hanifa, agreeing with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, is that reciting Quran in non-Arabic is invalid because the Quran is both wording and meaning. For other acts like talbiyah, salam, and oaths, non-Arabic is universally allowed even with ability, by consensus. The text includes a detailed discussion of what constitutes pure dhikr: it must not be a supplication for worldly needs. It also notes that the two companions (Sahibayn) are reported to have retracted to Imam Abu Hanifa's position on shuru' in non-Arabic, as he retracted to theirs on Quran recitation. The fatwa is on the first statement of the Imam regarding recitation.

Key Terms
شروع (shuru'): The act of beginning the prayer, which is initiated by the opening takbir or a complete dhikr.
ذكر خالص (dhikr khalis): Pure remembrance of Allah, free from any request for worldly benefit, used for the opening of prayer.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six core books, considered the authoritative position of the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in the Hashiya, what is the ruling if a person capable of Arabic uses Persian for the opening dhikr (shuru')?
A) It is completely valid without any dislike.
B) It is valid but prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).
C) It is invalid and the prayer is not accepted.
D) It is valid only if the person is unable to pronounce Arabic.

Key Takeaway
Shuru' is valid with any complete sentence of pure dhikr; non-Arabic is permissible when unable, but even if able, it is valid with prohibitive dislike, unlike Quran recitation which is invalid in translation.

Imamah of Those with Defects: Speech Impediments and Chronic Excuses
Rulings on imamah of those with speech defects and chronic excuses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of prayer led by a person with a chronic excuse or speech impediment, and identify the conditions under which such a person can lead others.

Core Idea
A person with a speech defect or chronic excuse cannot lead prayer for others without the same defect, though his own prayer is valid due to necessity.

This passage from Al-Tahtawi's Hashiya discusses who may lead the prayer when affected by speech impediments or chronic impurities. It clarifies the balance between necessity and perfection in the imam. Importantly, the rulings distinguish between the imam's own prayer (valid due to excuse) and his leadership for others (limited). We will unpack these distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of defects
List the speech impediments (fafaa, tamtama, luthgh) and chronic excuses (incontinence, flatulence) mentioned in the passage.
Each defect is considered an 'udhr' that excuses the individual in his own prayer.
2
Determine the ruling for leading others
State that such a person cannot lead prayer for a person without the same defect, according to the relied-upon view. Note the exception: if the follower has the same defect, it is valid.
3
Analyze the condition of striving to correct
If the person has strived to correct his speech or condition and failed, his own prayer is valid. If he neglects effort, his own prayer becomes invalid.
There is ikhtilaf on whether this condition of striving is required; many later scholars did not mention it due to hardship.
4
Consider the additional conditions for imam
The imam must be free from unforgiven impurity (more than a dirham of najasah) and must cover his awrah. Lack of these makes imamah invalid for those who are pure and covered.
5
Recognize the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Muhammad ibn al-Fadl and Ibn Amir Hajj allow a person with a speech defect to lead even those without it, reasoning that his habitual pronunciation becomes his language.
The mufta bihi is the stricter view, but the other is also considered valid.

Source Text

السين إلى الثاء ومن الراء إلى الغين ونحوه لا يكون إماماً لغيره وإذا لم يجد في القرآن شيئاً خالياً وعجز عن إصلاح لسانه آناء الليل وأطراف النهار فصلاته جائزة لنفسه وإذا ترك التصحيح والجهد فصلاته فاسدة (و) السلامة من فقد شرط كطهارة) فإن عدمها بحمل خبث لا يعفى لا تصح إمامته الطاهر (و) كذا حكم (ستر) عورة) لأن العاري لا يكون إماماً لمستور وشرحه مختصراً، ومقتضاه عدم انعقادها أصلاً فيما إذا اقتدى القاريء الحروف. قوله: (ونحوه) كاللام والياء، أو السين ثاء أو اللام نوناً. قوله: (لا يكون إماماً لغيره إلا لمثله) وفي الخانية ذكر الشيخ أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل أنها تصح إمامته لغيره لأن ما يقوله صار لغة له واختاره ابن أمير حاج وحمل قولهم: لا يؤم أعلى منه على الأولوية خروجاً من الخلاف وقواه قوله: (جائزة لنفسه) إن لم يمكنه الاقتداء وإن أمكنه لا تصح كما يؤخذ من الدر. قوله: (وإذا ترك التصحيح والجهد الخ) قال في الخلاصة: إذا كان يجتهد آناء الليل والنهار في تصحيحه، ولا يقدر على ذلك فصلاته جائزة وإن ترك جهده فصلاته فاسدة إلا أن يجعل العمر في تصحيحه، ولا يسعه أن يترك جهده في باقي عمره اه قال صاحب الذخيرة: وهذا الشق الثاني مشكل لأن ما كان خلقة لا يقدر العبد على تغييره اهـ وكذا إذا كان لعارض ليس مما يزول عادة، وإذا كان كذلك فلا يعول في الفتوى على مقتضى هذا الشرط، ومن ثم ذكر في خزانة الأكمل عن فتاوى أبي الليث لو قال الهمد الله بالهاء بدل الحاء، أو كل هو أحد بالكاف بدل القاف جاز إذا لم يقدر على غير ذلك، أو بلسانه علة، قال الفقيه: وإن لم يكن بلسانه علة، ولكن جرى ذلك على لسانه لا تفسد اهـ فلم يذكر هذا الشرط، وإن كان بعد ذكره عن إبراهيم بن يوسف وحسين بن مطيع اهـ كلام ابن أمير حاج قلت: كلامه يفيد أن هذا الشرط فيه خلاف، والأكثر لم يذكروه لأن فيه حرجاً عظيماً. قوله: (كطهارة) أي من حدث، أو خبث وإن كان كلام الشارح قاصراً على الثاني. قوله: (بحمل خبث) أي بسبب حمله خبثاً.
The one with urine incontinence or flatulence should not follow the one with the same, and the one with repetition in speech (fafaa, tamtama) and speech impediment (luthgh) cannot be imam for others; if he cannot find in the Quran something free of his impediment and is unable to correct his tongue night and day, his prayer is valid for himself; if he leaves correction and effort, his prayer is invalid. Also, safety from lacking a condition like purity: if it is absent due to carrying an unforgiven impurity, his imamah for the pure is not valid. Likewise, covering the private parts, because the uncovered cannot be imam for the covered.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the hashya discussing imamah of those with defects. It lists persons who cannot lead prayer: those with chronic excuses like incontinence or flatulence (considered having two excuses), and those with speech impediments like stuttering (fafaa), stammering (tamtama), or lisp (luthgh). Such a person may lead prayer only for someone with the same defect, according to the relied-upon view, though there is a difference of opinion. The passage also discusses that if such a person cannot find a Quranic passage free of his impediment and strived to correct his pronunciation but failed, his own prayer is valid; but if he does not bother to correct, his prayer is invalid. Additionally, an imam must be free from unforgiven impurity (e.g., more than a dirham of najasah) and must cover his awrah. The commentary expands on these rulings, noting exceptions and ikhtilaf, such as the view that a person with a speech impediment may lead even one without it if his pronunciation becomes like a second language. The passage also discusses purity requirements, clarifying that the impurity mentioned is unforgiven (more than a dirham). Overall, the teaching is that an imam must be in a state of perfection in terms of ability, purity, and covering, and those with defects may only lead if the follower shares the same defect.

Key Terms
الفأفأة (al-fa'fa'ah): Stuttering with repetition of the letter 'fa'.
التمتمة (al-tamtamah): Stammering with repetition of the letter 'ta'.
اللثغ (al-luthgh): A speech impediment causing substitution of letters, e.g., sin to tha, ra to ghayn.
عذر (udhr): Chronic excuse or condition that makes complete purity or correct recitation difficult.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Anyone, because his own prayer is valid.
B) Only those with the same condition.
C) Only if he also covers his private parts.
D) Even if he does not strive to correct it.

Key Takeaway
A person with a chronic defect may pray alone, but may only lead others who share the same defect.

Fasad vs Butlan: The Hanafi Distinction
Defining fasad vs butlan and stating the number of invalidators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi distinction between fasad and butlan and identify when the ruling differs in ibadat versus muamalat.

Core Idea
Fasad and butlan are identical in worship but distinct in transactions — the Hanafi school distinguishes defective (fasid) from void (batil) contracts.

The commentator begins the chapter on invalidators of prayer by clarifying a foundational terminological distinction that pervades Hanafi law. Without this distinction, a student may misapply rulings across different fiqh chapters. This lesson unpacks that definition and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context: ibadat vs muamalat
Notice that the passage first addresses worship (عبادة) and then transactions (معاملات). The same terms may carry different meanings depending on the area of fiqh.
The context determines whether fasad = butlan or not.
2
Extract the ruling for each context
In worship: 'فساد وبطلان سيان' — they are identical; both render the act invalid and requiring repetition. In transactions: fasad means a contract defective in description (e.g., a sale with an invalid condition), while butlan means void ab initio (e.g., selling a corpse).
The passage uses 'كالبيع' as an example.
3
Understand the practical consequence
In a fasid sale, the contract is not entirely void; it can be corrected if the defect is removed. In a batil sale, no contract exists. This distinction affects rulings like ownership and return of goods.
Example: a sale with a condition that contradicts the contract's nature is fasid, not batil.
4
Distinguish the Shafi'i view
The Shafi'i school does not distinguish: fasad and butlan are synonymous in all contexts. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical implications in muamalat.
Hanafi mufti must apply the distinction when issuing fatwas on contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يفسد الصلاة كتاب الصلاة الفساد ضد الصلاح والفساد والبطلان في العبادة سيان وفي المعاملات كالبيع المفسد بالعد تقريباً لا تحديداً فقال (وهو : ثمانية وستون شيئاً) منه مفترقان، وحصر دوسه [؟] الحقد [؟] العادل، وفي غيرهما إن أراد شيئاً من عرض الدنيا فمكروه وإن أراد تعظيم المسلم، وإكرامه فلا بأس به اهـ
Chapter of what invalidates prayer. The book of prayer. Corruption is the opposite of soundness. Corruption and invalidity in worship are synonymous, and in transactions like sale, corruption is approximately but not exactly by number. So he said: (It is sixty-eight things) from it are two separate [categories]? and enumeration... and in others, if he intends something of worldly gain then it is disliked, and if he intends glorifying a Muslim and honoring him, then there is no harm. End.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on what invalidates prayer. The commentator first clarifies the key terms: فساد (fasad) and بطلان (butlan). In the context of worship (عبادة), these two terms are identical in meaning—both render the act invalid. However, in transactions (معاملات) like sale, they are distinct: a fasad contract is one that has a defect in its description (e.g., a sale with a condition that contradicts the contract's nature), while a batil contract is one that is not valid in its very foundation (e.g., selling a dead animal). The matn of Maraqi al-Falah states that the invalidators of prayer are sixty-eight things. The commentator adds that these are divided into two categories: those that invalidate in both worship and transactions, and those that differ. The last part indicates that if one intends worldly gain through an action (like kissing the Quran?) it is disliked, but if intending to honor a Muslim, it is permissible.

Key Terms
فساد (fasad): In worship, fasad is identical to butlan; in transactions, it refers to a contract that is valid in its foundation but defective in its description (e.g., sale with an invalid condition).
بطلان (butlan): In worship, butlan means the act is invalid and must be repeated. In transactions, butlan refers to a contract that has no legal effect from the outset (e.g., sale of a corpse).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which context do the Hanafis treat fasad and butlan as synonymous?
A) In all contexts
B) In worship (ibadat)
C) In transactions (muamalat)
D) Only in marriage contracts

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, fasad and butlan are identical in worship but different in transactions; a fasid contract is defective but corrigible, while a batil contract is void ab initio.

Ruling on a Mutayammim Seeing Water During Prayer: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Timing
Intra-Hanafi dispute on invalidation when a mutayammim sees water, with timing before/after tashahhud as the key variable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mutayammim seeing water during prayer before and after sitting for tashahhud, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding invalidation in description (wasfan) vs. essence (aslan).

Core Idea
When a mutayammim sees water after tashahhud, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say prayer is valid (wasfan); Muhammad and Zufar say invalid (aslan).

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of seeing water during prayer for someone performing tayammum. The timing—before or after sitting for tashahhud—determines whether the ruling is agreed upon or contested. More importantly, the disagreement reveals a key distinction in Hanafi legal theory: whether invalidation affects the prayer's description (wasfan) or its very essence (aslan). Understanding this distinction is crucial for deriving related rulings, such as the effect of laughter behind such an imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and agreed ruling
Recognize that the passage deals with a mutayammim (or his follower) who sees water during prayer. The agreed ruling is that if this occurs before sitting for the measure of tashahhud, the prayer is invalidated by all Hanafi imams.
This consensus provides a baseline for the disputed case.
2
Locate the disputed timing
The disagreement arises when the mutayammim sees water after sitting for tashahhud but before completing the prayer. Determine the two opposing views: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad and Zufar.
Tashahhud is the final sitting before salams.
3
State the two positions and their proofs
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: prayer not invalidated (wasfan) because the essential acts (fara'id) are complete; seeing water after completion is like a hadath occurring after the prayer is essentially valid. Muhammad and Zufar: prayer invalidated (aslan) because tayammum's condition (absence of water) is broken, retroactively invalidating the prayer.
Each side uses a different legal lens: condition vs. completion.
4
Understand the wasfan vs. aslan distinction
Invalidation 'wasfan' means the prayer is valid in essence but descriptively deficient (e.g., it must be repeated but the tahrimah remains). Invalidation 'aslan' means the prayer was never valid from the start (tahrimah is cut off). This distinction governs related rulings like the effect of the follower's laughter.
This is a unique Hanafi conceptual tool.
5
Apply to the follower's laughter case
The passage illustrates the practical consequence: if a follower behind a mutayammim imam laughs loudly, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf the follower must renew wudu (because the imam's tahrimah remains), while Muhammad and Zufar say no wudu needed (because the imam was never truly in prayer).
This case shows the real impact of the wasfan/aslan distinction.

و (يفسدها رؤية متيمم) أو مقتد به، ولم يره إمامه (ماء) قدر على استعماله قبل قعوده قدر التشهد كما سنقيد به المسائل التي بعد. قال في البحر: المتوضي خلف المتيمم إذا رأى الماء فقهقه المؤتم فعليه الوضوء عندهما خلافاً لمحمد وزفر بناء على أن الفريضة متى فسدت لا تقطع التحريمة عندهما خلافاً لمحمد وزفر وحاصله أن هذه المسألة متفق فيها على بطلان الصلاة غير أن الإمام وأبا يوسف يبطلانها وصفاً فقط، ومحمد وزفر وصفاً وأصلاً، ولذا حكما بعدم النقض بالقهقهة فيها لأنه لم يكن في الصلاة أصلاً، ولا شك أن هذا الحكم ليس من الأحكام الإثني عشرية فافهم. قوله: (قدر على استعماله) الضمير في قدر للإمام في الصورتين. قوله: (قبل قعوده قدر التشهد) إنما قيد به ليكون الفساد فيها متفقاً عليه بخلاف ما إذا قعد قدر التشهد حيث لا تفسد عندهما، وتفسد عنده لهما أن هذه المعاني وإن كانت مفسدة كالحدث، والكلام، إلا أن حدوثها إنما جاء بعد التمام إذا لم يبق عليه شيء من الفرائض.
And it (the prayer) is invalidated by the sighting of water by a mutayammim who is praying behind an imam and the imam does not see it, in the time he is able to use it before he sits for the measure of tashahhud, as we will qualify the subsequent issues. He said in al-Bahr: The one performing wudu behind a mutayammim, if he sees water and the muqtadi (follower) laughs loudly, then he must perform wudu according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad and Zufar, based on the principle that when the obligatory prayer is invalidated, the tahrimah is not cut off according to the two, contrary to Muhammad and Zufar. The summary is that this issue is agreed upon regarding the invalidation of the prayer, but the Imam (Abu Hanifa) and Abu Yusuf invalidate it only in description (wasfan), while Muhammad and Zufar invalidate it in description and in essence (aslan). Hence they rule that the prayer is not nullified by loud laughter because he was not in prayer at all. There is no doubt that this ruling is not among the twelve rulings? Understand. His statement: 'able to use it' – the pronoun in 'able' refers to the imam in both cases. His statement: 'before he sits for the measure of tashahhud' – it is qualified thus to make the invalidation agreed upon, contrary to the case where he sits for the measure of tashahhud; then it does not invalidate according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), but invalidates according to him (Imam Muhammad? unclear). For them, these meanings, although invalidating like hadath and speech, their occurrence comes after completion when nothing of the obligatory acts remains.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario of a person performing tayammum (dry ablution) who, during prayer, sees water that he can use. The ruling depends on the timing: if he sees water before sitting for the duration of tashahhud, the prayer is invalidated by agreement among the Hanafi imams. However, if he sees it after sitting for tashahhud, there is a dispute: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the prayer is not invalidated because the essential acts are complete, while according to Muhammad and Zufar, it is invalidated. The commentary also discusses a related issue: if a person performing wudu behind a mutayammim sees water and laughs loudly, the follower must perform wudu according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, because the imam's prayer is invalidated only in description (wasf), not in essence, so the tahrimah (the prohibition that starts prayer) remains. Muhammad and Zufar hold that the prayer is invalidated in essence, so the follower was never in a valid prayer, hence no wudu is required. The key distinction is 'wasfan' vs. 'aslan' invalidation.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The initial takbir that prohibits worldly actions and starts the prayer; its being 'cut off' means the prayer state ends.
وصفاً وأصلاً (wasfan wa aslan): Invalidation in description (wasfan) means the prayer is valid in its essential validity but descriptively deficient; invalidation in essence (aslan) means it was never valid from the start.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if a mutayammim sees water after sitting for the measure of tashahhud in prayer, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalidated.
B) The prayer is not invalidated.
C) The prayer is valid but must be repeated.
D) The prayer is invalid only if the imam also sees water.

Key Takeaway
The timing of seeing water relative to sitting for tashahhud determines whether the prayer is invalidated by consensus or disputed, and the distinction between wasfan and aslan governs related rulings.

Taharah — Purification

Invalidation of Prayer by a Woman's Proximity (Muhadhat): Conditions and Dispute
Analyzing the conditions under which a woman's proximity invalidates the man's prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a woman's proximity (muhadhat) invalidates a man's prayer according to the Hanafi school, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the required duration of alignment.

Core Idea
Muhadhat invalidates only when the woman is desirable, they share the same prayer, alignment is of a specific limb, and no barrier exists—and the duration must equal a rukn.

The Hanafi school holds that a woman's alignment with a man during prayer can invalidate the prayer if certain conditions are met. This ruling is based on the principle that women should stand behind men to avoid distraction. However, there is an internal dispute over how long the alignment must last. In this lesson, we will dissect the conditions for muhadhat and examine the preferred opinion within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act being ruled is muhadhat—a woman's alignment with a man during prayer. The ruling is that it invalidates the prayer (mufsid). Note that not every alignment invalidates; specific conditions must be met.
Muhadhat is one of the mufsidat al-salah listed in the text along with other invalidators like intentional hadath or fainting.
2
List the conditions for invalidation
From the text, extract all conditions: (1) the woman must be desirable (mushatah), (2) alignment must be of the shin and ankle (or at least one organ), (3) the prayer must be shared (mushtaraka tahreema), (4) they must be in the same place (mutahid al-makan) with no barrier, (5) the alignment must last for the duration of a rukn (pillar) according to the relied-upon view.
The condition of 'desirable' includes mahram and wife; it is not limited to non-mahram.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad (and Abu Hanifa) require the alignment to persist for the time it takes to perform a rukn, while Abu Yusuf considers even a brief alignment to invalidate. Determine which view is mufta bihi.
The dispute is purely over duration: both sides agree that some alignment is required, but disagree on how long.
4
Locate the dalil (proof)
The primary proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (marfu' or mawquf) instructing women to stand behind men, and the general principle that the prayer's validity depends on proper arrangement and avoiding distraction.
The text also uses qiyas: the distraction (shahwah) only becomes effective when it lasts a significant time.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The relied-upon position is Imam Muhammad's view that the alignment must last for the duration of a rukn. This is adopted by al-Halabi and al-Haskafi, and follows the principle of facilitating the prayer (istihsan).
The mufta bihi is not unanimous; some later works attribute general invalidation to Abu Yusuf.

With a complete time for it, (and intentional hadath) meaning it does not precede him because he builds upon it, (or by the action of someone else) like the falling of a nail that bloodies him, (and fainting and insanity and janaba occurring by looking or wet dream) a sleeping person who is firmly settled, (and the alignment of a desirable woman with her shin and ankle according to the most correct view, even if she is a mahram for him or a wife whom he desires, even if past desire like an ugly old woman, in the performance of a pillar according to Muhammad or its equivalent according to Abu Yusuf, (in prayer) even if by gestures, (absolute) so the funeral prayer is not invalidated because it has no prostration, (sharing the tahreema) by both being led by an imam or her following him, (in a single place) even virtually by her standing on less than a qama [height] without a barrier of a cubit or a gap that can fit a man, and he did not gesture to her to step back, then if she does not step back at his gesture, her prayer is invalidated but not his, and he is not required...
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement (hishiya) on Maraqi al-Falah, explaining the rules of invalidators of prayer (mufsidat), with particular focus on muhadhat—a woman's proximity invalidating a man's prayer. The text first lists other invalidators: intentional hadath (ritual impurity) does not invalidate because one builds upon it (yabni) under certain conditions; hadath caused by another's action (like drawing blood) invalidates because building is not allowed—the condition for valid building is that the hadath be from a heavenly cause (samawi); fainting, insanity, and janaba from looking or wet dream also invalidate, with a nuance about the sleeping person needing to be firmly settled. 

The core of the passage is muhadhat. The ruling states that a man's prayer is invalidated if he stands alongside a desirable woman (mushatah) with her shin and ankle level with his, according to the most correct view (al-asahh). This applies even if she is a mahram or his wife, provided she is desirable, and even if past desire like an ugly old woman—only that she is past childbearing age. The invalidation occurs during the performance of a pillar (rukn) according to Imam Muhammad, or according to its equivalent duration according to Abu Yusuf. The prayer must be a shared prayer (mushtaraka tahreema), meaning both are following the same imam or she is following him, and they are in the same place (mutahid) either actually or virtually (e.g., she stands on a higher ground but within a qama's height). 

The hashiya clarifies key points: (1) The woman must be 'desirable' (mushatah)—fit for intercourse, regardless of age, so a young girl of nine is included. (2) The alignment must be with the shin and ankle, but some scholars hold any single organ suffices. (3) There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad requires the alignment to last for the duration of a rukn, while Abu Yusuf considers even a short alignment invalid. (4) The prayer must be a 'shared prayer'—both must be in the same prayer with the same imam at the time of alignment; if they are not in the act of prayer (e.g., going for wudu), no invalidation occurs. (5) The imam or follower must gesture the woman to step back; if she does not, her prayer invalidates but not his, unless the imam fails to gesture—then his prayer invalidates. 

The authority weight: The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah via the matn, with the hashiya providing critical refinements from later scholars like al-Zayla'i, al-Halabi, and al-Haskafi. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that muhadhat invalidates only when all conditions are met: desire, shared prayer, alignment of a specific organ, and no barrier.

Key Terms
محاذاة (muhadhat): Alignment of a woman's body part (especially shin and ankle) with a man's during prayer, in a shared prayer without barrier.
مشتهاة (mushatah): A woman desirable for intercourse, including those past childbearing age but still capable of arouse, but excluding young girls below nine or without development.
مشتركة تحريمة (mushtaraka tahreema): Both the man and woman are in the same obligatory prayer with the same tahreema (opening takbir), i.e., following the same imam or her following him.
حائل (hail): A physical barrier such as a wall, pillar, or space that separates the man and woman during prayer, preventing invalidation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a necessary condition for muhadhat (a woman's proximity) to invalidate a man's prayer?
A) The woman must be a non-mahram and not his wife.
B) The alignment must last for the duration of at least one rukn (pillar) according to the relied-upon view.
C) The woman must be standing exactly at the same level as the man, not higher or lower.
D) The man must have gestured her to step back twice before continuing.

Key Takeaway
Muhadhat invalidates a man's prayer only when all conditions are met: a desirable woman, shared prayer, limb alignment, no barrier, and duration of a rukn (mufta bihi).

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Time Sufficient for a Pillar and Effect of Uncovering Awrah or Impurity
Ruling on the minimum duration of a pillar and the effect of uncovering or impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the measure of time sufficient to perform a pillar of prayer according to the chosen Hanafi view, and explain when uncovering the awrah or presence of impurity invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
Prayer invalid if pillar time passes with awrah uncovered or impurity, unless removed instantly.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from Maraqi al-Falah regarding the effect of a delay in performing a pillar while the prayer is compromised by uncovering the awrah or impurity. The text clarifies the measurement of time considered sufficient to perform a pillar, and distinguishes between harmful persisting conditions and harmless momentary incidents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Condition
Recognize that the ruling addresses a scenario where a person delays a pillar (rukn) while the awrah is uncovered or prohibitive impurity is present.
The term 'pillar' refers to essential acts like ruku' or sujud.
2
Understand the Time Measurement
Learn that the minimal time sufficient to perform a pillar is measured by the sunnah duration, set as three tasbihat (Subhana Rabbi al-Adheem x3). This is the chosen view (mukhtar) of the second imam.
Three tasbihat is approximately 6-10 seconds, used as a benchmark.
3
Distinguish Harmful vs. Harmless Duration
Note that if uncovering or impurity persists for the time of a pillar (three tasbihat or more), the prayer becomes invalid. However, if it is momentary and rectified instantly (e.g., immediate covering or removal), it does not harm the prayer.
The text gives examples of wind uncovering the awrah and the person covering it immediately.
4
Apply the Rule to Scenarios
Practice applying the rule: much uncovering in much time is harmful; little in little is not; much in little or little in much? The text states the same logic applies as for impurity.
The key is whether the invalidating condition lasted as long as a pillar.

كترك ركن (أو إمكانه أي مضى زمن يسع أداء ركن (مع كشف العورة أو مع نجاسة مانعة) لوجود المنافي فإن دفع النجاسة بمجرد وقعها ولا أثر لها، أو ستر عورته بمجرد كشفها فلا يضره) قوله: (زمن يسع أداء ركن) وإن كان في ركن طويل، والمراد أنه يسعه بسنته، وهو قدر ثلاث تسبيحات، وهذا مذهب الثاني، وهو المختار كما في الدر. قوله: (مع كشف العورة) الحاصل أن الكشف الكثير في الزمن الكثير مضر، والقليل في القليل غير مضر كالكثير في القليل، والقليل في الكثير، والمراد بكشف العورة ما كشف العضو منها. قوله: (أو مع نجاسة مانعة) ولو سهو، وتأتي الصور المذكورة في الكشف هنا. قوله: (أو ستر عورته الخ) كأن هبت الريح فكشفته فستر عورته من ساعته فلا يضره.
(Like leaving a pillar) or the possibility of it, meaning the passing of time sufficient to perform a pillar (with uncovering of the private parts or with prohibitive impurity) because the contradiction exists. So if he removes the impurity immediately upon its occurrence and it has no effect, or covers his private parts immediately upon its uncovering, it does not harm him. He said: (Time sufficient to perform a pillar) even if it is in a long pillar, and what is meant is that it suffices with its sunnah, which is the measure of three tasbihat. This is the madhhab of the second (Imam), and it is the chosen (view) as in al-Durr. He said: (With uncovering of the private parts) the conclusion is that much uncovering in much time is harmful, and little in little is not harmful, like much in little, and little in much. And what is meant by uncovering the private parts is that which uncovers the organ. He said: (Or with prohibitive impurity) even if forgetfully, and the same scenarios mentioned for uncovering apply here. He said: (Or covers his private parts etc.) like if the wind blew and uncovered him, so he covers his private parts immediately, so it does not harm him.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of Maraqi al-Falah, commented upon by al-Tahtawi. It addresses the situation where a person delays a pillar of prayer (e.g., ruku') for a period sufficient to perform that pillar while his awrah is uncovered or while there is prohibitive impurity on his body or clothes. The ruling is that this invalidates the prayer because it combines two defects: delaying the pillar without excuse and having an invalidating condition. However, if the impurity is removed immediately upon occurring, or the awrah is covered immediately upon being uncovered, the prayer is not harmed. The hashiya clarifies that the 'time sufficient' means the time to perform the pillar with its sunnah actions, which is approximately the time to say three tasbihat (Subhana Rabbi al-Adheem three times). This measurement is the second opinion (of Abu Yusuf or Muhammad) and is the chosen view, as noted in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. The hashiya further explains the details: much uncovering in much time is harmful, but little uncovering in little time is not harmful, and likewise little uncovering in much time is not harmful? Actually the text says: 'الكثير في القليل مضر' no it says 'الكثير في القليل مضر؟' careful: The text says: 'الكشف الكثير في الزمن الكثير مضر، والقليل في القليل غير مضر كالكثير في القليل، والقليل في الكثير' This seems contradictory: it says much in little is harmful? Actually it says much uncovering in much time is harmful, little in little is not harmful, like much in little? Wait: 'كالكثير في القليل' might be a typo in OCR. Probably it means that much uncovering in little time is also harmful? But the hashiya says the same scenarios apply as for impurity. The overall point is that if the uncovering or impurity persists for the duration of the pillar, it invalidates; if it is instantaneous and rectified immediately, it does not.

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): A fundamental pillar of prayer without which the prayer is invalid, e.g., qiyam, ruku', sujud.
ثلاث تسبيحات (thalath tasbihat): The measure of time to say 'Subhana Rabbi al-Adheem' three times, used as the standard for a minimal rukn.
مذهب الثاني (madhhab al-thani): The opinion of the second imam (either Abu Yusuf or Muhammad al-Shaybani), as opposed to Imam Abu Hanifa.

What is the measure of time considered sufficient to perform a pillar (rukn) during prayer, according to the chosen view in this text?
A) The time to say one tasbih
B) The time to say three tasbihat
C) The time to recite al-Fatiha
D) The time to perform one rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Uncovering the awrah or presence of prohibitive impurity invalidates prayer only if it persists for the duration of one rukn (three tasbihat), but immediate removal avoids harm.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Wajib of Including the Nose in Sujud
Ruling on sujud and intra-Hanafi difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for sujud when the nose does not touch the ground, explain the intra-madhhab difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the ruling to a prayer scenario.

Core Idea
Omitting the nose in sujud without excuse is makruh tahrimi because it leaves a wajib — but the sequence of contact is disputed within the Hanafi school.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah addresses a key detail of prostration: the obligation to include the nose. While the forehead is the primary limb, the Hanafi school holds that the nose must also touch the ground. The text clarifies that restricting to the forehead alone is makruh tahrimi, and it presents an internal dispute regarding the order of placement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'al-iqtisar 'ala al-jabhah' — restricting prostration to the forehead only, without the nose, and without an excuse. The text rules it as 'makruh tahrimi' (prohibitively disliked).
The term 'تحريماً' explicitly indicates this is stronger than ordinary dislike.
2
Identify the wajib that is left
The wajib (obligatory element) is 'ضم الأنف' — including the nose on the ground during sujud. Omitting it without excuse triggers the makruh tahrimi.
In Hanafi usul, leaving a wajib without excuse incurs sin and requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw), but does not invalidate the prayer.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute on sequence
Imam Abu Hanifa permits starting with the forehead and then adding the nose later. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) prohibit this unless there is an excuse from the forehead.
The commentator notes: 'وكذا عكسه عند الإمام ومنعه الصاحبان إلا إذا كان بالجبهة عذر' — the opposite (starting with forehead first) is allowed by Imam but forbidden by the Sahibayn.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and practical caution
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) follows Imam Abu Hanifa: the sujud is valid regardless of sequence. However, for caution (ihtiyat), the Sahibayn's view is recommended to avoid any dispute.
The school's principle is that following the cautious opinion is praiseworthy when there is a recognized difference.

البيع والكنائس لما فيها من التماثيل. فتكون مأوى الشياطين كما أفاده العيني في شرح البخاري في بحث المساجد من كتاب الصلاة. قوله: (ولا يصلي في الحمام إلا لضرورة الخ) عبارة البرهان الحلبي الأولى أن لا يصلي في الحمام الخ.
Book of Prayer: (Restricting to the forehead in prostration without excuse by the nose leads to leaving the obligatory act of including the nose, which is prohibitively disliked. And) Prayer is disliked in the road because it occupies the right of the public and prevents them from passing. And in the bathroom and in the [makhraj] i.e. the impure place. And prayer is disliked in the graveyard and similar places because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade that... the house implies the establishment of dislike also if the image is under his feet or in his sitting place, and they have stated that there is no dislike in that. And similarly, the hadith of Jibril 'We do not enter a house in which there is a dog or an image' establishes it. It is answered that there is what specifies it, which is in Sahih Ibn Hibban: Jibril (peace be upon him) asked permission from the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he said: 'Enter.' He said: 'How can I enter when in your house there is a curtain with pictures? If you must do something, cut off their heads, or cut them into cushions, or make them into a carpet.' This suggests that there is no dislike for praying on a carpet that has images, even if they are in the place of prostration, unless it is said that it includes the form of resembling worshippers of them while standing and bowing, and it includes honoring them if he prostrates on them. And they differed regarding whether an image on dirhams or dinars prevents the entry of angels. Qadi 'Iyad held that it does not prevent, and the hadiths are specified. Al-Nawawi held that it prevents due to the generality. Then what is meant is the angels of mercy, not the recording angels, for they do not leave him except during intercourse and relieving oneself. And in Sharh al-Mishkat by Mulla 'Ali, quoting from al-Khattabi and Ibn al-Malik, they do not enter a house in which there is a dog or an image that it is prohibited to possess, such as dogs and images. As for what is not prohibited, like the dog of hunting, agriculture, and livestock, and images that are disrespected in carpets, cushions, and others, it does not prevent the angels from entering his house, and this does not contradict the prohibition of making images. He said: 'And it is disliked to restrict [to the forehead] etc.' And likewise its opposite according to Imam, and the two companions prohibit it except if there is an excuse with the forehead, as stated by al-Sayyid. He said: 'Prohibitively disliked' meaning dislike of prohibition, and it is indicated by his saying 'leaving the obligatory act of including the nose.' He said: 'Its occupation of the public right' and the preoccupation of the mind distracts from khushu, so one becomes occupied with creation from the truth. And because of this, some conditioned that it is in inhabited areas, not in the wilderness, as stated by Sharh al-Mishkat. He said: 'And in the bathroom' derived from hamim, which is hot water, and likewise the bathing place. And they differed on the cause: some said because each is a place for removing impurities and a drain for washings. According to this, if one washes a spot in the bathroom, it is not disliked, and Qadikhan followed this, and al-Kamal confirmed it in Zad al-Faqir. And some said the cause is that it is a dwelling of devils, for it is narrated that when Iblis descended to earth, he said: 'O Lord, make a house for me.' He said: 'The bathroom.' He said: 'Make a seat for me.' He said: 'The markets.' He said: 'Make companions for me.' He said: 'The poets.' He said: 'Make a book for me.' He said: 'Tattooing.' And it follows from this that prayer is disliked inside the bathroom whether that spot is washed or not. He said: 'And in the graveyard' with three possible vowellings of the ba, because it is resembling the Jews and Christians. He said: 'May Allah curse the Jews and Christians, they took the graves of their prophets as places of worship.' And it is the same whether it is above or behind or under what one is standing on. And the graves of the prophets (peace be upon them) are exempted, so prayer is absolutely not disliked in them, whether exhumed or not, as long as the grave is not in the direction of the qibla because they are alive in their graves. Do you not see that the resting place of Isma'il (peace be upon him) is in al-Hijr under the spout? Prayer is performed in seven places: in the dunghill, slaughterhouse, graveyard, highway, bathroom, camel resting places, and on top of the House of Allah. And one should not pray in the bathroom except out of necessity for fear of losing the time of prayer. And that between the Black Stone and Zamzam there is the grave of seventy prophets. Then that mosque is the best place to seek, unlike the graves of others, as stated in Sharh al-Mishkat and Zad al-Faqir. And prayer in the graveyard is disliked unless there is a place prepared for prayer with no impurity and no filth. Al-Halabi said: Because the dislike is due to resemblance, and that is absent then. And in al-Qahistani from Jana'iz al-Mudmarat: prayer towards the grave is not disliked unless it is in front of him such that if he prays the prayer of the humble, his sight falls upon it. He said: 'And the like' are what are mentioned in the hadith. He said: 'In the dunghill' (al-mazbala) with fatha and damma on the mim and ba, two dialects, and it is the place of dung i.e. manure. Sharh al-Mishkat said: and similar to it are all impurities. He said: 'And the slaughterhouse' (al-majzara) because it is a place of blood and dung. And some said the cause of dislike is fear of harm coming to him from the animals' aversion. It is with fatha, damma, and kasra on the zay. Sharh al-Mishkat said: the correct transmission and corrected copies have kasra on the zay, and that is what al-Jawhari restricted to, meaning that others are also permissible. He said: 'And the highway' (qari'at al-tariq) meaning the road that is beaten (maqru'a) by sandals, so the active participle is in the sense of the passive participle. He said: 'And camel resting places' (ma'atin al-ibil) intended here are their resting places absolutely. The cause is that they are from the devils. Yahya ibn Adam said: the prohibition is because camels are feared for their sudden assault, so one may be harmed. And the meaning of 'they are from the devils' is that their characteristics are from the characteristics of devils. In another hadith, 'they were created from the devils,' and Ibn Hibban interpreted it as they were created with them. And al-ma'atin in language are the places of camels where they kneel when they drink the first draught, then the trough is filled for them a second time, so they return from their thirst to the trough and drink the second draught, and this only occurs in hot days. When it becomes cold, there is no 'atn for camels. He was asked about prayer in sheep folds, and he said: 'Pray in them, for they were created with blessing.' And the prohibition of prayer in camel resting places is for tanzih, just as the command for sheep folds is for permissibility. And cattle folds are annexed to sheep folds, so prayer is not disliked in them. The full discussion is in al-'Ayni on Bukhari. And if the camels are not in their resting places, Ibn Malik said: prayer is still disliked in them because these places are places of impurity. If one prays without a prayer mat, the prayer is invalid unless the place is pure, or with a prayer mat it is disliked due to the foul smell. And Sharh al-Mishkat said about his saying 'pray in sheep folds': meaning on a prayer mat when there is necessity, or that the sheep owners used to clean the folds, so prayer was permitted in them for that reason. He said: And prayer is disliked in all places of devils, including the valley in which one slept through the Fajr prayer, and every place that has been afflicted with anger, like the land of Thamud, Babylon, and the dwellings of the people of Lut. I say: And from this it is known that prayer is disliked in churches and synagogues because of the images in them, so they become dwellings of devils, as stated by al-'Ayni in Sharh al-Bukhari in the section on mosques from the Book of Prayer. He said: 'And one should not pray in the bathroom except out of necessity etc.' The statement of Burhan al-Halabi: the first is that one should not pray in the bathroom, etc.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah is an expansion (sharh) of the matn that lists disliked (makruh) situations and places for prayer. The commentary provides the legal reasoning, proofs, and some intra-madhhab differences. The opening ruling states that restricting prostration to the forehead only (without including the nose) without an excuse is makruh tahrimi, because including the nose (ضم الأنف) is wajib. The commentator notes that the opposite case—beginning with the forehead and then adding the nose later—is permitted by Imam Abu Hanifa but prohibited by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) unless there is an excuse. The text then discusses images (suwar) and dogs in the context of a hadith that angels do not enter a house containing them, clarifying that this does not make prayer in such a house disliked if the image is underfoot or in a place that is disrespected. It also addresses the difference of opinion on whether images on coins prevent angelic entry. The main body of the passage covers the seven places mentioned in the hadith: dunghill, slaughterhouse, graveyard, highway, bathroom, camel resting places, and atop the Ka'ba. For each, the commentary explains the cause of dislike (علة الكراهة): for the bathroom, either because it is a place of impurity or a dwelling of devils; for the graveyard, due to resemblance to Jews and Christians, except for the graves of prophets; for camel resting places, because camels are associated with devils or due to danger, and the dislike is for tanzih (i.e., makruh tanzihi). Sheep folds are exempted and are considered a place of blessing. The passage also mentions that prayer is disliked in any place where devils gather or where divine wrath occurred, such as the valley of Thamud. It concludes with the ruling that prayer in the bathroom is only permissible out of necessity, such as fear of missing the prayer time.

Key Terms
الاقتصار على الجبهة (al-iqtisar 'ala al-jabhah): Restricting prostration to the forehead only, without including the nose.
ضم الأنف (damm al-anf): The act of placing the nose on the ground in prostration along with the forehead.
كراهة تحريم (karahah tahrimiyyah): A dislike that is close to haram; omitting a wajib action is at this level.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling (hukm) for a person who prostrates using only the forehead without touching the nose, without any excuse?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
C) It is makruh tanzih (mildly disliked).
D) It is permissible without any dislike.

Key Takeaway
In sujud, including the nose is wajib; omitting it without excuse is makruh tahrimi, and the preferred order is to place both together.

The Seven Places Where Prayer Is Disliked
Enumeration and explanation of disliked prayer places

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven places where prayer is disliked according to the Hanafi school, explain the illa (cause) for each, and identify the exceptions and degrees of dislike.

Core Idea
Prayer in certain places is disliked due to impurity, resemblance to non-believers, or being a dwelling of devils — but the ruling is generally makruh tanzih, not prohibitive.

This passage enumerates seven locations where the Prophet ﷺ prohibited or disliked prayer. The Hanafi school classifies most of these as makruh tanzih (mildly disliked), meaning the prayer is valid but one should avoid it. The commentary explores the legal causes ('illal) for each place, exceptions such as prophets' graves, and the distinction between places of impurity and places of devils.

Guided Path
1
List the seven places from the hadith
The passage mentions: المزبلة (dunghill), المجزرة (slaughterhouse), المقبرة (graveyard), قارعة الطريق (highway), الحمام (bathroom), معاطن الإبل (camel resting places), and فوق ظهر بيت الله (on top of the Ka'ba).
These are also known from other hadith compilations.
2
Identify the ruling and its degree
For most of these, the ruling is makruh tanzih (lightly disliked). The text specifically says for camel resting places it is 'للتنزيه'. For the sujud ruling earlier, it was makruh tahrimi; here it is generally milder.
The degree depends on the 'illa. For example, bathroom and graveyard have stronger causes but still tanzih in the relied-upon view.
3
Understand the 'illa (legal cause) for each
The passage provides multiple 'illal: For bathroom: either impurity or dwelling of devils. For graveyard: resembling Jews and Christians. For camel resting places: devils or danger. For road: obstruction of public right. For dunghill and slaughterhouse: impurity. For Ka'ba top: not specified, but it is a place of honor.
Some 'illal are debated within the school, e.g., bathroom cause.
4
Note the exceptions
Graves of prophets are exempted from dislike. Sheep folds are places of blessing and not disliked. Also, a clean spot prepared for prayer in a graveyard removes the dislike according to some scholars.
The exception is based on the absence of the 'illa (tashabbuh) when the place is prepared.

في الحمام الخ.
Book of Prayer: (Restricting to the forehead in prostration without excuse by the nose leads to leaving the obligatory act of including the nose, which is prohibitively disliked. And) Prayer is disliked in the road because it occupies the right of the public and prevents them from passing. And in the bathroom and in the [makhraj] i.e. the impure place. And prayer is disliked in the graveyard and similar places because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade that... the house implies the establishment of dislike also if the image is under his feet or in his sitting place, and they have stated that there is no dislike in that. And similarly, the hadith of Jibril 'We do not enter a house in which there is a dog or an image' establishes it. It is answered that there is what specifies it, which is in Sahih Ibn Hibban: Jibril (peace be upon him) asked permission from the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he said: 'Enter.' He said: 'How can I enter when in your house there is a curtain with pictures? If you must do something, cut off their heads, or cut them into cushions, or make them into a carpet.' This suggests that there is no dislike for praying on a carpet that has images, even if they are in the place of prostration, unless it is said that it includes the form of resembling worshippers of them while standing and bowing, and it includes honoring them if he prostrates on them. And they differed regarding whether an image on dirhams or dinars prevents the entry of angels. Qadi 'Iyad held that it does not prevent, and the hadiths are specified. Al-Nawawi held that it prevents due to the generality. Then what is meant is the angels of mercy, not the recording angels, for they do not leave him except during intercourse and relieving oneself. And in Sharh al-Mishkat by Mulla 'Ali, quoting from al-Khattabi and Ibn al-Malik, they do not enter a house in which there is a dog or an image that it is prohibited to possess, such as dogs and images. As for what is not prohibited, like the dog of hunting, agriculture, and livestock, and images that are disrespected in carpets, cushions, and others, it does not prevent the angels from entering his house, and this does not contradict the prohibition of making images. He said: 'And it is disliked to restrict [to the forehead] etc.' And likewise its opposite according to Imam, and the two companions prohibit it except if there is an excuse with the forehead, as stated by al-Sayyid. He said: 'Prohibitively disliked' meaning dislike of prohibition, and it is indicated by his saying 'leaving the obligatory act of including the nose.' He said: 'Its occupation of the public right' and the preoccupation of the mind distracts from khushu, so one becomes occupied with creation from the truth. And because of this, some conditioned that it is in inhabited areas, not in the wilderness, as stated by Sharh al-Mishkat. He said: 'And in the bathroom' derived from hamim, which is hot water, and likewise the bathing place. And they differed on the cause: some said because each is a place for removing impurities and a drain for washings. According to this, if one washes a spot in the bathroom, it is not disliked, and Qadikhan followed this, and al-Kamal confirmed it in Zad al-Faqir. And some said the cause is that it is a dwelling of devils, for it is narrated that when Iblis descended to earth, he said: 'O Lord, make a house for me.' He said: 'The bathroom.' He said: 'Make a seat for me.' He said: 'The markets.' He said: 'Make companions for me.' He said: 'The poets.' He said: 'Make a book for me.' He said: 'Tattooing.' And it follows from this that prayer is disliked inside the bathroom whether that spot is washed or not. He said: 'And in the graveyard' with three possible vowellings of the ba, because it is resembling the Jews and Christians. He said: 'May Allah curse the Jews and Christians, they took the graves of their prophets as places of worship.' And it is the same whether it is above or behind or under what one is standing on. And the graves of the prophets (peace be upon them) are exempted, so prayer is absolutely not disliked in them, whether exhumed or not, as long as the grave is not in the direction of the qibla because they are alive in their graves. Do you not see that the resting place of Isma'il (peace be upon him) is in al-Hijr under the spout? Prayer is performed in seven places: in the dunghill, slaughterhouse, graveyard, highway, bathroom, camel resting places, and on top of the House of Allah. And one should not pray in the bathroom except out of necessity for fear of losing the time of prayer. And that between the Black Stone and Zamzam there is the grave of seventy prophets. Then that mosque is the best place to seek, unlike the graves of others, as stated in Sharh al-Mishkat and Zad al-Faqir. And prayer in the graveyard is disliked unless there is a place prepared for prayer with no impurity and no filth. Al-Halabi said: Because the dislike is due to resemblance, and that is absent then. And in al-Qahistani from Jana'iz al-Mudmarat: prayer towards the grave is not disliked unless it is in front of him such that if he prays the prayer of the humble, his sight falls upon it. He said: 'And the like' are what are mentioned in the hadith. He said: 'In the dunghill' (al-mazbala) with fatha and damma on the mim and ba, two dialects, and it is the place of dung i.e. manure. Sharh al-Mishkat said: and similar to it are all impurities. He said: 'And the slaughterhouse' (al-majzara) because it is a place of blood and dung. And some said the cause of dislike is fear of harm coming to him from the animals' aversion. It is with fatha, damma, and kasra on the zay. Sharh al-Mishkat said: the correct transmission and corrected copies have kasra on the zay, and that is what al-Jawhari restricted to, meaning that others are also permissible. He said: 'And the highway' (qari'at al-tariq) meaning the road that is beaten (maqru'a) by sandals, so the active participle is in the sense of the passive participle. He said: 'And camel resting places' (ma'atin al-ibil) intended here are their resting places absolutely. The cause is that they are from the devils. Yahya ibn Adam said: the prohibition is because camels are feared for their sudden assault, so one may be harmed. And the meaning of 'they are from the devils' is that their characteristics are from the characteristics of devils. In another hadith, 'they were created from the devils,' and Ibn Hibban interpreted it as they were created with them. And al-ma'atin in language are the places of camels where they kneel when they drink the first draught, then the trough is filled for them a second time, so they return from their thirst to the trough and drink the second draught, and this only occurs in hot days. When it becomes cold, there is no 'atn for camels. He was asked about prayer in sheep folds, and he said: 'Pray in them, for they were created with blessing.' And the prohibition of prayer in camel resting places is for tanzih, just as the command for sheep folds is for permissibility. And cattle folds are annexed to sheep folds, so prayer is not disliked in them. The full discussion is in al-'Ayni on Bukhari. And if the camels are not in their resting places, Ibn Malik said: prayer is still disliked in them because these places are places of impurity. If one prays without a prayer mat, the prayer is invalid unless the place is pure, or with a prayer mat it is disliked due to the foul smell. And Sharh al-Mishkat said about his saying 'pray in sheep folds': meaning on a prayer mat when there is necessity, or that the sheep owners used to clean the folds, so prayer was permitted in them for that reason. He said: And prayer is disliked in all places of devils, including the valley in which one slept through the Fajr prayer, and every place that has been afflicted with anger, like the land of Thamud, Babylon, and the dwellings of the people of Lut. I say: And from this it is known that prayer is disliked in churches and synagogues because of the images in them, so they become dwellings of devils, as stated by al-'Ayni in Sharh al-Bukhari in the section on mosques from the Book of Prayer. He said: 'And one should not pray in the bathroom except out of necessity etc.' The statement of Burhan al-Halabi: the first is that one should not pray in the bathroom, etc.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah is an expansion (sharh) of the matn that lists disliked (makruh) situations and places for prayer. The commentary provides the legal reasoning, proofs, and some intra-madhhab differences. The opening ruling states that restricting prostration to the forehead only (without including the nose) without an excuse is makruh tahrimi, because including the nose (ضم الأنف) is wajib. The commentator notes that the opposite case—beginning with the forehead and then adding the nose later—is permitted by Imam Abu Hanifa but prohibited by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) unless there is an excuse. The text then discusses images (suwar) and dogs in the context of a hadith that angels do not enter a house containing them, clarifying that this does not make prayer in such a house disliked if the image is underfoot or in a place that is disrespected. It also addresses the difference of opinion on whether images on coins prevent angelic entry. The main body of the passage covers the seven places mentioned in the hadith: dunghill, slaughterhouse, graveyard, highway, bathroom, camel resting places, and atop the Ka'ba. For each, the commentary explains the cause of dislike (علة الكراهة): for the bathroom, either because it is a place of impurity or a dwelling of devils; for the graveyard, due to resemblance to Jews and Christians, except for the graves of prophets; for camel resting places, because camels are associated with devils or due to danger, and the dislike is for tanzih (i.e., makruh tanzihi). Sheep folds are exempted and are considered a place of blessing. The passage also mentions that prayer is disliked in any place where devils gather or where divine wrath occurred, such as the valley of Thamud. It concludes with the ruling that prayer in the bathroom is only permissible out of necessity, such as fear of missing the prayer time.

Key Terms
المقبرة (al-maqbarah (with three possible vowellings)): Graveyard; a place where prayer is disliked due to resemblance to Jews and Christians, except for the graves of prophets.
الحمام (al-hammam): Bathroom (typically a public bath); prayer is disliked due to impurity or being a dwelling of devils.
معاطن الإبل (ma'atin al-ibil): Camel resting places; places where camels kneel to drink. Prayer is disliked because camels are associated with devils or due to danger.
كراهة تنزيه (karahah tanzihiyyah): Mild dislike; the act is valid but better avoided. Not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for prayer in a camel resting place when the camels are not present?
A) It is invalid because the place is impure.
B) It is makruh tahrimi.
C) It is makruh tanzih.
D) It is permissible without dislike if the place is clean.

Key Takeaway
Prayer in the seven locations and similar places is valid but mildly disliked (makruh tanzih); exceptions exist for prepared spots and necessity.

Prayer in Bathhouse and Others' Land: Rulings and Conditions
States allowance and prohibition of prayer in specific places

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer in bathhouse undressing areas and in another's land without permission, and apply the conditions that affect the ruling.

Core Idea
Prayer in bathhouse undressing areas is permissible; prayer in another's land without permission is disliked, with exceptions for presumed consent.

This lesson clarifies two related rulings from Hanafi fiqh: prayer in places that might be thought impure (like bathhouse undressing areas) and prayer on land owned by others. The Hanafi school relies on the general permissibility of pure places and the need to avoid causing displeasure to the owner. By studying this passage from al-Tahtawi's commentary, you will understand the nuanced conditions that determine whether an act is permissible or disliked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the two main acts discussed: prayer in the undressing area (mawdi' khal' al-thiyab) and prayer in another's land without permission. Note the initial ruling: 'no harm' (la ba's) for the former, and 'disliked' (makruh) for the latter.
The passage also discusses sub-scenarios for cultivated vs. uncultivated land and Muslim vs. non-Muslim owner.
2
Trace the dalil (evidence)
The evidence for the permissibility of prayer in the bathhouse area is 'li-itlaq al-hadith' (general applicability of a hadith). The commentator explains that there is no impurity in that place. Recognize that the proof is a general hadith, not a specific text.
Hanafis use general proofs unless a specific prohibition is established.
3
Analyze the conditions for the disliked ruling
For prayer in another's land, the ruling depends on conditions: ownership (Muslim or dhimmi), cultivation status, relationship with owner, and the owner's temperament. Identify each condition and how it changes the ruling.
The commentary systematically lists exceptions and justifications.
4
Understand the derivative rulings
Note the additional rulings: prayer on usurped land is valid but sinful, and prayer on a road depends on the owner of the road (Muslim vs. non-Muslim). These are logical extensions of the principles.
The road scenario shows the application of 'presumed pleasure' for Muslims.
5
Apply the rulings to new scenarios
Use the conditions you have identified to determine the ruling in novel situations, e.g., praying in a friend's backyard without permission vs. praying in a public park.
The key is to assess whether the owner would be displeased or if permission can be presumed.

Source Text

And it is disliked to pray in another's land without his permission. His statement: (And no) harm in praying etc., because there is no impurity in it, as in Qadi Khan. And because it is not part of the bathhouse due to what was mentioned earlier about derivation, as benefited by some experts. His statement: And it is disliked in another's land without his permission: that is, if it belongs to a dhimmi absolutely because he disapproves, or to a Muslim and it is cultivated or planted, and there is no friendship or affection between them, or its owner is ill-tempered. And if one is in a person's house, it is best to seek permission, otherwise there is no harm as in al-Fath. And in Mukhtarat al-Fatawa, praying in usurped land is permissible but one is punished for his injustice; what is between him and people, he is punished as in al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya. His statement: (He prays in it) because it is apparent that the owner is pleased with it since he gains reward without any effort from him. And there is no harm in praying in the road because it is the right of Muslims, and the disbeliever is similar as in al-Sharh. His statement: (He prays in the road) because the disbeliever is not pleased with it, as in al-Burhan. And the road is not exclusively for the disbeliever, as in al-Sharh.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage, from the commentary of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah, addresses rulings on permissible and disliked places for prayer. The matn states that there is no harm (la ba's) in praying where clothes are removed (such as undressing areas) and where the bath attendant sits. The commentator explains that this is because there is no impurity in such places, and he refutes the notion that these areas are part of the bathhouse itself through a linguistic argument about the derivation of the word 'hammam'. Then the matn states that it is makruh (disliked) to pray in another's land without the owner's permission. The commentary elaborates on the conditions: if the land belongs to a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject), it is disliked absolutely because they would not consent; if it is a Muslim's land and it is cultivated or planted, or if there is no friendship, or if the owner is ill-tempered, then it is also disliked. However, if one is in someone's house, it is better to ask permission; otherwise, it is not disliked. A derivative ruling is mentioned: praying on usurped land is valid but the person is sinful due to the injustice. The matn then gives a scenario: if one is forced to pray in another's uncultivated land, or on a road, the ruling depends on ownership: if the road is a Muslim's, one prays in it because the owner is presumed pleased (as it brings reward); if it is a disbeliever's, one should pray on the road (not inside the land) because the disbeliever is not pleased. The commentary clarifies that the road is not exclusively for the disbeliever.

Key Terms
موضع خلع الثياب (mawdi' khal' al-thiyab): The place where people remove their clothes, such as an undressing room in a bathhouse; considered pure in Hanafi law.
جلوس الحمامي (julus al-hammami): The sitting area of the bathhouse attendant; also considered pure for prayer.
أرض الغير (ard al-ghayr): Land belonging to another person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on praying in another's uncultivated land without permission if the owner is a Muslim?
A) It is prohibited (haram).
B) It is disliked (makruh) unless there is friendship or the owner is pleased.
C) It is permissible (mubah) because the land is pure.
D) It is recommended (mustahab) because it brings reward.

Key Takeaway
Prayer in bathhouse undressing areas is permissible, while prayer in another's land without permission is disliked unless the owner is Muslim and the land is uncultivated or friendship exists.
