Sutrah in Prayer: Size, Positioning, and Line Drawing
Commentary on sutrah requirements and line drawing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum size and positioning of the sutrah according to the Hanafi school, and explain the evidence and intra-school dispute regarding drawing a line as a substitute sutrah.

Core Idea
The sutrah must be at least a cubit high and finger-thick; if no object is available, a line may be drawn – this later view is relied upon.

In this passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, we explore the details of the sutrah in prayer. The text clarifies the minimum size, the recommended distance, and the proper positioning relative to the worshipper. It also addresses a key dispute among Hanafi scholars: whether drawing a line on the ground is permissible when no physical sutrah is available. This lesson will walk you through these rulings and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that using a sutrah is a sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah), not wajib. Omitting it does not invalidate prayer but loses reward.
The sutrah's purpose is to prevent passersby from crossing in front of the worshipper.
2
Determine the minimum size
The sutrah must be at least a cubit (dhira') in height and finger-thick. This ensures it is visible to an observer, fulfilling its function.
Some narrations allow even a fine object like a hair, but the relied-upon madhhab is the cubit and finger-thick.
3
Position the sutrah correctly
The worshipper should stand close, within about three cubits. The sutrah should be placed to one side (preferably right eyebrow), not directly in front.
Positioning helps prevent the worshipper from leaning forward and avoids direct confrontation.
4
Handle the case of no object
If no physical sutrah is available, early Hanafi scholars prohibited drawing a line, but later scholars permitted it based on the hadith: 'If one does not have a stick, let him draw a line.'
The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is permissibility, as preferred by al-Kamal due to the authentic hadith.

It is an error, and it was interpreted as a cubit and above (in finger-thickness) and that is its minimum, because what is less than that may not appear to the viewer, so the purpose is not achieved. And the Sunnah is to be close to it due to the Prophet's saying: When one of you prays facing a sutrah, let him be close to it, so that Satan does not cut his prayer. And he should place it towards one of his eyebrows and not face it directly. As narrated from al-Miqdad: I never saw the Messenger of Allah pray facing a pillar or a tree except that he placed it to his right or left eyebrow, not facing it directly, but rather he inclined from it. And if he does not find something to erect, a group of early scholars prohibited the line, while later scholars permitted it because the Sunnah is more deserving of following, due to what is narrated in the Sunan from the Prophet: If one does not have a stick, then let him draw a line. So it becomes apparent in general, because the purpose is to gather the mind by tying the imagination so that it does not scatter, and he makes it either lengthwise like a wooden stake planted in front of him, or as they also said, he makes it crosswise like a crescent, and if the ground is hard, he throws what he has lengthwise as if it were planted then fell. From al-Ayni on al-Bukhari: his saying: and it was interpreted as a cubit... The narrators of the Sunan reported from Ata: the rear part of the saddle is a cubit and above. So in Ghayat al-Bayan. His saying: (in finger-thickness) is contrary to the madhhab, so there is no limit, because al-Hakim narrated from Abu Hurayra marfu'an: A sutrah suffices of the size of the rear of the saddle, even if as fine as a hair. So in al-Bahr from al-Bada'i. And in al-Qahistani: wells, rivers, and small ponds are not valid sutrahs in the most correct view, and the large ones like a road are not a sutrah because they are likely to have passersby. In al-Ayni: the large river is not a sutrah like a road, and similarly the large pond. His saying: (and that is its minimum) meaning the minimum of what is planted. And it is apparent that this amount is considered. His saying: (he does not cut) is jussive in the answer of an implied conditional: if he is close to it, Satan does not cut his prayer. The reason for cutting is that if he is far, the passerby thinks there is no sutrah, so he passes within it, and he pushes him, and perhaps the pushing involves much action, spoiling the prayer. His saying: (and he places it towards one of his eyebrows) and the right is better. His saying: (a group of early scholars prohibited the line) among them the author of al-Hidaya. His saying: (and later scholars permitted it) and al-Kamal preferred it due to the report, and even if al-Bada'i considered the hadith shadhdh and al-Nawawi weakened it, its authenticity has been established by Imam Ahmad and Ibn Hibban and others. And even if it is not beneficial, there is no harm in it, with the much practice on the hadith, which is permissible to act upon in such matters. His saying: (so it becomes apparent) it is better to say: so it benefits in general. His saying: (by tying the imagination) i.e., the imagination of the worshipper, his imaginative power, so his thought is reduced; unlike when it is missing, then he follows the sight and thought increases. His saying: (like a planted wooden stake) so it becomes similar to the shadow of the sutrah. His saying: (like a crescent) and it is said circular like a mihrab. And the imams analogized the line to the prayer mat spread out, and it is a more fitting analogy because the worshipper is more effective in repelling... Thus, al-Faqih Abu Ja'far chose it, and Hisham said: I performed Hajj with Abu Yusuf, and he would place a whip in front of him. And the sutrah of the imam is a sutrah for those behind him, because the Prophet prayed at al-Abtah towards a small spear that was fixed for him, and the people had no sutrah. The 'anaza is a stick with an iron tip at its bottom.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement (hashiya) on the rulings of the sutrah (screen) in prayer. The commentator opens by explaining the minimum size of the sutrah: it must be at least a cubit (dhira') in height and finger-thick. This is the minimum because anything less may not be visible to the observer and thus fails the purpose of preventing people from passing in front of the worshipper. The Sunnah is to stand close to the sutrah, with a distance not exceeding three cubits, based on the hadith: 'When one of you prays facing a sutrah, let him be close to it, so that Satan does not cut his prayer.' The commentator explains that if one is far, a passerby may think there is no sutrah and walk within it, causing the worshipper to push them, potentially with much action that spoils the prayer. Next, the sutrah should be placed towards one eyebrow, preferably the right, not directly in front, following the practice of the Prophet as narrated by al-Miqdad. If no object is available, the majority of later scholars permit drawing a line on the ground, while some early scholars like the author of al-Hidayah prohibited it. The later scholars prefer it due to the hadith: 'If one does not have a stick, let him draw a line.' The hadith is considered authentic by Ahmad and Ibn Hibban, and even if weak, acting upon it is permissible because it is a matter of practice. The purpose of the line is to occupy the worshipper's mind and prevent distraction. The commentator also notes that large rivers, ponds, and roads are not valid sutrahs because they are likely to have passersby. The imam's sutrah serves as a sutrah for those behind him, based on the practice of the Prophet at al-Abtah.

Key Terms
السترة (al-sutrah): An object placed in front of the worshipper to prevent people from passing in front of him during prayer.
الخط (al-khatt): A line drawn on the ground as a substitute for a physical sutrah.
آخرة الرحل (akhirat al-rahil): The rear part of a camel saddle, used as a measure for the sutrah's height (approx. a cubit).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi position regarding drawing a line as a sutrah?
A) It is prohibited because it is an innovation.
B) It is permissible and recommended when no object is available.
C) It is only allowed in mosques, not elsewhere.
D) It is equivalent to using a physical object in reward.

Key Takeaway
The sutrah is a confirmed sunnah with specific conditions; if no object is available, drawing a line is permissible and recommended based on authentic hadith.

Witr: Three Rak'ahs with One Taslim
Ruling on number and structure of Witr with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number and structure of Witr prayer and identify the hadith proof and consensus supporting it.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib as three continuous rak'ahs with a single taslim; one rak'ah is insufficient.

Witr is a unique prayer with a specific structure. The Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's practice and companion consensus, insists on three rak'ahs performed continuously with one salam. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the refutation of the one-rak'ah practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on Witr's structure
Read the matn statement: 'it is three rak'ahs, with one taslim'. This is the core Hanafi position.
The term 'bi-taslimat' means a single salam at the end.
2
Locate the hadith proof
Find the hadith cited: the Prophet used to pray Witr with three rak'ahs, not making taslim except at the end. Note the authentication by al-Hakim.
The hadith is considered reliable and on the condition of Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the opposition to one rak'ah
See the narrations from Umar and Ibn Mas'ud condemning praying Witr as a single rak'ah (the 'butaira' practice). This reinforces the three-rak'ah requirement.
The term 'butaira' means 'cut off' or 'mutilated'.
4
Note the consensus and fiqh consequences
The salaf agreed on three rak'ahs. The ruling is wajib; if a group abandons it, the imam disciplines them.
Witr is not fard but wajib, so omission does not invalidate iman but requires correction.

برفعه يديه عند صلاة، يصح من وهي الوتر فصلوها فيما بين العشاء، إلا صلاة الصبح قوله : (وعلى) أي في قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم الوتر واجب على كل مسلم وأجمعوا على أنه لا يصلي بدون نية الوتر، وأنه لا قعود ولا على الدابة إلا من عذر وعلى وجوب القراءة في جميع ركعاته، ولو اجتمع قوم على تركه أدبهم الإمام وحبسهم فإن لم يصلوه قاتلهم كذا في النهر عن التجنيس، والمراد بوجوب القراءة إفتراضها، أو يحمل على خصوص الفاتحة والسورة أفاده السيد قوله : (وكميته الخ) لا حاجة إلى التصريح بها لعلمه مما ذكره المصنف . قوله : (ثلاث ركعات) بالتحريك، وقد تسكن قوله : (كان) يوتر بثلاث وهذا مذهب الفقهاء السبعة وروى ابن أبي شيبة في مصنفه عن الحسن البصري قال: أجمع السلف على أنّ الوتر ثلاث لا يسلم إلا في آخرهن، وهو مذهب أبي بكر وعمر والعبادلة وأبي هريرة روي أن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه رأى سعيداً يوتر بركعة فقال : ما هذه البتيراء تشفعها أو لأؤذبنك اهـ، وروي أن سعد بن أبي وقاص أوتر بركعة فقال له عبد الله بن مسعود ما هذه البتيراء ما أجزأت ركعة قط، وروي أنه حلف على ذلك أهـ كذا في الشرح قوله : (وقال على شرط الشيخين شرط البخاري أنه لا بد من تحقق اللقي بين الراوي، ومن روى عنه وشرط مسلم إمكان اللقي فكلما تحقق شرط البخاري تحقق شرط مسلم، ولا عكس، ومسلم تلميذ البخاري قال : الدارقطني لولا البخاري ما راح مسلم، ولا جاء . قوله: (وفي حديث عائشة) رواه أصحاب السنن الأربعة وابن حبان في صحيحه والحاكم في مستدركه من طريق عبد العزيز بن جريج عنها قوله فيعمل به في بعض الأوقات) أصله للكمال، وتمام كلامه كما في الشرح، ولكن قال :اسحق أصح شيء ورد في قراءته صلى الله عليه وسلم في الوتر سبح وقل يا أيها الكافرون، وقل هو الله أحد، وزيادة المعوذتين أنكرها الإمام أحمد، ويحيى بن معين اهـ فهذا سر اقتصار أئمتنا على الإخلاص في الثالثة قوله : (إلا إذا قضاه) أي عند الناس بدليل ما بعده قوله (برفعه) متعلق بیری .
Book of Prayer. And the word 'truth' and 'upon' indicate obligation. And its quantity: it is three rak'ahs, which must be performed with one taslim, because the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, used to pray Witr with three rak'ahs, not making the taslim except at the end of them. Al-Hakim authenticated it and said it is on the condition of the two Shaykhs. And he recites, as an obligation, in each rak'ah al-Fatiha and a surah, because it is narrated that he, peace be upon him, recited in the first, after al-Fatiha, 'Glorify the name of your Lord Most High', and in the second 'Say: O disbelievers', and in the third 'Say: He is Allah, One', and he performed qunut before ruku'. In the hadith of Aisha, she said he recited in the third 'Say: He is Allah, One' and the Mu'awwidhatayn. So one acts on it at some times, acting on both hadiths, not in an obligatory manner. And he sits, as an obligation, at the end of the first two rak'ahs, following what is transmitted, and confines himself to the tashahhud due to the semblance of obligatory nature. And he does not recite the opening supplication when standing for the third, because it is not the beginning of another prayer. When he finishes reciting the surah in the third, he raises his hands parallel to his ears as we presented, except when he makes it up, so that he is not seen as negligent in it by raising his hands at prayer. It is valid from... And the Witr prayer is performed between Isha and the break of dawn, except for the Fajr prayer. His statement: 'And upon' in his saying, peace be upon him, 'Witr is obligatory upon every Muslim'. And they agreed that it is not prayed without intention of Witr, and that there is no sitting nor riding except due to an excuse, and upon the obligation of recitation in all its rak'ahs. If a group agrees to abandon it, the Imam disciplines them and imprisons them; if they do not pray it, he fights them. This is from al-Nahr from al-Tajnīs. And the meaning of obligation of recitation is its being fard, or it is carried specifically on the Fatiha and surah as stated by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'and its quantity' etc., there is no need to specify it because it is known from what the author mentioned. His statement: 'three rak'ahs' with tashdīd of rā', and it may be silent. His statement: 'used to pray Witr with three' is the school of the seven jurists. Ibn Abi Shayba narrated in his Musannaf from al-Hasan al-Basri that he said: The salaf agreed that Witr is three, not making taslim except at the end. It is the school of Abu Bakr, Umar, the 'Abdā'ila (ibn Mas'ud, ibn Umar, etc.), and Abu Hurayra. It is narrated that Umar saw Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab praying Witr with one rak'ah and said: 'What is this cut-tail? Make it even or I will punish you.' And it is narrated that Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas prayed Witr with one rak'ah and Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: 'What is this cut-tail? One rak'ah is never sufficient.' And it is narrated that he swore to that. This is in the Sharh. His statement: 'and he said on the condition of the two Shaykhs' – the condition of Bukhari is that meeting between the narrator and the one he narrates from must be verified, while Muslim's condition is the possibility of meeting. Thus whenever Bukhari's condition is met, Muslim's condition is met, not vice versa. Muslim was a student of Bukhari. al-Daraqutni said: 'If not for Bukhari, Muslim would not have gone nor come.' His statement: 'and in the hadith of Aisha' – it was narrated by the four Sunan compilers, Ibn Hibban in his Sahih, and al-Hakim in his Mustadrak from the route of Abd al-Aziz ibn Jurayj from her. His statement: 'so one acts on it at some times' – its origin from al-Kamal, and the complete text as in the Sharh. But Ishaq said: 'The most authentic thing reported of his recitation in Witr is: Glorify, Say: O disbelievers, and Say: He is Allah, One. The addition of the Mu'awwidhatayn was denied by Imam Ahmad and Yahya ibn Ma'in.' This is the reason our imams confined themselves to al-Ikhlas in the third. His statement: 'except when he makes it up' i.e., in the eyes of the people, as indicated by what follows. His statement: 'by raising them' is attached to 'see'.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed rulings for performing Witr prayer according to the Hanafi school. The matn states that Witr is three rak'ahs with a single taslim, and the commentary supports this with hadith from the Prophet and consensus of the Companions. Recitation of Fatiha and a surah in each rak'ah is wajib; the prescribed surahs are Sabbih, Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun, and Qul huwa Allahu ahad. Qunut is before ruku'. One sits for tashahhud after two rak'ahs, recites only tashahhud, and does not recite istiftah when standing for the third. Raising hands at the time of qunut is sunnah unless the prayer is being made up. The passage also addresses the obligation of recitation and the consequences of abandoning Witr as a community. Later parts mention the conditions of the hadith narrators and a discussion about reciting the Mu'awwidhatayn as optional.

Key Terms
بتسليمة (bi-taslimat): With a single taslim at the end of the three rak'ahs.
البتيراء (al-butaira): A term used by the Companions to describe a single rak'ah of Witr, meaning 'cut off' or 'mutilated'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many rak'ahs does the Hanafi school require for Witr and with how many taslims?
A) Two rak'ahs with one taslim.
B) Three rak'ahs with one taslim.
C) One rak'ah with one taslim.
D) Three rak'ahs with a taslim after each rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
Witr is wajib as three continuous rak'ahs with one salam; one rak'ah is invalid.

Recitation and Qunut in Witr
Specific recitations and qunut in Witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to specify the wajib recitations and the sunnah recitations in Witr, explain the placement of qunut, and identify the ruling on raising hands and istiftah.

Core Idea
Recite Sabbih, Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun, and Qul huwa Allahu ahad; qunut before ruku' is wajib; no istiftah in third rak'ah.

Witr has specific recitations that distinguish it from other prayers. The Hanafi school prescribes certain surahs for each rak'ah and requires qunut in the third rak'ah before ruku'. This lesson details these elements and clarifies optional additions like the Mu'awwidhatayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recitation in each rak'ah
Read the text: in the first rak'ah after Fatiha, recite 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la'; in the second, 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun'; in the third, 'Qul huwa Allahu ahad'. This is the sunnah.
Recitation of a surah after Fatiha is wajib; these specific surahs are sunnah muakkadah.
2
Understand the qunut placement and its ruling
Qunut is performed in the third rak'ah before ruku'. The text says 'wa qanta qabla al-ruku''. It is wajib; if omitted, sajdah al-sahw is required.
Qunut is a special supplication.
3
Note the optional recitation of Mu'awwidhatayn
The hadith of Aisha mentions that the Prophet recited Qul huwa Allahu ahad and the Mu'awwidhatayn in the third rak'ah. The commentator says to act on this occasionally, not as an obligation.
This allows flexibility without changing the sunnah.
4
Recognize the absence of istiftah in the third rak'ah
When standing for the third rak'ah, one does not recite the opening supplication (istiftah) because it is not a new prayer.
Istiftah is only at the beginning of the entire prayer.

Source Text

The Qunut Supplication: Lexical Analysis and Hanafi Ruling on Tawbah
Explanation of the qunut du'a with lexical and legal analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the lexical meanings of key phrases in the qunut du'a and explain the Hanafi ruling on the conditions of tawbah when it involves a human right.

Core Idea
Repentance from a sin against another requires their forgiveness; without it, tawbah is incomplete.

This lesson unpacks the qunut du'a transmitted from Ibn Mas'ud, focusing on the phrase 'wa natubu ilayka' (and we repent to You). The commentary provides a precise definition of tawbah and highlights a critical fiqh ruling: if the sin involves a human right, seeking pardon from the wronged person is obligatory for valid repentance. We will work through the lexical analysis and derive the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure of the qunut du'a
The supplication includes multiple requests: help, guidance, forgiveness, repentance, belief, reliance. We parse each phrase to understand its lexical and legal meaning.
Focus on the sequence and how each term builds on the previous.
2
Analyze the definition of tawbah
The text defines tawbah linguistically and legally. Break down the three components: regret, immediate cessation, resolution not to return. Note the addition when human rights are involved.
Regret is identified as the greatest pillar (rukn).
3
Examine the ruling on human rights
The text states 'la budda min musamahatihi wa irda'ihi' – it is necessary to seek pardon and satisfaction. Understand the obligation and its implications for financial and non-financial rights.
If restitution is impossible, charity in equivalent amount is required for financial rights.
4
Consider the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some later Hanafi scholars hold that repentance is valid without immediate restitution, treating the obligation as a debt. The mufta bihi is the majority view requiring immediate action.
This ikhtilaf does not affect the basic conditions of tawbah but affects when it is considered complete.
5
Summarize the broader fiqh implications
Connect the ruling to the distinction between haqq Allah (rights of Allah) and haqq al-'abd (rights of humans). Sins against the latter require active reparation beyond internal repentance.
This distinction is fundamental in Hanafi fiqh for many rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باللفظ الذي روي عن ابن مسعود أن يقول اللهم) أي يا الله إنا نستعينك) أي نطلب منك الإعانة على طاعتك ونستهديك) أي نطلب منك الهداية لما يرضيك (ونستغفرك) نطلب منك ستر عيوبنا فلا تفضحنا بها ونتوب إليك) التوبة الرجوع عن الذنب وشرعاً الندم على ما مضى من الذنب والإقلاع عنه في الحال والعزم على ترك العود في المستقبل تعظيماً لأمر الله تعالى فإن تعلق به حق لآدمي فلا بد من مسامحته وإرضائه ( ونؤمن) أي نصدق معتقدين بقلوبنا ناطقين بلساننا فقلنا آمنا (بك) وبما جاء من عندك وبملائكتك، وكتبك ورسلك وباليوم الآخر وبالقدر خيره وشره ( ونتوكل) أي نعتمد (عليك) بتفويض أمورنا إليك لعجزنا وهو مائة، كذلك ذكرها الجلال السيوطي في الدر المنثور بألفاظ مختلفة. قوله: (أن يقول اللهم الخ) ذكر السيوطي أن دعاء القنوت من جملة الذي أنزله الله على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وكانا سورتين كل سورة ببسملة وفواصل إحداهما تسمى سورة الخلع وهي بسم ا الله الرحمن الرحيم اللهم إنا نستعينك إلى قوله من يكفرك والأخرى تسمى سورة الحقد وهي بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم اللهم إياك نعبد إلى ملحق، وقد اختلفت الصحابة في نسخهما وكتبهما أبي في مصحفه فعدة سور القرآن عنده وست عشرة سورة. قوله : أي) نطلب منك الهداية لما يرضيك) المراد من الهداية الوصول لا الدلالة فقط . قوله : (ستر عيوبنا) الأولى ستر ذنوبنا لأنّ العيب قد لا يكون ذنباً كالعور، والشلل اللهم إلا أن يقال المراد ما يعيب الشارع عليه، والستر إما بالمحو من الصحيفة أو بعدم المؤاخذة به وإن بقي فيها والأول أرجح. قوله : (فلا تفضحنا بفتح التاء والحاء المهملة. قوله: (وشرعاً الندم) وهو أعظم أركانها قوله والإقلاع عنه في الحال) أي إن كانت آلة الفعل حاضرة كأن تاب عن السكر وآلته بين يديه فيريقه ويبعد آلته عنه . قوله: (والعزم على ترك العود) أفاد العارف ابن عربي أن هذا الشرط لا يلزم لأنه غيب فالأولى فيه التسليم، وفيه أن المغيب هو العود فلا ينافي طلب العزم على عدمه في التوبة. قوله: (فلا بد من مسامحته وإرضائه أي برد الظلامة إليه إن أمكنه وإن لم يمكنه تصدق بقدرها إن كانت من الأموال، وقال بعضهم أن التوبة تصح عنها في المستقبل، ويكون ما عليه كالديون. قوله: (ناطقين بلساننا هذا جرى فيه على أن الإيمان قول وعمل ونسب إلى الإمام أو هو بيان لشرطه الدنيوي الذي تجري عليه الأحكام الظاهرة قوله: (فقلنا آمنا بك الخ لما كان الإيمان به تعالى لا يتم إلا بالإيمان بما ذكر بعد قال ذلك . قوله : (وبما جاء . عندك) فيه أنه لا يعم الأنبياء فإن الإيمان بهم لازم. من ما يخرج عن الكتب والقدر وقد ذكرهما بعد قوله (ورسلك) المراد بهم قوله: (وباليوم الآخر ) أي بوقوعه. قوله : ( وبالقدر خيره وشره القدر إيجاد الله تعالى الأشياء على وفق ما أراده تعالى وكله من الله تعالى وهو من هذه الجهة جميل، وإنما يقبح باكتساب العبد ونسبته إليه قوله : (بتفويض) الباء للتصوير. قوله : (لعجزنا) أي عن جلب نفعنا ودفع شرنا بصرف جميع ما أنعمت ونثني عليك الخير (كله أي نمدحك بكل خير مقرين بجميع آلائك افضالاً منك (نشكرك) به من الجوارح إلى ما خلقته لأجله سبحانك لك الحمد لا نحصي ثناء عليك أنت كما أثنيت على نفسك ولا) نكفرك أي لا نجحد نعمة لك علينا، ولا نضيفها إلى غيرك الكفر نقيض الشكر، وأصله الستر يقال كفر النعمة إذا لم يشكرها كأنه سترها بجحوده وقولهم كفرت فلاناً على حذف مضاف والأصل كفرت بنعمته ومنه لا نكفرك ونخلع بثبوت حرف العطف أي نلقي ونطرح ونزيل ربقة الكفر من أعناقنا، وربقة كل ما لا يرضيك يقال خلع الفرس رسنه ألقاه ( ونترك) أي نفارق (من يفجرك) بجحده نعمتك وعبادته غيرك نتحاشى عنه وعن صفته بأن نفرضه عدما تنزيهاً لجنابك إذ كل ذرة في الوجود شاهدة بأنك المنعم المتفضل الموجود المستحق لجميع المحامد الفرد المعبود، والمخالف لهذا هو الشقي المطرود
With the wording reported from Ibn Mas'ud that he says: 'O Allah (i.e., O God), we seek Your help (i.e., we ask You for assistance in obeying You), and we seek guidance from You (i.e., we ask You for guidance to what pleases You), and we seek Your forgiveness (we ask You to conceal our faults so that You do not expose us with them), and we repent to You (repentance is turning away from sin, and legally it is regret over past sin, desisting from it immediately, and resolving not to return to it in the future, out of reverence for Allah Almighty; if it involves a right of a human, then it is necessary to seek his pardon and satisfaction), and we believe (i.e., we affirm with our hearts, speaking with our tongues, so we said 'we believe') in You, and in what has come from You, and in Your angels, Your books, Your messengers, the Last Day, and in predestination, its good and evil, and we rely (i.e., we depend) upon You (by entrusting our affairs to You because of our inability), and it is one hundred. Likewise, al-Jalal al-Suyuti mentioned it in al-Durr al-Manthur with different wordings. His saying: 'that he says O Allah, etc.' Al-Suyuti mentioned that the qunut supplication is among what Allah sent down upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), and they were two surahs, each surah with a basmalah and verses; one is called Surat al-Khal' i.e., 'In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful: O Allah, we seek Your help...' up to His saying 'whoever disbelieves in You'; and the other is called Surat al-Haqd i.e., 'In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful: O Allah, You alone we worship...' up to an appendix. The Companions differed regarding their abrogation, and Ubayy wrote them in his mushaf; thus the number of surahs of the Quran according to him is one hundred and sixteen. His saying: 'i.e., we ask You for guidance to what pleases You' means by guidance the reaching, not just indication. His saying: 'conceal our faults' - the preferred wording is 'conceal our sins' because a fault may not be a sin like being one-eyed or paralyzed, unless it is said what the Lawgiver deems blameworthy. Concealment is either by erasing from the record or by not taking to account even if it remains, and the first is more preponderant. His saying: 'so that You do not expose us' - with fath on the ta and ha. His saying: 'and legally it is regret' - and it is the greatest of its pillars. His saying: 'and desisting from it immediately' i.e., if the means of the act are present, like if he repents from drinking and the vessel is before him, he pours it out and removes the vessel from himself. His saying: 'and resolving not to return' - the gnostic Ibn Arabi stated that this condition is not necessary because it is the unseen; so the better view is to submit (to Allah). It is said that what is unseen is the return, so it does not negate seeking resolve not to do it in repentance. His saying: 'so it is necessary to seek his pardon and satisfaction' i.e., by returning the usurpation to him if possible; if not possible, he gives charity in its amount if it is from wealth. Some said that repentance from it is valid in the future, and what is upon him is like debts. His saying: 'speaking with our tongues' - this runs on the view that faith is speech and action, and it is attributed to the Imam, or it is an explanation of its worldly condition by which the apparent rulings are applied. His saying: 'so we said we believe in You, etc.' - because belief in Him Almighty is not complete except by belief in what was mentioned afterwards, he said that. His saying: 'and in what has come from You' - therein is that it does not include the prophets, because belief in them is necessary. From what goes out from the books and predestination, and he mentioned them after His saying 'Your messengers'. His saying: 'and the Last Day' i.e., its occurrence. His saying: 'and in predestination, its good and evil' - predestination is Allah Almighty's bringing things into existence according to what He willed; everything from Allah is beautiful from this aspect; it is only ugly by the acquisition of the servant and its attribution to him. His saying: 'by entrusting' - the ba is for making an image. His saying: 'because of our inability' i.e., to bring benefit and repel harm. 'To spend all what You have bestowed, and we praise You with all good (i.e., we praise You with every good, acknowledging all Your bounties as favors from You), we thank You with the limbs for what You created them for; glory be to You, praise is Yours; we cannot count praise upon You; You are as You have praised Yourself; and we do not disbelieve in You (i.e., we do not deny any favor of Yours upon us, nor do we attribute it to other than You; disbelief is the opposite of gratitude; its origin is concealment; it is said he disbelieved the blessing when he did not thank it, as if he concealed it by denial; and their saying 'I disbelieved so-and-so' is with ellipsis of the object, the original is 'I disbelieved in his blessing'; from this is 'we do not disbelieve in You'), and we cast off (with the letter of conjunction, i.e., we throw and discard and remove the rope of disbelief from our necks; and the rope is everything that does not please You; it is said the horse cast off its halter meaning it threw it), and we abandon (i.e., we separate from) whoever disbelieves in You (by denying Your favor and worshipping other than You; we avoid him and his attribute by assuming him non-existent, to exalt Your court, for every atom in existence testifies that You are the Benefactor, the Bestower, the Existing, the Deserving of all praises, the Unique, the Worshipped; and the one who opposes this is the wretched, expelled).'
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage is a line-by-line commentary (sharh) on the qunut supplication (dua al-qunut) used in witr prayer, as transmitted from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). The commentator (al-Tahtawi) explains each phrase lexically and legally, integrating fiqh definitions and occasional rulings.

The commentary begins by clarifying the meaning of 'nasta'inuka' (we seek Your help) as requesting assistance in obedience. For 'nastahdeeka' (we seek guidance), the author specifies that the intended guidance is actual reaching (wusul) of the goal, not mere direction (dalalah). In 'nastaghfiruka' (we seek Your forgiveness), the primary meaning is concealment of sins, not faults, since faults like physical defects are not sins. The concealment is understood as erasing from the record or not punishing, with erasing being more preponderant.

The definition of 'tawbah' (repentance) is given: linguistically 'returning from sin,' legally it requires regret (nadam), immediate cessation (if the means of sin are present), and resolution not to return. The author notes that Ibn Arabi questioned the necessity of the resolution condition due to the unseen nature of the future, but the author refutes this by distinguishing the unseen act from the present intention. A crucial ruling is stated: if repentance involves a human right (haqq adami), it is not valid without seeking forgiveness and satisfaction from the wronged person; if the wrong is financial and restitution is impossible, charity in equivalent amount is required.

On 'iman' (faith), the text presents the Hanafi position that faith comprises both speech (qawl) and action ('amal), though this may refer to the worldly legal condition (shart dunyawi) for applying rulings. Belief in Allah necessitates belief in His messengers, books, angels, the Last Day, and predestination. The commentary on 'qadr' (predestination) clarifies that all creation from Allah is good; evil arises from the servant's acquisition (kasb).

The second half of the passage (from 'sarf jami' ma an'amta') continues the qunut with 'nuthni 'alayka bi'l-khayr' (we praise You with all good), emphasizing that praise is for all blessings as favors (ifdal), not obligation. 'Nashkuruka' (we thank You) uses limbs for their intended purpose. The phrase 'la nakfuruka' (we do not disbelieve in You) explains kufr as the opposite of shukr, meaning denial. 'Nakhla'u' (we cast off) is explained as removing the 'ribqah' (rope) of disbelief, meaning anything displeasing to Allah, using the metaphor of a horse casting off its halter. Finally, 'natruku man yafjuruka' (we abandon whoever disbelieves in You) indicates total dissociation, even to the point of considering them non-existent to exalt Allah. The passage concludes by stating that the person who opposes Allah's oneness is 'wretched and expelled' (shaqi matrud).

Throughout, the commentary reflects the Hanafi school's precise definitions, such as the distinction between faults and sins, and the emphasis on repentance involving human rights. The mention of al-Suyuti's view that the qunut was revealed as two surahs is a textual note but does not affect the fiqh ruling.

Key Terms
التوبة (al-tawbah): Linguistically: returning from sin. Legally: regret over past sin, immediate desistance, and resolve not to return, done out of reverence for Allah. If it involves a human right, seeking pardon and satisfaction is necessary.
الإيمان (al-iman): Faith is affirmation with the heart (tasdiq) and utterance with the tongue (qawl); it includes both speech and action. The text mentions this as a condition for applying worldly rulings.
القدر (al-qadr): Predestination: Allah's creation of things according to His will. All from Allah is good; evil is attributed to the servant's acquisition (kasb).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what must a person do if their repentance involves a human right (haqq adami) from financial wrongdoing?
A) Simply regret the sin and resolve not to return to it.
B) Return the wrongfully taken property or its value if possible; if not, give charity in the amount.
C) Confess to the wronged person and ask for forgiveness after performing two rak'ahs of prayer.
D) The repentance is valid without any further action because the right is a debt that can be paid later.

Key Takeaway
Repentance from sins against Allah requires internal regret, cessation, and resolve; but sins against others demand active seeking of forgiveness or restitution.

Rulings on Qunut in Witr: Salawat and Recitation
Commentary on the opening supplication and salawat in qunut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sending salawat in qunut and explain the conditions for loud versus quiet recitation.

Core Idea
Sending salawat in qunut is recommended, and quiet recitation is the sunnah unless teaching requires loudness.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explores the qunut supplication in witr, emphasizing the necessary balance of fear and hope. The commentary then turns to two practical fiqh questions: the ruling on sending salawat upon the Prophet during qunut, and whether the imam should recite aloud or quietly. These rulings are supported by hadith and the practice of 'Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fiqh issues
Extract the two main rulings discussed: sending salawat in qunut and the volume of recitation (jahr vs. ikhfa').
These are separate but related issues in the same passage.
2
Extract the proofs
Locate the hadith of Zayd ibn Kharijah (salawat wording) and the precedent of 'Umar reciting aloud for teaching.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Nasa'i; 'Umar's practice is narrated in historical accounts.
3
Determine the Hanafi position
State that salawat is mustahab (sunnah muakkadah), quiet recitation is preferred (al-sahih), but loudness is allowed for teaching.
Al-Tahtawi uses 'al-asahh' for follower reciting like imam, and 'huwa al-sahih' for quiet recitation.
4
Note the tarjih
Identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) positions: salawat is recommended, quiet is the default, and the imam may recite aloud for educational purposes.
This tarjih is based on the practice of 'Umar and the need for learning.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة أمن المكر كفر كالقنوط من الرحمة وجمع بين الرجاء والخوف لأن شأن القادر أن يرجى نواله ويخاف نكاله وفي الحديث لا يجتمعان في قلب عبد مؤمن إلا أعطاه الله ما يرجوه وآمنه مما يخاف فلا نعامك علينا بالإيمان وتوفيقك للعمل بالأركان ممتثلين لأمرك لا مقتصرين على القلب واللسان، إذ هو طمع الكاذبين ذوي البهتان نعتقد ونقول (إن هذابك الجد) أي الحق، وهو بكسر الجيم اتفاقاً بمعنى الحق، وهو ثابت في مراسيل أبي داود، فلا يلتفت لمن قال أنه لا يقول الجدّ (بالكفار (ملحق أي لا حق بهم بكسر الحاء أفصح، وقيل : بفتحها يعني أن الله سبحانه وتعالى ملحقه بهم ولما روى النسائي بإسناد حسن إن في حديث القنوت وصلى الله على النبي صلينا عليه صلى الله عليه (و) على (آله وسلم) كما عن علته، معناه أنه يوصل إليه بسبب استرساله في المعاصي. قال تعالى: فلا يأمن مكر الله إلا القوم الخاسرون). قوله : (كالقنوط من الرحمة) أي اليأس منها والجزم بأنه من أهل العذاب فإنه يؤدي إلى تقليل العمل وإنكار الرحمة وفيه ما تقدم في الأمن قال تعالى : إنه لا يأس من روح الله إلا القوم الكافرون). قوله : أني) يرجى (نواله أي إنعامه ونكاله عقابه. قوله: (لا يجتمعان الخ) قد علمت أنّ الرجاء لا يتحقق إلا مع الأعمال الصالحة وإلا فهو طمع. قوله : (بالأركان) أي الأعضاء قوله : (ممتثلين لأمرك حال مؤكدة قوله : (لا) مقتصرين على القلب واللسان) بأن يرجو بقلبه، أو ينطق بلسانه من غير عمل الأركان قوله : (ذوي البهتان) هو الكذب، وفسره في القاموس بأن يقول على الشخص ما لم يفعل قوله : (نعتقد ونقول) معلول مؤخر وهو قوله : فلإنعامك علينا بالإيمان، ولا شك أن هذا الإعتقاد، والقول علته الإنعام بالإيمان قوله : (بكسر الحاء) قال النووي: هذا هو المشهور، وقال الجزري : هكذا روينا. قوله: (وقيل بفتحها) قاله ابن قتيبة ،وغيره ونص الجوهري على أنه صواب. قوله: (وصلى الله على النبي) هذا هو الذي رواه النسائي فقط بدون، وعلى آله وسلم كما يفهم من الشرح. قوله : ( صلينا) معلول لقوله، ولما روى النسائي. قوله : (وعلى آله وسلم) في الواقعات بعد ما ذكر اختيار الفقيه أبي الليث أنه يصلي قال : والمستحب في كل دعاء أن يكون فيه الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اللهم صل على محمد وعلى آل محمد اهـ فهذا يفيد أنّ كيفية الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في القنوت بهذه الكيفية، ويشهد له ما أخرجه النسائي بسند صحيح عن زيد بن خارجة قال : سألت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كيف الصلاة عليك فقال: صلوا علي واجتهدوا في الدعاء وقولوا اللهم صل على محمد وعلى آل محمد وعنه : الدعاء موقوف بين السماء، والأرض لا يصعد حتى يصلى علي فلا تجعلوني كغمر الراكب صلوا علي في أوّل الدعاء وأوسطه وآخره ) اختار الفقيه أبو الليث رحمه الله تعالى أنه يصلي في القنوت على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والمؤتم يقرأ القنوت كالإمام على الأصح ويخفي الإمام والقوم هو الصحيح لكن استحب للإمام الجهر به في بلاد العجم ليتعلموه كما جهر عمر رضي الله عنه بالثناء حين قدم عليه وفد العراق ولذا فصل بعضهم إن لم يعلم القوم فالأفضل للإمام الجهر ليتعلموا وإلا فالإخفاء أفضل
The Book of Prayer: Being secure from Allah's scheme is disbelief, like despair of mercy, and combining hope and fear because the capable one is such that his bounty is hoped for and his punishment is feared. In the hadith: 'They do not come together in the heart of a believing servant except that Allah gives him what he hopes for and secures him from what he fears.' So [we say] 'We ask You to bestow favor upon us through faith and grant us success to act upon the pillars, obeying Your command, not confining ourselves to heart and tongue, for that is the hope of liars, people of falsehood.' We believe and say: 'Indeed this is the great truth' — meaning the truth, and it is with kasr of jīm by agreement meaning truth, and it is established in the mursal of Abu Dawood, so no attention is paid to those who say that one should not say 'al-jadd' with the disbelievers — it means attached, i.e., not attached to them, with kasr of ḥā being more eloquent, and it is said with fatḥa, meaning that Allah Almighty attaches him to them. And because al-Nasa'i narrated with a good chain that in the hadith of qunut: 'and may Allah bless the Prophet', we prayed upon him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and upon his family, as from its cause, meaning that it reaches him due to his persistence in sins. He said: 'Then do not feel secure from Allah's scheme except the losing people.' His saying: 'like despair of mercy' means hopelessness of it and certainty that one is among the people of punishment, for it leads to decreasing deeds and denying mercy, and in it is what preceded about security. Allah says: 'Indeed, no one despairs of relief from Allah except the disbelieving people.' His saying: 'that his bounty is hoped for and his punishment feared.' His saying: 'They do not come together etc.' You have known that hope is not realized except with righteous deeds, otherwise it is wishful thinking. His saying: 'with the pillars' means the limbs. His saying: 'obeying Your command' is a confirming circumstantial phrase. His saying: 'not confining ourselves to heart and tongue' means by hoping in his heart or speaking with his tongue without action of the limbs. His saying: 'people of falsehood' is lying, and al-Qamus explained it as saying about a person what he did not do. His saying: 'we believe and say' is an effect delayed, and it is his saying: 'So we ask You to bestow favor upon us through faith', and there is no doubt that this belief and saying is caused by the favor of faith. His saying: 'with kasr of ḥā' al-Nawawi said: this is the famous, and al-Jazari said: thus we narrated. His saying: 'and it is said with fatḥa' Ibn Qutaybah and others said it, and al-Jawhari stated it is correct. His saying: 'and may Allah bless the Prophet' this is what al-Nasa'i narrated only without 'and upon his family and grant them peace' as understood from the commentary. His saying: 'we prayed' is an effect of his saying: 'and because al-Nasa'i narrated'. His saying: 'and upon his family and grant them peace' in al-Waqi'at after mentioning the choice of al-Faqih Abu al-Layth that he prays, he said: 'and it is recommended in every supplication that it contain prayer upon the Prophet, O Allah send prayers upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad.' So this indicates that the manner of prayer upon the Prophet in qunut is in this manner, and it is supported by what al-Nasa'i narrated with a sound chain from Zayd ibn Kharijah who said: I asked the Messenger of Allah how to pray upon you? He said: 'Pray upon me and strive in supplication, and say: O Allah send prayers upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad.' And from him: 'Supplication is suspended between heaven and earth, it does not ascend until prayers are sent upon me, so do not make me like the small cup of the rider, pray upon me at the beginning, middle, and end of supplication.' Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth chose that one should pray upon the Prophet in qunut, and the follower recites qunut like the imam according to the most correct view, and both imam and congregation recite quietly—this is correct, but it is recommended for the imam to recite aloud in non-Arab lands so they learn it, just as 'Umar recited aloud when the delegation of Iraq came to him. Therefore some differentiate: if the people do not know, then it is better for the imam to recite aloud so they learn; otherwise, quiet recitation is better.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the qunut supplication recited in the witr prayer. The author begins by explaining the meaning of the supplication 'we ask You to bestow favor upon us through faith…' emphasizing that true faith balances fear of Allah's punishment and hope for His mercy. Both are necessary; security from Allah's plan and despair of His mercy are acts of disbelief, as supported by Quranic verses. The commentary then addresses the phrase 'this is the great truth,' affirming it means the truth and that the word 'al-jadd' is correctly pronounced with a kasra. It rejects the opinion that one should not say 'al-jadd' with the disbelievers. Next, the passage discusses sending salawat (prayers) upon the Prophet ﷺ during qunut. It cites the hadith of Zayd ibn Kharijah, teaching the specific wording and emphasizing that supplication is not accepted until salawat is sent. The commentator highlights that Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi chose this practice, and it is recommended in every dua. Regarding recitation, the follower recites qunut like the imam according to the most correct view. Both imam and congregation recite quietly, but if the congregation does not know the supplication, the imam may recite aloud for teaching purposes, following the practice of 'Umar. This passage combines rulings on belief, supplication etiquette, and prayer practice.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): A specific supplication recited in the witr prayer after ruku' or before it, asking for guidance, forgiveness, and other blessings.
الرجاء والخوف (al-raja' wa al-khawf): Hope for Allah's mercy and fear of His punishment, both required for proper faith and worship.
الجهر والإخفاء (al-jahr wa al-ikhfa'): Loud and quiet recitation in prayer; in qunut, quiet is norm, but loud is allowed for teaching.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for the imam's recitation of qunut in witr in a non-Arab land where the people are unfamiliar with it?
A) The imam must recite quietly at all times.
B) The imam may recite aloud so the people learn, following the practice of 'Umar.
C) The imam must recite aloud always.
D) The imam should recite in a tone that is neither loud nor quiet.

Key Takeaway
Sending salawat in qunut is recommended (sunnah muakkadah), and the imam recites quietly unless teaching requires loudness.

Ruling on Praying Sunnah Sitting and Virtues of Fajr Sunnah
Explains ruling on sitting in sunnah prayers and virtues of Fajr sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying the sunnah of Fajr while sitting without an excuse, and explain the intra-madhhab difference regarding its obligation.

Core Idea
The Fajr sunnah is emphasized sunnah, not wajib; praying it sitting is permissible but less virtuous.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi addresses a key point in Hanafi fiqh: the ruling on performing the sunnah of Fajr while sitting without a valid excuse. It also discusses the reported view of Abu Hanifa that the Fajr sunnah is wajib, contrasting it with the majority Hanafi position. By studying this passage, you will understand the distinction between the reported and mufta bihi views, and the evidence used to support each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage deals with praying the sunnah of Fajr (and by extension other sunnah prayers) while sitting without an excuse. The author first states that it is invalid (la yajuz), then clarifies that the relied-upon view is permissibility.
The initial statement reflects a minority view; the subsequent clarification is the mufta bihi.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence cited is the hadith: 'The two rak'ahs of Fajr are more beloved to me than the world and what is in it' (Muslim) and the hadith: 'Do not abandon them even if the horses chase you.'
These hadith emphasize the virtue and encouragement, not obligation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith use words like 'more beloved' and 'do not abandon' which indicate strong encouragement but not a command that imposes obligation. In Hanafi usul, such expressions are interpreted as sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib.
The imperative 'do not abandon' is read as a recommendation, not an obligation, due to other evidence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa is reported to have said the Fajr sunnah is wajib. However, the majority of Hanafi scholars (including Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it sunnah mu'akkadah. The text notes that the alleged consensus on invalidity when sitting is actually a consensus on emphasis.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is the majority view.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author (al-Tahtawi) states that the relied-upon view is permissibility of sitting, as will come in the commentary. The tarjih is based on the strength of the evidence for permissibility and the lack of clear evidence for obligation.
The mufta bihi ruling is that the prayer is valid if performed sitting, but standing is more virtuous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الله تعالى : لو صلاها قاعداً من غير عذر لا يجوز وروى المرغيناني عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنها واجبة، وقال : لا تدعوهما وإن طردتكم الخيل وقال : ركعتا الفجر أحب إلي من الدنيا وما فيها وفي لفظ : خير من الدنيا وما فيها. قوله : (أنها واجبة) أجمعوا على أنها لا تصح قاعداً من غير عذر كما في الخلاصة، ويخشى على جاحدها الكفر كما في المضمرات، وتقضى إذا مع الفرض دون غيرها، والأصح أنها تصاب بمطلق النية وفي مسلم عن أبي هريرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قرأ في ركعتي الفجر قل يا أيها الكافرون) وقل هو الله أحد) وفي مسند الإمام أحمد ابن عباس في الأولى بخاتمة البقرة، وفي الثانية قل يا أهل الكتاب تعالوا الآية فتستحب قراءة هاتين السورتين، وهذه الآيات على سبيل المناوبة أياماً، واستحسن الغزالي أن يقرأ في الأولى ألم نشرح وفي الثانية ألم تر كيف وقال: إنّ ذلك يردّ شر اليوم كذا في ابن أمير حاج لكنه لم يرد في السنة كما في مقاصد السخاوي، والأفضل في سنة الفجر أداؤها في أول الوقت مع التخفيف ، وقيل : يفضل الأسفار وفي البناية عن المبسوط : يكره الكلام بعد إنشقاق الفجر لأنها ساعة تشهدها ملائكة الليل وملائكة النهار كما في تأويل إن قرآن الفجر كان مشهوداً فلا ينبغي أن يشهدهم إلا على خير، وفي حكاية الإجماع على أنها لا تصلي من قعود نظر، بل المجمع عليه إنما هو تأكدها، والمعتمد جوازها من قعود كما يأتي في الشرح. قوله : (وإن طردتكم (الخيل المقصود الحث على الفعل، وإلا فترك الفرد عند طرد الخيل يباح لعدم التمكن قوله : ( أحب إلي من الدنيا وما فيها باعتبار ما يترتب على فعلها من الثواب .
Allah Almighty said: If he prays it sitting without an excuse, it is not permissible. Al-Marghinani related from Abu Hanifa that it is obligatory. He said: Do not abandon them even if the horses chase you. He said: The two rak'ahs of Fajr are more beloved to me than the world and what is in it. In another wording: Better than the world and what is in it. His statement: (that it is obligatory) they agreed that it is not valid sitting without an excuse as in al-Khulasa, and it is feared that the denier may fall into disbelief as in al-Mudmarat, and it is made up with the obligatory prayer but not others, and the correct view is that it is attained with absolute intention. Muslim reported from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet recited in the two rak'ahs of Fajr 'Say: O disbelievers' and 'Say: He is Allah, the One.' In the Musnad of Imam Ahmad, Ibn Abbas reported that in the first he recited the end of al-Baqara and in the second 'Say: O People of the Scripture, come to a common word.' So it is recommended to recite these two surahs and these verses alternately over days. Al-Ghazali recommended reciting 'Have We not opened' in the first and 'Have you not considered' in the second, saying that this repels the evil of the day. This is quoted in Ibn Amir Hajj, but it is not established in the Sunnah as in Maqasid al-Sakhawi. The best in the sunnah of Fajr is to perform it at the beginning of the time briefly. Some say: it is better to delay until the time is light. In al-Binaya from al-Mabsut: It is disliked to speak after the break of dawn because it is an hour witnessed by the angels of night and the angels of day, as in the interpretation of 'Indeed the recitation of the dawn is witnessed.' So one should not make them witness except good. Regarding the claim of consensus that it should not be prayed sitting, there is consideration; rather, what is agreed upon is its emphasis, and the relied-upon view is its permissibility sitting as will come in the commentary. His statement: (even if the horses chase you) the intention is encouragement to perform it. Otherwise, abandoning it when chased by horses is permissible due to lack of ability. His statement: (more beloved to me than the world and what is in it) considering the reward resulting from its performance.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the sunnah prayers, specifically the Fajr sunnah. The author first states the ruling: praying the sunnah sitting without an excuse is invalid. He then narrates from Abu Hanifa that the sunnah is wajib (obligatory). This is a minority view within the Hanafi school; the majority consider it sunnah mu'akkadah. The hadith 'Do not abandon them even if the horses chase you' emphasizes their importance. The hadith 'Two rak'ahs of Fajr are better than the world and what is in it' shows their great virtue. The commentary then confirms the consensus that the sunnah is invalid sitting without excuse, and that denying it could lead to disbelief. It must be made up if the obligatory prayer is made up. The correct view is that it is performed with absolute intention. The passage then discusses recommended recitations in the Fajr sunnah: Surah al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas, or other verses. Al-Ghazali's recommendation of Surah al-Sharh and al-Fil is noted but not authenticated. The best is to perform it early and lightly. The ruling on speaking after Fajr is disliked. Finally, the passage addresses the issue of sitting: the claim of consensus against sitting is rejected; the relied-upon view is that it is permissible to pray sunnah sitting, even without excuse, though standing is more virtuous. The final lines explain that the hadith about horses is an encouragement, and the love for the sunnah is due to its reward.

Key Terms
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of sunnah prayed before the obligatory Fajr prayer.
قاعداً (qa'idan): Performing the prayer in a sitting position without valid excuse (illness, etc.).
واجبة (wajibah): Obligatory; according to the narration from Abu Hanifa, the Fajr sunnah is wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is valid and makruh tanzihan
B) It is invalid and must be repeated
C) It is permissible and the prayer is valid
D) It is wajib to stand

Key Takeaway
The Fajr sunnah is an emphasized sunnah; praying it sitting is permissible, but standing is better.

Recommended Non-Emphasized Prayers (Mandub): Four Before Asr, Four Around Isha, Six After Maghrib
Lists recommended prayers with hadith proofs and commentary on performance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sets of mandub prayers mentioned, identify their hadith proofs, and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on their specifics.

Core Idea
Four before Asr, four around Isha, six after Maghrib: these mandub prayers carry immense reward, yet their performance is not obligatory.

In this lesson, we examine the second category of sunnah prayers: the mustahab or mandub acts. While the emphasized sunnahs (sunan muakkadah) are regularly performed by the Prophet, the non-emphasized recommended prayers (mandub) are encouraged through specific hadith promising great reward, but their omission does not incur sin. The passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi lists these prayers, discusses variant narrations, and clarifies the preference for praying them at home.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sets of mandub prayers
The passage explicitly mentions: four before Asr, four before Isha, four after Isha, and six after Maghrib. Note that these are in addition to the emphasized sunnahs.
The six after Maghrib are distinct from the two emphasized rak'ahs after Maghrib.
2
Examine the hadith proofs for each
For each prayer, the author quotes a hadith. For example, 'Whoever prays four rak'ahs before Asr, the Fire will not touch him.' Recognise that these proof texts are ahad and thus the ruling level is mandub, not wajib.
The hadith for six after Maghrib uses the term 'awwabin' (penitent).
3
Note the intra-Hanafi variant opinions
Al-Quduri gave a choice between two or four rak'ahs before Asr due to differing reports. Also, for the six after Maghrib, some say one taslim, others two or three. The mufta bihi is four before Asr and one taslim for the six.
This shows that within a single madhhab, there can be ikhtilaf on details.
4
Understand the reward and regular practice
The commentary explains that the promised reward is for those who regularly perform these prayers, not just once. Missing occasionally due to an excuse does not harm.
Consistency is key for attaining the full reward.
5
Apply the ruling on the best place to pray
The passage states that it is better to pray these sunnahs at home, unless one fears laziness. The wisdom is to keep homes illuminated with prayer.
The obligatory prayers are better in the mosque; these are better at home.

فلذا خيره القدوري بينهما (و) ندب أربع قبل (العشاء) لما روي عنها أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يصلي قبل العشاء أربعاً، ثم يصلي بعدها أربعاً ثم يضطجع (و) ندب أربع (بعده) أي بعد العشاء لما روينا ولقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من صلى قبل الظهر أربعاً كان كأنما تهجد من ليلته ومن صلاهن بعد العشاء كان كمثلهن من ليلة القدر» (و) ندب (ست) ركعات (بعد المغرب) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من صلى بعد المغرب ست ركعات كتب التكلم وفي التجنيس الست بثلاث تسليمات، وذكر القونوي أنها بتسليمتين وفي الدرر بتسليمة واحدة وقد عطفنا المندوبات على المؤكدات كما في الكنز ، وغيره من المعتبرات وظاهره المغايرة فتكون الست في المغرب غير الركعتين المؤكدتين، وكذا في الأربع بعد الظهر، وقيل بها لما في الدراية أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال من حافظ على أربع ركعات قبل الظهر وأربع بعدها حرمه الله على النار ومثله في الاختيار
And the second category is the recommended (mustahab) of the sunnahs. He began it with His statement: 'And it is recommended (mandub), i.e., mustahab, four rak'ahs before Asr prayer' because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever prays four rak'ahs before Asr, the Fire will not touch him.' And it is reported from Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, that he prayed two rak'ahs, and it is reported four, so al-Quduri gave him a choice between them. And it is recommended four before Isha, based on what is reported from her that the Prophet, peace be upon him, used to pray four before Isha, then four after it, then lie down. And it is recommended four after Isha, for what we narrated and for his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever prays four before Zuhr is like one who prayed during the night, and whoever prays them after Isha is like one who prayed them on Laylat al-Qadr.' And it is recommended six rak'ahs after Maghrib, for his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever prays six after Maghrib will be recorded among the penitent (awwabin),' and he recited His statement: 'Indeed, He is ever Forgiving to the penitent.' The penitent is one who, when he commits a sin, hastens to repentance. And from Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him, that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever prays twenty rak'ahs after Maghrib, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise.' And from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'Whoever prays six rak'ahs after Maghrib without speaking evil between them, they will be counted for him as worship of twelve years.' And from Aisha that he said: 'Whoever prays twenty rak'ahs after Maghrib, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise.' And from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'Whoever prays four rak'ahs after Maghrib before speaking to anyone, it will be raised for him in Illiyin, and he will be like one who... And the best regarding the before and after sunnahs is to perform them at home, as was his usual practice. Abu Dawud narrated: 'A person's prayer in his home is better than his prayer in this mosque of mine, except for the obligatory prayer.' And in al-Munya: 'Supererogatory prayer in the mosque is good, and in the home is better.' And this is the fatwa of al-Faqih Abu Ja'far. He said: 'Unless he fears that he will be distracted from it when he returns home. If he does not fear, then the home is better.' And the wisdom in it is that homes should not be devoid of prayer, as he alerted: 'Illuminate your homes with prayer and do not make them graves.' As in al-Halabi and others. His statement: 'Perhaps, etc.' This is something the author researched uniquely, and the words of the madhhab scholars are more worthy to follow. His statement: 'The recommended of the sunnahs: mustahab, mandub, encouraged, and good are synonymous terms meaning the same thing: an act whose performance is preferred by Shari'ah over its abandonment.' His statement: 'Thus al-Quduri gave him a choice' i.e., due to the difference in reports, al-Quduri gave him a choice. Likewise, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan gave a choice between praying two or four, as in al-Fath. His statement: 'Whoever prays before Zuhr, etc.' He said in Raf' al-Awa'iq 'an al-Fawa'id al-Qurashiyya: 'The meaning in such cases—i.e., like what was mentioned of the promise of reward in return for actions—is continuous performance, not doing it once. It appears that omission occasionally due to an excuse is not a hindrance.' His statement: 'It will be raised for him in Illiyin' is the highest place in Paradise, meaning immense reward is stored for him on account of it; otherwise, other deeds have their reward stored in... The Book of Prayer. Fifty. 391. He attained Laylat al-Qadr in al-Aqsa Mosque, and it is better for him than half a night of standing. And from Ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever prays six rak'ahs after Maghrib before speaking, Allah will forgive him a year's sins.' And from Ammar ibn Yasir, may Allah be pleased with him, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever prays six rak'ahs after Maghrib, his sins will be forgiven even if they are like the foam of the sea.' And it is not restricted to before speaking. And in al-Tajnis, the six are with three taslims. Al-Qunawi mentioned that they are with two taslims. In al-Durar, with one taslim. And we have appended the mandub acts to the mu'akkad acts, as in al-Kanz and other reliable works. And its apparent meaning is that they differ, so the six after Maghrib are other than the two emphatic rak'ahs, and likewise the four after Zuhr. And it is said because, as in al-Diraya, the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever preserves four rak'ahs before Zuhr and four after it, Allah will forbid him from the Fire.' And similar is in al-Ikhtiyar.

Commentary
This passage is from the hashish of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah, discussing the second category of sunnah prayers: the mustahab (recommended/desirable) non-emphasized prayers. The author lists several prayers with their proofs: four rak'ahs before Asr, four before and after Isha, and six after Maghrib. The hadith cited for each show the merits, though some reports vary (e.g., two vs. four before Asr). Al-Quduri gave a choice between two and four before Asr due to differing narrations. Following this, the passage discusses the preference for praying these sunnahs at home rather than the mosque, citing hadith and scholarly opinions. The hashish comments clarify definitions (mustahab=mandoob=muraggab fih=hasan), explain the reward promises as conditional on regular performance, and address the number of taslims for the six after Maghrib (one, two, or three). The passage also notes that these mandub acts are distinct from the emphasized (mu'akkadah) sunnahs.

Key Terms
مندوب (mandub): An act preferred by Shari'ah, synonymous with mustahab, murghab fih, and hasan; its performance is better than abandonment, but not sinful to leave.
أواب (awwab): One who repents immediately after sinning; a penitent person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab as presented in this passage, how many rak'ahs are recommended before Asr prayer?
A) Two only
B) Four only
C) Either two or four
D) None

Key Takeaway
The mandub prayers before Asr, before and after Isha, and after Maghrib are non-obligatory but highly rewarding, and their performance is best at home.

The Conditions for Leaving the Residence: Houses, Tents, Courtyard, and Suburb
Hanafi rulings on when a traveler is considered to have left his residence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four components of the residence a traveler must pass to qualify for qasr and explain why the courtyard is not annexed for shortening prayer.

Core Idea
Shortening prayer is a license for leaving the built-up area; passing houses alone is insufficient.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi conditions for becoming a traveler eligible for qasr. The source passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies what counts as leaving the place of residence: not just houses but also tents, courtyard, and suburb. We'll also see a key intra-Hanafi disagreement about whether the courtyard annexation affects qasr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is shortening prayer (qasr) while traveling. The ruling is that it is a concession (rukhsah) for the traveler, not an obligation.
The hukm level is mubah; it is not fard or wajib.
2
List the conditions for eligibility
The passage states that the traveler must pass (1) the houses of his residence, (2) tent houses, (3) the courtyard (fina'), and (4) the suburb (rabad).
Passing only houses is insufficient; all four must be left behind.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the general license in the Quran (2:184) and hadith for the traveler. The passage quotes the Quranic verse and the hadith about wiping for three days.
The dalil is zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on the courtyard
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Qadi Khan holds that passing the courtyard suffices, while al-Nihaya requires leaving the entire built-up area. The relied-upon view is the latter.
The courtyard is annexed for Jumu'ah but not for qasr.
5
Apply to a scenario
Try a scenario: a person leaves his house, crosses the courtyard, but is still in the suburb. He may not shorten until he passes the suburb as well.
The suburb is considered part of the town.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة
٤٢٣
وقاطع طريق لإطلاق نص الرخصة إذا جاوز بيوت مقامه ولو بيوت الأخبية من الجانب الذي خرج منه ولو حاذاه في أحد جانبيه فقط لا يضره (و) يشترط أن يكون قد جاوز أيضاً ما اتصل به أي بمقامه من فنائه كما يشترط مجاوزة ربضه وهو ما حول المدينة من بيوت ومساكن فإنه في حكم المصر، وكذا القرى المتصلة بربض المصر يشترط مجاوزتها في الصحيح (وإن انفصل الفناء بمزرعة أو ) فضاء (قدر غلوة وتقدم أنها . من ثلثمائة خطوة إلى أربعمائة (لا يشترط مجاوزته أي الفناء وكذا لو اتصلت القرية بالفناء لا بالربض لا يشترط مجاوزتها، بل مجاوزة الفناء كذا في قاضي خان، ويخالفه ما في النهاية، والفتاوي الولوالجية والتجنيس والمزيد ونصها يقصر بخروجه عن عمران المصر، ولا يلحق فناء المصر بالمصر في حق السفر، ويلحق الفناء بالمصر لصحة صلاة الجمعة، والفرق
مقامه) عبر
ذهب لطلب ابق أو غريم ولم يعلم أين يدركه أتم في الذهاب وفي موضع المكث، وإن طالت المدة أما في الرجوع، فإن كانت مدة سفر ،قصر، وإلا لا . قوله: (ولو كان عاصياً بسفره بأن سافر لطلب الزنا، أو قطع الطريق، ولو طرأ عليه قصد المعصية بعد إنشاء السفر فإنه يترخص بالاتفاق، واعلم أنه يكون عاصياً بقصد فعل المعصية سواء وجدت منه المعصية بالفعل، أم لا أفاده السيد قوله : لإطلاق) نص الرخصة قال تعالى : فمن كان منكم مريضاً، أو على سفر) [البقرة/ ٢] الآية وقال : يمسح المسافر ثلاثة أيام ولياليها والقبح المجاور لا ينفي الأحكام كالبيع وقت النداء، والصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة. قوله: (إذا جاوز بيوت بالجمع ليفيد اشتراط مجاورة الكل فيدخل فيه محلة منفصلة، وفي القديم كانت متصلة لأنها تعد من المصر كما في الخانية . قوله : ( ولو بيوت الأخبية) متصلة، أو متفرقة فإن نزلوا على ماء، أو محتطب يعتبر مفارقة الماء والمحتطب . قال في الشرح : ولعله ما لم يكن محتطباً واسعاً جداً اهـ ولا يشترط غيبوبة البيوت عن بصره لما روي عن علي بن ربيعة الأسدي : خرجنا مع علي ونحن ننظر إلى الكوفة فصلى ركعتين، ثم رجعنا فصلى ركعتين، وهو ينظر إلى القرية فقلنا ألا نصلي أربعاً فقال حتى ندخلها قوله (المتصلة بربض المصر) قيد بالربض احترازاً عن القرية المتصلة بالفناء فلا يشترط مجاوزتها على هذا الصحيح الذي الشرع تبعاً للنهاية معزياً للمحيط، وأفاد في النهر عن الولوالجية أن المختار عدم اشتراط مجاوزة القرية مطلقاً . قوله : (وتقدم أنها من ثلثمائة الخ) فإذا تحقق أقلها لا يشترط مجاوزته، وفي البحر الغلوة أربعمائة ذراع في الأصح ، ولعله بيان لنهايتها قال التمرتاشي : إنّ هذا التفصيل هو الأشبه. قوله: (ويخالفه الخ) يؤيده ما عنه أنه قصر العصر بذي الحليفة، وهو من فناء المدينة. قوله : ( ويلحق) الفناء بالمصر لصحة صلاة الجمعة) ومن المشايخ من منع الجمعة فيه إذا كان منقطعاً عن العمران وهو المعوّل عليه كما سيأتي في الجمعة إن شاء الله تعالى . صححه

كتاب الصلاة
الجمعة من مصالح المصر، وفناء المصر ملحق بالمصر فيما هو من حوائج المصر وآداء الجمعة منها وقصر الصلاة ليس من حوائج أهل المصر فلا يلحق فناء المصر بالمصر في حق هذا الحكم أي قصر الصلاة والفناء المكان المعد لمصالح البلد كركض الدواب ودفن الموتى وإلقاء التراب ولا تعتبر البساتين من عمران ،المدينة وإن كانت متصلة ببنائها، ولو سكنها أهل البلدة في جميع السنة أو بعضها، ولا يعتبر سكنى الحفظة، والاكرة اتفاقاً
Book of Prayer. And a road-cutter (brigand) due to the general application of the text of license if he has passed the houses of his place of residence, even the houses of tents, from the side from which he departed, and even if he is parallel to it on one side only, it does not harm him. (And) it is also required that he has passed what is attached to his place of residence from its courtyard, just as it is required to pass its suburb, which is the houses and dwellings around the city, for it is considered part of the town. Similarly, villages attached to the suburb of the town require passing them in the correct view. (And if the courtyard is separated by a field or an open space the distance of a bowshot, and it was previously mentioned that it is from three hundred steps to four hundred, then passing it is not required, meaning the courtyard. Similarly, if a village is attached to the courtyard but not to the suburb, passing it is not required; rather, passing the courtyard is sufficient, as in Qadi Khan. And what is in al-Nihaya, al-Fatawa al-Walwaljiyya, al-Tajnis, and al-Mazid contradicts it, and their text is: he shortens by leaving the built-up area of the town, and the courtyard of the town is not annexed to the town with regard to travel, but is annexed to the town for the validity of Friday prayer, and the difference is... (His saying: 'his place of residence') he went to seek a runaway slave or a creditor and did not know where he would find him, he completes (prayer) in going and in the place of staying, even if the period is long. As for returning, if the return journey is a travel period (three days), he shortens, otherwise not. His saying: ('Even if he is a sinner in his travel, such as traveling for adultery or highway robbery, and if the intention of sin arises after initiating travel, then he is entitled to concessions by consensus. And know that he becomes a sinner by intending the act of sin, whether the sin actually occurs or not, as stated by al-Sayyid.) His saying: 'for the general application of the text of license' – Allah said: 'So whoever among you is ill or on a journey...' (2:184) and He said: 'The traveler wipes for three days and their nights.' And the associated evil does not negate the rulings, like selling at the time of the call to prayer and prayer in usurped land. His saying: ('When he has passed the houses' – the plural indicates that passing all is required, so it includes a separate quarter, and in ancient times it was connected because it is considered part of the town as in al-Khaniyya.) His saying: ('Even the houses of tents' – connected or scattered; if they settle at water or firewood, the criterion is leaving the water and firewood. The commentator said: 'Perhaps as long as the firewood is not very extensive.' And the houses disappearing from sight is not required because of what was narrated from Ali ibn Rabi'a al-Asadi: 'We went out with Ali while we were looking at Kufa, and he prayed two rak'ahs, then we returned and he prayed two rak'ahs while looking at the village. We said: Should we not pray four? He said: Until we enter it.' His saying: ('attached to the suburb of the town' – he restricted with suburb to exclude the village attached to the courtyard, so passing it is not required according to this correct view which the author followed, citing al-Nihaya quoting al-Muhit. And al-Nahr reports from al-Walwaljiyya that the chosen view is not requiring passing the village absolutely.) His saying: ('And it was previously mentioned that it is from three hundred etc.') – so if the minimum is established, passing it is not required. And in al-Bahr, the bowshot is four hundred cubits in the most correct view, and perhaps it is an explanation of its maximum. Al-Timirtashi said: 'This detail is the more appropriate.' His saying: ('And it contradicts etc.') – it is supported by what he narrated that he shortened Asr at Dhu al-Hulayfa, which is from the courtyard of Madina.) His saying: ('And he annexes the courtyard to the town for the validity of Friday prayer.') – and some shuyukh prohibit Friday prayer in it if it is disconnected from the built-up area, and that is the relied-upon view, as will come in Friday prayer, Allah willing. Correct. Correct. BestUrduBooks.wordpress.com. Page 424. Book of Prayer. Friday prayer is from the interests of the town, and the courtyard of the town is annexed to the town in matters that are needs of the town and performing Friday prayer from it, but shortening prayer is not from the needs of the townspeople, so the courtyard of the town is not annexed to the town with regard to this ruling, that is, shortening prayer. And the courtyard is the place prepared for the interests of the town, like exercising horses, burying the dead, and dumping dirt. Orchards are not considered part of the built-up area of the city, even if they are attached to its buildings, even if the townspeople reside in them all year or part of it. And the residence of guards and farmers is not considered by consensus.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the conditions under which a traveler may shorten prayer (qasr). The ruling: a person is considered a traveler once he has passed the houses, tents, courtyard, and suburb of his residence. The proof is the general license in Quran and Hadith for the traveler. The passage details that passing houses includes even tent houses, and only one side being parallel does not harm. It also requires passing the courtyard (fina') and the suburb (rabad). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether villages attached to the courtyard but not the suburb require passing; the preferred view (from al-Nihaya) is that they do not. The courtyard is considered part of the town for Friday prayer but not for shortening prayer, due to the different purposes. The passage also clarifies that a sinner in his journey (e.g., a brigand) is entitled to concessions because the text is general, and evil does not negate rulings. Additionally, the traveler need not lose sight of his houses, as per the hadith of Ali. The distance of a bowshot is defined as 300-400 steps or 400 cubits. The overall lesson: becoming a traveler depends on physically leaving the built-up area including adjacent spaces, and the ruling differs for qasr versus Jumu'ah due to the nature of the benefit.

Key Terms
فناء (fina'): The courtyard or outer area attached to the town used for purposes like horse exercise, burial, and dumping dirt.
ربض (rabad): The suburb around the city consisting of houses and dwellings; considered part of the town.
غلوة (ghulwa): A bowshot, defined as 300-400 steps or 400 cubits, used to measure separation from the courtyard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on shortening prayer for a person who has passed the houses and the courtyard but is still within the suburb (rabad) of his town?
A) He may shorten because he has left the houses and courtyard.
B) He may not shorten because he must also pass the suburb.
C) He may shorten only if the suburb is less than a bowshot away.
D) He may not shorten because the courtyard is not annexed for qasr.

Key Takeaway
A traveler becomes eligible for qasr only after physically leaving the entire built-up area including houses, tents, courtyard, and suburb.

The Annexation of the Courtyard for Qasr vs. Jumu'ah: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Hanafi dispute on the annexation of the courtyard for qasr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the courtyard's annexation for qasr, evaluate the proofs for each view, and identify the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
The courtyard is annexed for Jumu'ah but not for qasr; the need determines the annexation.

While the general conditions for qasr seem clear, there is a significant difference of opinion within the Hanafi school on whether passing the courtyard (fina') is sufficient or whether one must leave the entire built-up area. This lesson explores the arguments of Qadi Khan versus al-Nihaya and clarifies the underlying principle: the courtyard is annexed only when there is a need (hajah) of the townspeople, which applies to Jumu'ah but not to qasr.

Guided Path
1
State the two opposing views within the Hanafi school
Qadi Khan holds that passing the courtyard suffices to start qasr. Al-Nihaya and others hold that the traveler must leave the entire built-up area.
Both views are within the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the evidence for each view
Qadi Khan analogizes to Jumu'ah where the courtyard is annexed. Al-Nihaya cites that qasr is not a need of the townspeople and that Ali shortened at Dhu al-Hulayfa, a place in the courtyard of Madina.
The hadith of Ali is used as a proof against annexation.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the analogy
The response is that the need (hajah) for Jumu'ah is greater; qasr is a personal concession, not a communal need. Therefore, the analogy is weak.
The principle of hajah differentiates the two cases.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a traveler stops in the courtyard, according to Qadi Khan he may shorten; according to al-Nihaya he may not.
This affects the validity of prayer.
5
Recognize the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is that of al-Nihaya: the courtyard is not annexed for qasr.
This is the position for fatwa.

Source Text
