His saying: ('Even if he is a sinner in his travel, such as traveling for adultery or highway robbery, and if the intention of sin arises after initiating travel, then he is entitled to concessions by consensus. And know that he becomes a sinner by intending the act of sin, whether the sin actually occurs or not, as stated by al-Sayyid.) His saying: 'for the general application of the text of license' – Allah said: 'So whoever among you is ill or on a journey...' (2:184) and He said: 'The traveler wipes for three days and their nights.' And the associated evil does not negate the rulings, like selling at the time of the call to prayer and prayer in usurped land. His saying: ('When he has passed the houses' – the plural indicates that passing all is required, so it includes a separate quarter, and in ancient times it was connected because it is considered part of the town as in al-Khaniyya.) His saying: ('Even the houses of tents' – connected or scattered; if they settle at water or firewood, the criterion is leaving the water and firewood. The commentator said: 'Perhaps as long as the firewood is not very extensive.' And the houses disappearing from sight is not required because of what was narrated from Ali ibn Rabi'a al-Asadi: 'We went out with Ali while we were looking at Kufa, and he prayed two rak'ahs, then we returned and he prayed two rak'ahs while looking at the village. We said: Should we not pray four? He said: Until we enter it.' His saying: ('attached to the suburb of the town' – he restricted with suburb to exclude the village attached to the courtyard, so passing it is not required according to this correct view which the author followed, citing al-Nihaya quoting al-Muhit. And al-Nahr reports from al-Walwaljiyya that the chosen view is not requiring passing the village absolutely.) His saying: ('And it was previously mentioned that it is from three hundred etc.') – so if the minimum is established, passing it is not required. And in al-Bahr, the bowshot is four hundred cubits in the most correct view, and perhaps it is an explanation of its maximum. Al-Timirtashi said: 'This detail is the more appropriate.' His saying: ('And it contradicts etc.') – it is supported by what he narrated that he shortened Asr at Dhu al-Hulayfa, which is from the courtyard of Madina.) His saying: ('And he annexes the courtyard to the town for the validity of Friday prayer.') – and some shuyukh prohibit Friday prayer in it if it is disconnected from the built-up area, and that is the relied-upon view, as will come in Friday prayer, Allah willing. Correct. Correct. BestUrduBooks.wordpress.com. Page 424. Book of Prayer. Friday prayer is from the interests of the town, and the courtyard of the town is annexed to the town in matters that are needs of the town and performing Friday prayer from it, but shortening prayer is not from the needs of the townspeople, so the courtyard of the town is not annexed to the town with regard to this ruling, that is, shortening prayer. And the courtyard is the place prepared for the interests of the town, like exercising horses, burying the dead, and dumping dirt. Orchards are not considered part of the built-up area of the city, even if they are attached to its buildings, even if the townspeople reside in them all year or part of it. And the residence of guards and farmers is not considered by consensus.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the conditions under which a traveler may shorten prayer (qasr). The ruling: a person is considered a traveler once he has passed the houses, tents, courtyard, and suburb of his residence. The proof is the general license in Quran and Hadith for the traveler. The passage details that passing houses includes even tent houses, and only one side being parallel does not harm. It also requires passing the courtyard (fina') and the suburb (rabad). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether villages attached to the courtyard but not the suburb require passing; the preferred view (from al-Nihaya) is that they do not. The courtyard is considered part of the town for Friday prayer but not for shortening prayer, due to the different purposes. The passage also clarifies that a sinner in his journey (e.g., a brigand) is entitled to concessions because the text is general, and evil does not negate rulings. Additionally, the traveler need not lose sight of his houses, as per the hadith of Ali. The distance of a bowshot is defined as 300-400 steps or 400 cubits. The overall lesson: becoming a traveler depends on physically leaving the built-up area including adjacent spaces, and the ruling differs for qasr versus Jumu'ah due to the nature of the benefit.

Key Terms
فناء (fina'): The courtyard or outer area attached to the town used for purposes like horse exercise, burial, and dumping dirt.
ربض (rabad): The suburb around the city consisting of houses and dwellings; considered part of the town.
غلوة (ghulwa): A bowshot, defined as 300-400 steps or 400 cubits, used to measure separation from the courtyard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi position regarding the courtyard's annexation for shortening prayer (qasr)?
A) The courtyard is annexed to the town for qasr, so passing it suffices.
B) The courtyard is not annexed; the traveler must leave the built-up area.
C) The courtyard is annexed only if it is less than a bowshot away.
D) The courtyard is annexed only for Jumu'ah, not for any other ruling.

Key Takeaway
The courtyard is annexed for Jumu'ah due to need, but not for qasr; the mufta bihi is that the traveler must leave the entire built-up area.

6 min
Doubt About Ritual Purity and the First Occurrence Rule
Ruling on doubt regarding hadath and its frequency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that frequent doubt (al-shakk al-kathir) is ignored and state when the first occurrence of doubt requires action.

Core Idea
Certainty is not removed by doubt; only the first occurrence of doubt triggers action.

This lesson explores a key application of the maxim 'al-yaqin la yuzalu bi al-shakk' (certainty is not removed by doubt). The text presents several scenarios: doubt about hadath while certain of purity, doubt about a part of wudu, doubt about the opening takbir during prayer, and doubt about impurities or wiping. The ruling distinguishes between the first time such doubt occurs, which requires corrective action, and frequent doubt, which is to be ignored to avoid hardship. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly maintaining purity and prayer in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the state of certainty
Start by determining what the person is certain of (e.g., purity or wudu). The person has yaqin (certainty) of being in a state of purity.
Certainty is the baseline.
2
Analyze the doubt and its frequency
Next, consider whether the doubt is about a specific action (like washing a part of wudu or saying the takbir) and whether it is the first time such doubt occurs or if the person frequently experiences such doubts.
Frequent doubt (al-shakk al-kathir) is defined as occurring often, e.g., three times in one prayer.
3
Apply the ruling based on frequency
If the doubt is the first occurrence, the person must act (e.g., wash the part or repeat the takbir). If the doubt is frequent, the person ignores it and continues.
The ruling for the opening takbir in the first rak'ah vs. later rak'ah is a specific application: if in the first rak'ah, repeat the takbir; if in the second, do not.
4
Confirm the outcome
Conclude that the person remains in the state of purity or prayer validity after applying the rule.
The principle prevents waswasa (whispers) and hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتمة: شك في الحدث، وتيقن الطهارة فهو متطهر وبالقلب، محدث، وشك في بعض وضوئه وهو أول ما عرض له غسل ذلك الموضع، وإن كثر شكه لا يلتفت إليه وكذا لو شك أنه كبر للإفتتاح وهو في الصلاة، أو أنه أصابته نجاسة، أو أحدث أو مسح رأسه أم لا فإن كان أول ما عرض استقبل، وإن كثر يمضي وفي العتابية لو شك هل كبر قيل : إن كان في الركعة الأولى يعيده وإن كان في الثانية لا .
Continuation: He doubts about the occurrence of hadath (ritual impurity) and is certain of purity, so he is pure, and in his heart he is impure. And if he doubts about some part of his wudu and it is the first time it occurs to him, he washes that part; but if his doubt becomes frequent, he does not pay attention to it. Similarly, if he doubts whether he said the opening takbir while he is in the prayer, or that impurity touched him, or that he had hadath, or that he wiped his head or not, if it is the first time it occurs, he starts again; if frequent, he continues. In al-Atabiyyah: if he doubts whether he said takbir, it was said: if he is in the first rak'ah he repeats it, if in the second he does not.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (hukm) that applies the established principle 'al-yaqin la yuzalu bi al-shakk' (certainty is not removed by doubt). The text presents several cases: a person who is certain of being in a state of purity but doubts whether hadath occurred remains considered pure (mutahhar), even if he inwardly feels impure. Similarly, if during wudu he doubts whether he washed a particular part, and it is the first time such doubt occurs, he must wash that part; but if he frequently experiences such doubt, he ignores it (the principle of 'la 'ibrah bi al-shakk al-kathir'). The same rule applies when in prayer: if he doubts whether he said the opening takbir, or if impurity touched his body, or if he had hadath, or if he wiped his head, the first time the doubt arises he must act upon it (e.g., repeat the takbir), but if such doubt is frequent, he continues without action. The text also cites a specific view from al-Atabiyyah that if he doubts the takbir in the first rak'ah, he repeats it; in the second, he does not. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi emphasis on disregarding frequent doubts to avoid hardship.

Key Terms
الشك الكثير (al-shakk al-kathir): Frequent doubt that persists and is considered pathological; such doubt is ignored in Hanafi fiqh.
اليقين (al-yaqin): Certainty, which is not overruled by doubt according to the legal maxim.
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity that nullifies wudu, such as passing wind, urination, etc.
أول ما عرض (awwal ma 'arada): The first time such a doubt occurs to the person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person is certain they have made wudu but doubts whether they passed wind (hadath) during the prayer, and such doubt occurs frequently. What should they do according to the Hanafi school?
A) Repeat wudu and the prayer because doubt invalidates certainty.
B) Continue the prayer and ignore the doubt.
C) Make sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) and continue.
D) Repeat only the wudu and then continue the prayer.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, certainty of purity is not invalidated by doubt; only the first occurrence of doubt about a specific action requires a corrective step, while frequent doubt is disregarded.

8 min
Rulings on Doubt in Wudu and Prayer: Certainty vs Frequency
Continuation: detailed rulings on doubt in wudu and prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and apply the Hanafi ruling for both first-time and frequent doubt in wudu and prayer, distinguishing when action is required and when doubt is to be ignored.

Core Idea
Certainty overrides doubt: first-time doubt demands action; habitual doubt is disregarded.

The Hanafi school emphasizes that certainty is not removed by doubt—a foundational principle across fiqh. However, when doubt arises for the first time without preponderance, action is required to resolve it. When doubt becomes frequent (waswasa), the Lawgiver has provided ease by commanding to ignore it. This lesson unpacks these rules as they apply to wudu, prayer, and related matters, drawing on the commentary of al-Tahtawi.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the Core Principle
Understand that the criterion is certainty (al-yaqīn). If you are certain of purity, doubt about an event does not break it. Similarly, if you are certain of both events but doubt the order, you remain in the state of purity because the later state (purity after wudu) is default.
This derives from the hadith: 'If one of you feels something in his belly and doubts whether something came out, let him not leave the mosque unless he hears a sound or smells an odor.' (Muslim)
2
Identify First-Time Doubt
A doubt that occurs for the first time during an act—without any preponderance—must be acted upon. For example, if during wudu you doubt whether you washed a certain limb, you must wash that limb. If in prayer you doubt whether you said the takbīr, you must repeat it (if you are still in the act).
This is only if the doubt has no indication (qarīna) tilting one way.
3
Distinguish Frequent Doubt
If the same doubt occurs often (such as in cases of waswasa), the ruling changes: you ignore it and proceed. The Lawgiver has facilitated this to prevent hardship. For instance, if you constantly doubt whether you passed wind, you do not repeat wudu.
The criterion for 'frequent' is that it happens three or more times in an act, or the person is known to have waswasa.
4
Apply to Specific Cases
Work through the scenarios in the passage: doubt about ḥadath after wudu (remain pure), doubt about part of wudu during wudu (wash that part), doubt about takbīr during prayer (repeat takbīr if first time), doubt about impurity on garment (ignore if frequent; wash if first time but note nuances).
The text specifies that doubt about takbīr in the first rak‘ah is acted upon; in the second rak‘ah, a weak view says no action is required, but the relied-upon view is to always act if it is the first occurrence.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
The commentator mentions a view from al-Atābiyya that if doubt about takbīr occurs in the second rak‘ah, one does not repeat it. However, al-Tahtawi notes this is weak (ḍa‘īf), and the muftā bihi is to act on first-time doubt regardless of the rak‘ah, unless it becomes frequent.
This illustrates how later Ḥanafī scholars evaluate and choose between transmitted views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتمة: شك في الحدث، وتيقن الطهارة فهو متطهر وبالقلب ،محدث، وشك في بعض وضوئه وهو أول ما عرض له غسل ذلك الموضع، وإن كثر شكه لا يلتفت إليه وكذا لو شك أنه كبر للإفتتاح وهو في الصلاة، أو أنه أصابته نجاسة، أو أحدث أو مسح رأسه أم لا فإن كان أول ما عرض استقبل، وإن كثر يمضي وفي العتابية لو شك هل كبر قيل : إن كان في الركعة الأولى يعيده وإن كان في الثانية لا . قوله : (مع تيسر طرق الخ) أي مع تيسير الشارع طريقاً الخ، والطريق هو الإتيان بالقعود قوله : (شك في الحدث الخ) حاصله أن العبرة بالمتيقن به ، ولو تيقنهما، وشك في السابق فهو متطهر كذا في الدر ومن نواقض الوضوء، قوله: (غسل ذلك الموضع) محله ما لو كان الشك في خلال الوضوء أما بعد تمامه فلا يعتبر أفاده صاحب الدر في المحل المذكور، وهو قياس ما تقدم في الصلاة، وفيه لو شك في نجاسة ما، أو ثوب، أو طلاق، أو عتق لم يعتبر اهـ. قوله : (وهو في الصلاة) التقييد به يفيد أنه إذا كان بعدها لا يعتبر . قوله : (أو أنه أصابته نجاسة هذا لا يقيد بحال الصلاة كما يتبادر من عبارة الشرح، فإنه قال : وإن كان يقع له كثيراً جاز له، ولا يلزمه الوضوء، ولا غسل الثوب، وقوله أو أنه أصابته نجاسة يحمل على ما إذا لم يكثر فلا ينافي ما في الدر. قوله : (أو أحدث فيه أنه تقدم أن العبرة باليقين إلا أن يحمل ما تقدم على ما إذا كثر، ويغني عنه قوله سابقاً شك في بعض وضوئه، وهو ظاهر، في أنه شك في عضو، أو شك في تعيينه غسل رجله اليسرى لأن آخر العمل، وانظر ما لو شك في ترك غير معين، وقياس ما تقدم فيمن شك أنه ترك صلاة من صلوات يوم وليلة أن يعيد كل ما شك في غسله كما يعيد صلاة اليوم والليلة أي إلا ما تيقن فعله منها قوله : (أو مسح رأسه) أي وكان في خلال الوضوء، أما لو صدر بعد، فلا يعتبر كما يؤخذ مما تقدم قريباً. قوله : (قيل الخ) أفاد بذكر قيل : ضعفه فالاعتماد على ما تقدم والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
Appendix: He doubts about an event (breaking wudu) and is certain of purity: he is in a state of purity. And if he is certain about both (purification and event) and doubts which came first: he is in a state of purity. And if he doubts about part of his wudu and it is the first occurrence, he washes that part. If his doubt becomes frequent, he pays no attention to it. Similarly, if he doubts whether he said the takbirat al-ihram while he is in prayer, or whether he was struck by impurity, or whether he committed an event, or whether he wiped his head or not—if it is the first occurrence, he repeats; if frequent, he proceeds. In al-Atabiyya: if he doubts whether he said takbir, it is said: if in the first rak'ah he repeats it, but if in the second, he does not. His saying: 'with ease of ways etc.' means with the Lawgiver's facilitation of a way, and the way is sitting. His saying: 'doubts about an event etc.' summary: the criterion is what is certain; if he is certain of both and doubts which came first, he is in a state of purity—thus in al-Durr from the nullifiers of wudu. His saying: 'washes that part' applies if doubt occurs during wudu; after its completion it is not considered—stated by the author of al-Durr in the mentioned place, and it is analogous to what preceded in prayer; and in it: if he doubts about impurity on something or a garment, or divorce, or emancipation, it is not considered. His saying: 'while he is in prayer' shows that if it is after it, it is not considered. His saying: 'or that he was struck by impurity' this is not restricted to the state of prayer as may appear from the commentator's expression, for he said: if it happens to him frequently, it is permissible for him, and he is not obligated to perform wudu or wash the garment; and his saying 'or that he was struck by impurity' is interpreted as when it is not frequent, so it does not contradict what is in al-Durr. His saying: 'or committed an event' wherein it was previously stated that the criterion is certainty, unless what was previously stated is interpreted as when it is frequent; and what he said earlier 'doubts about part of his wudu' suffices, and it is apparent that he doubts about a limb or about whether he washed his left foot because it is the end of the act. Consider: what if he doubts about leaving an unspecified part? And analogy to what preceded: if he doubts that he missed a prayer from the prayers of a day and night, he repeats everything he doubts about washing, just as he repeats the prayers of the day and night—i.e., except what he is certain of having performed. His saying: 'or wiped his head' means during wudu; if it occurs after, it is not considered as is taken from what preceded. His saying: 'it is said etc.' shows by mentioning 'it is said' its weakness, so reliance is on what preceded. And Allah, Exalted and Exalted, knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Great.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage is a continuation (tamāmah) from the chapter on doubt (shakk) in purification and prayer. It provides detailed rulings on how to deal with doubt when certainty exists about one state. The core principle is that certainty is not overridden by doubt. If a person is certain of having performed wudu but doubts whether an event occurred, he is considered pure. If he is certain of both but doubts the sequence, he is also pure because the later state (purity after wudu) is the default. Doubts that occur for the first time require action—such as washing the doubted limb during wudu or repeating the takbīr if it is the first time. However, frequent or persistent doubt (waswās) is ignored, and one proceeds. The text cites al-Atābiyya with a weaker view that if the doubt about takbīr occurs in the second rak'ah, it is not repeated. The commentary clarifies that the ruling for doubting impurity during prayer applies when it is not frequent; if it is frequent, it is excused. Similarly, doubting an event after completing wudu is not considered. The passage concludes with a note that the opinion 'qīla' (it is said) is weak, and the relied-upon view is what preceded.

Key Terms
الحدث (al-ḥadath): A state of ritual impurity that nullifies wudu, such as passing wind, urine, etc.
الاستقبال (al-istiqbāl): The act of repeating or starting anew when doubt occurs for the first time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is certain he performed wudu but doubts whether he passed wind after that, what is his status according to the Hanafi school?
A) He is impure and must repeat wudu.
B) He is pure because certainty overrides doubt.
C) He must wash the part he doubts.
D) He must perform tayammum.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on doubt: rely on certainty, act on first-time doubt, ignore frequent doubt.
